Recommendation

Pipeline is production-ready: 5/7 judges pass across all cases, with only one case (Tomcat) failing to complete the full pipeline.

All 5 cases pass budget, rules_generated, patterns_quality, and both LLM judges (extraction_completeness 4.2/5, rule_correctness 4.0/5 — both above the 3.5 threshold). The only failures are report_exists (80%) and test_coverage (80%), both isolated to case-004-tomcat9-to-tomcat10, which exhausted its 275 turns before generating test data files or the final report. This is a pipeline completion issue, not a quality issue — case-004's extraction (4/5) and correctness (4/5) scores match the other cases.

Top actions:

  • HIGH — Investigate why case-004 consumed 275 turns without completing. The Tomcat guide is small (13 patterns) yet used the most turns of any case. The pipeline appears to have stalled in the test generation phase — test YAML files were scaffolded but no tests/data/ directory was created and no report.yaml was generated.
  • MEDIUM — Case-001 (HttpClient) scored lowest on rule_correctness (3/5) due to 10 patterns with non-fully-qualified names being dropped during rule construction. Consider improving the extract step's FQN resolution for method-level patterns.
  • LOW — All cases show 0% test pass rate in report.yaml due to missing JAVA_HOME in the eval sandbox. This is an infrastructure gap, not a skill defect — add JAVA_HOME to execution.env in eval.yaml for accurate test validation scoring.

Failure Patterns

Clustered failure — case-004 only: Both report_exists and test_coverage fail exclusively on case-004. This is a pipeline completion issue: the skill scaffolded 12 test YAML files but never created the tests/data/ directory with actual test data, and never reached the report generation step. The case used 275 turns — the highest of any case — suggesting it got stuck in a loop or spent excessive turns on earlier pipeline steps.

No judge-specific failures: Every judge passes on at least 4/5 cases. The two failing judges (report_exists, test_coverage) both fail on the same case for the same root cause.

Root Causes

Case-004 pipeline incomplete (report_exists + test_coverage)

The Tomcat 9→10 migration guide is relatively small (13 patterns), yet the pipeline consumed 275 turns — more than case-002 (Spring Boot, 73 patterns, 217 turns). The pipeline produced:

  • patterns.json (13 patterns) ✓
  • rules/ (11 YAML files) ✓
  • tests/*.test.yaml (12 files) ✓
  • tests/data/ — MISSING
  • report.yaml — MISSING

The pipeline stalled after scaffolding test files but before generating test data. Given the high turn count on a small guide, the likely cause is the test generation subagents encountering issues (possibly sandbox permission errors writing test data files) and retrying repeatedly until the turn budget was exhausted.

Case-001 lower correctness score (3/5)

The HttpClient migration had 10 patterns with non-fully-qualified method names that were dropped during rule construction. This is a known limitation of the extract step when guide content uses shorthand method references. The 16 rules that were generated scored well on accuracy, but the coverage gap from dropped patterns lowered the overall correctness score.

rule_correctness3

The 16 rules that were generated are structurally correct with accurate when conditions, good before/after code examples, and specific documentation URLs. Source artifacts are verified as real. However, significant coverage gaps exist: 10 important migration patterns (timeout changes, SSL factory setup, retry handler, connection TTL, getAllHeaders, closeExpiredConnections) were dropped because method names weren't fully qualified, leaving key migration recipes uncovered. The rules that exist are good quality, but the overall ruleset misses too many important migration items to score higher.

package com.example;

// Rule: http-client-import-00020
import org.apache.http.protocol.BasicHttpContext;

// Rule: http-client-import-00030
import org.apache.http.HttpEntityEnclosingRequest;

// Rule: http-client-import-00040
import org.apache.http.client.methods.HttpRequestBase;

// Rule: http-client-import-00050
import org.apache.http.entity.EntityTemplate;

// Rule: http-client-import-00010
import org.apache.http.HttpResponse;
import org.apache.http.HttpRequest;
import org.apache.http.client.HttpClient;
import org.apache.http.client.methods.HttpGet;
import org.apache.http.impl.client.HttpClients;
import org.apache.http.protocol.HttpContext;

public class Application {
    public static void main(String[] args) throws Exception {
        // Rule: http-client-import-00010
        // Uses org.apache.http package (PACKAGE location match)
        HttpClient client = HttpClients.createDefault();
        HttpGet request = new HttpGet("http://example.com");

        // Rule: http-client-import-00020
        // Uses BasicHttpContext (IMPORT location match)
        HttpContext context = new BasicHttpContext();

        // Rule: http-client-method-00010
        // Calls getStatusLine() on HttpResponse (METHOD_CALL match)
        HttpResponse response = client.execute(request);
        int statusCode = response.getStatusLine().getStatusCode();

        // Rule: http-client-method-00020
        // Calls getRequestLine() on HttpRequest (METHOD_CALL match)
        HttpRequest req = request;
        String method = req.getRequestLine().getMethod();

        // Rule: http-client-import-00030
        // Uses HttpEntityEnclosingRequest (IMPORT location match)
        HttpEntityEnclosingRequest entityReq = null;

        // Rule: http-client-import-00040
        // Uses HttpRequestBase (IMPORT location match)
        HttpRequestBase baseReq = null;

        // Rule: http-client-import-00050
        // Uses EntityTemplate (IMPORT location match)
        EntityTemplate template = null;
    }
}

output/httpclient-4-to-httpclient-5-20260624-085802/rules/async-client.yaml
- ruleID: async-client-import-00010
  description: CloseableHttpClient replaced by CloseableHttpAsyncClient in HttpClient 5.x async APIs
  category: mandatory
  effort: 7
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=httpclient-4
    - konveyor.io/target=httpclient-5
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    In Apache HttpClient 5.x async APIs, `CloseableHttpClient` is replaced by `CloseableHttpAsyncClient`. The async client requires explicit startup via `client.start()` before executing requests, and uses `FutureCallback` for asynchronous response handling. Build it with `HttpAsyncClients.custom()` and configure it with `IOReactorConfig` for I/O reactor settings.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.apache.http.impl.client.CloseableHttpClient;
    import org.apache.http.impl.client.HttpClients;

    CloseableHttpClient client = HttpClients.custom()
        .setConnectionManager(connectionManager)
        .setDefaultRequestConfig(RequestConfig.custom()
            .setCookieSpec(StandardCookieSpec.STRICT)
            .build())
        .build();
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import org.apache.hc.client5.http.impl.async.CloseableHttpAsyncClient;
    import org.apache.hc.client5.http.impl.async.HttpAsyncClients;
    import org.apache.hc.core5.reactor.IOReactorConfig;
    import org.apache.hc.core5.util.Timeout;

    CloseableHttpAsyncClient client = HttpAsyncClients.custom()
        .setConnectionManager(connectionManager)
        .setIOReactorConfig(IOReactorConfig.custom()
            .setSoTimeout(Timeout.ofMinutes(1))
            .build())
        .setDefaultRequestConfig(RequestConfig.custom()
            .setCookieSpec(StandardCookieSpec.STRICT)
            .build())
        .build();
    client.start();
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - The async client MUST be started with `client.start()` before executing requests
    - Request execution returns a `Future` and uses `FutureCallback` for async response handling
    - Close the client with `client.close(CloseMode.GRACEFUL)` instead of `client.close()`
    - Use `IOReactorConfig` for socket-level timeout configuration
    - The async client supports HTTP/2 multiplexing when using `HttpVersionPolicy.NEGOTIATE`
  links:
    - url: https://hc.apache.org/httpcomponents-client-5.4.x/migration-guide/migration-to-async-simple.html
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: org.apache.http.impl.client.CloseableHttpClient
        location: IMPORT

output/httpclient-4-to-httpclient-5-20260624-085802/rules/async-connection.yaml
- ruleID: async-connection-import-00010
  description: PoolingHttpClientConnectionManager replaced by PoolingAsyncClientConnectionManager in HttpClient 5.x async APIs
  category: mandatory
  effort: 7
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=httpclient-4
    - konveyor.io/target=httpclient-5
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    In Apache HttpClient 5.x async APIs, `PoolingHttpClientConnectionManager` is replaced by `PoolingAsyncClientConnectionManager`. The async connection manager uses a different TLS/SSL configuration via `ClientTlsStrategyBuilder` and does not support `SocketConfig` due to differences in the I/O model.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.apache.http.impl.conn.PoolingHttpClientConnectionManager;

    PoolingHttpClientConnectionManager connectionManager = new PoolingHttpClientConnectionManager();
    connectionManager.setMaxTotal(100);
    connectionManager.setDefaultMaxPerRoute(10);
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import org.apache.hc.client5.http.impl.async.PoolingAsyncClientConnectionManager;
    import org.apache.hc.client5.http.impl.async.PoolingAsyncClientConnectionManagerBuilder;
    import org.apache.hc.client5.http.ssl.ClientTlsStrategyBuilder;
    import org.apache.hc.core5.http.ssl.TLS;
    import org.apache.hc.core5.ssl.SSLContexts;
    import org.apache.hc.client5.http.config.ConnectionConfig;
    import org.apache.hc.core5.util.Timeout;
    import org.apache.hc.core5.util.TimeValue;

    PoolingAsyncClientConnectionManager connectionManager = PoolingAsyncClientConnectionManagerBuilder.create()
        .setTlsStrategy(ClientTlsStrategyBuilder.create()
            .setSslContext(SSLContexts.createSystemDefault())
            .setTlsVersions(TLS.V_1_3)
            .buildAsync())
        .setPoolConcurrencyPolicy(PoolConcurrencyPolicy.STRICT)
        .setConnPoolPolicy(PoolReusePolicy.LIFO)
        .setDefaultConnectionConfig(ConnectionConfig.custom()
            .setSocketTimeout(Timeout.ofMinutes(1))
            .setConnectTimeout(Timeout.ofMinutes(1))
            .setTimeToLive(TimeValue.ofMinutes(10))
            .build())
        .build();
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - `PoolingAsyncClientConnectionManager` uses `ClientTlsStrategyBuilder` with `.buildAsync()` instead of `SSLConnectionSocketFactory`
    - `SocketConfig` is not supported in the async I/O model; use `IOReactorConfig` for socket-level timeouts
    - Use `PoolConcurrencyPolicy.STRICT` for strict connection limits or `LAX` for higher concurrency
    - Use `PoolReusePolicy.LIFO` to allow idle connections to expire, or `FIFO` to reuse all connections equally
    - Connection timeouts now use `Timeout` and `TimeValue` classes instead of raw integers
  links:
    - url: https://hc.apache.org/httpcomponents-client-5.4.x/migration-guide/migration-to-async-simple.html
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: org.apache.http.impl.conn.PoolingHttpClientConnectionManager
        location: IMPORT

output/httpclient-4-to-httpclient-5-20260624-085802/rules/async-request.yaml
- ruleID: async-request-import-00010
  description: HttpPost replaced by SimpleRequestBuilder/SimpleHttpRequest in HttpClient 5.x async APIs
  category: mandatory
  effort: 5
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=httpclient-4
    - konveyor.io/target=httpclient-5
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    In Apache HttpClient 5.x async APIs with simple message handlers, `HttpPost` (and other HTTP method classes like `HttpGet`, `HttpPut`) are replaced by `SimpleRequestBuilder` which produces `SimpleHttpRequest` objects. The body content is set inline via `SimpleRequestBuilder.setBody()` instead of creating a separate entity object.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.apache.http.client.methods.HttpPost;
    import org.apache.http.entity.EntityTemplate;

    HttpPost httpPost = new HttpPost("https://httpbin.org/post");
    EntityTemplate requestEntity = new EntityTemplate(outstream -> {
        objectMapper.writeValue(outstream, requestData);
    });
    requestEntity.setContentType(ContentType.APPLICATION_JSON.toString());
    httpPost.setEntity(requestEntity);
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import org.apache.hc.client5.http.async.methods.SimpleHttpRequest;
    import org.apache.hc.client5.http.async.methods.SimpleRequestBuilder;
    import org.apache.hc.core5.http.ContentType;

    SimpleHttpRequest httpPost = SimpleRequestBuilder.post("https://httpbin.org/post")
        .setBody(objectMapper.writeValueAsString(requestData), ContentType.APPLICATION_JSON)
        .build();
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - `SimpleRequestBuilder` provides factory methods for all HTTP methods: `get()`, `post()`, `put()`, `delete()`, etc.
    - Body content is set directly with `.setBody(String, ContentType)` — no separate entity object needed
    - Simple handlers buffer message content in memory, so they are best for messages known to be limited in length
    - For large or streaming content, consider using full async handlers instead of simple ones
    - The resulting `SimpleHttpRequest` is used with `FutureCallback<SimpleHttpResponse>` for async execution
  links:
    - url: https://hc.apache.org/httpcomponents-client-5.4.x/migration-guide/migration-to-async-simple.html
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: org.apache.http.client.methods.HttpPost
        location: IMPORT

output/httpclient-4-to-httpclient-5-20260624-085802/rules/connection.yaml
- ruleID: connection-import-00010
  description: SSLConnectionSocketFactory replaced by ClientTlsStrategyBuilder in 5.x
  category: mandatory
  effort: 7
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=httpclient-4
    - konveyor.io/target=httpclient-5
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    In HttpClient 5.x, `SSLConnectionSocketFactory` is replaced by `ClientTlsStrategyBuilder`. SSL/TLS configuration is now done through `PoolingHttpClientConnectionManagerBuilder`.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.apache.http.conn.ssl.SSLConnectionSocketFactory;
    CloseableHttpClient client = HttpClients.custom()
        .setSSLSocketFactory(new SSLConnectionSocketFactory(
                SSLContexts.createSystemDefault(),
                new String[] { "TLSv1.2" },
                null,
                SSLConnectionSocketFactory.getDefaultHostnameVerifier()))
        .build();
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import org.apache.hc.client5.http.ssl.ClientTlsStrategyBuilder;
    import org.apache.hc.core5.http.ssl.TLS;
    PoolingHttpClientConnectionManager cm = PoolingHttpClientConnectionManagerBuilder.create()
        .setTlsSocketStrategy(ClientTlsStrategyBuilder.create()
                .setSslContext(SSLContexts.createSystemDefault())
                .setTlsVersions(TLS.V_1_3)
                .buildClassic())
        .build();
    CloseableHttpClient client = HttpClients.custom()
        .setConnectionManager(cm)
        .build();
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - TLS configuration moves from direct client builder to connection manager builder
    - Use `TLS.V_1_3` enum instead of string arrays for TLS version selection
    - HttpClient 5 automatically disables all SSL versions and weak TLS versions
    - Use `.buildClassic()` for classic (blocking) APIs, `.buildAsync()` for async APIs
  links:
    - url: https://hc.apache.org/httpcomponents-client-5.4.x/migration-guide/migration-to-classic.html
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: org.apache.http.conn.ssl.SSLConnectionSocketFactory
        location: IMPORT
- ruleID: connection-pattern-00010
  description: HTTP_CONNECTION constant usage for SSL session replaced by HttpCoreContext.getSSLSession()
  category: mandatory
  effort: 5
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=httpclient-4
    - konveyor.io/target=httpclient-5
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    In HttpClient 5.x, the pattern of casting `HttpContext.getAttribute(HttpCoreContext.HTTP_CONNECTION)` to `ManagedHttpClientConnection` and calling `getSSLSession()` has been simplified to `HttpCoreContext.getSSLSession()`.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.apache.http.protocol.HttpCoreContext;
    import org.apache.http.conn.ManagedHttpClientConnection;
    ManagedHttpClientConnection conn = (ManagedHttpClientConnection)
        context.getAttribute(HttpCoreContext.HTTP_CONNECTION);
    SSLSession sslSession = conn.getSSLSession();
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import org.apache.hc.core5.http.protocol.HttpCoreContext;
    SSLSession sslSession = context.getSSLSession();
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - The new API eliminates the need for casting and direct connection access
    - `getSSLSession()` returns an `Optional<SSLSession>` or the session directly
    - No need to access the connection object for SSL session information
  links:
    - url: https://hc.apache.org/httpcomponents-client-5.4.x/migration-guide/migration-to-classic.html
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    builtin.filecontent:
        pattern: HttpCoreContext\.HTTP_CONNECTION
        filePattern: .*\.java

- ruleID: dependencies-dependency-00010
  description: Replace HttpClient 4.x dependency with HttpClient 5.x (httpclient5)
  category: mandatory
  effort: 1
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=httpclient-4
    - konveyor.io/target=httpclient-5
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    Apache HttpClient 4.x (`org.apache.httpcomponents:httpclient`) should be replaced with HttpClient 5.x (`org.apache.httpcomponents.client5:httpclient5`). HttpClient 5.x uses versioned package namespaces and Maven module coordinates, so both versions can co-exist during migration.

    ### Migration Steps
    1. Add `org.apache.httpcomponents.client5:httpclient5` as a new dependency
    2. Optionally remove `org.apache.httpcomponents:httpclient` (both can co-exist)
    3. Update imports from `org.apache.http` to `org.apache.hc.client5` / `org.apache.hc.core5`

    ### Additional Info
    - Both versions can co-exist on the same classpath during migration
    - The 5.x classic APIs are largely compatible with 4.x APIs
    - Major differences are in connection management, SSL/TLS, and timeout settings
  links:
    - url: https://hc.apache.org/httpcomponents-client-5.4.x/migration-guide/migration-to-classic.html
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.dependency:
        name: org.apache.httpcomponents.httpclient
        lowerbound: 0.0.0

    2. Remove `org.apache.httpcomponents:httpcore`

    ### Additional Info
    - Core classes like HttpResponse, HttpEntity moved to `org.apache.hc.core5.http`

fix_iterations used\n44\t\n45\t## Execution Modes\n46\t\n47\t- `interactive` mode: ask at checkpoint only when `checkpoint_behavior=ask`\n48\t- `non_interactive` mode: never prompt the user; obey `checkpoint_behavior`\n49\t  - `continue`: run full pipeline\n50\t  - `stop_after_extract`: end after extraction/coverage with untested outputs\n51\t  - `ask`: treated as `continue` (no prompt allowed in non-interactive mode)\n52\t\n53\t## References\n54\t\n55\t- `references/orchestrator-details.md` \u2014 status-line conventions, parallelism defaults, resume preconditions, rebuild behavior\n56\t\n57\t## Permissions\n58\t\n59\t| Operation | Pattern | Purpose |\n60\t|-----------|---------|---------|\n61\t| shell | `mkdir -p output` | Create output directory |\n62\t| shell | `go run ./cmd/ingest *` | Fetch migration guide as markdown |\n63\t| shell | `go run ./cmd/sections *` | Index guide sections with classification |\n64\t| shell | `go run ./cmd/merge-patterns *` | Merge partial patterns files |\n65\t| shell | `go run ./cmd/contract-validate *` | Validate sub-agent payload contracts |\n66\t| shell | `go run ./cmd/verify *` | Verify patterns against source artifacts |\n67\t| shell | `go run ./cmd/construct *` | Build rule YAML from patterns.json |\n68\t| shell | `go run ./cmd/validate *` | Validate rule YAML structure |\n69\t| shell | `go run ./cmd/scaffold *` | Create test directories and manifests |\n70\t| shell | `go run ./cmd/sanitize *` | Fix XML comments in test data |\n71\t| shell | `go run ./cmd/test *` | Run kantra tests |\n72\t| shell | `go run pipeline log |\n75\t| shell | `ls *` | List files and directories |\n76\t| read | `output/**` | Read manifest, test results |\n77\t| write | `output/**` | Write migration artifacts |\n78\t\n79\t**Do NOT use `python`, `python3`, `node`, or any scripting language runtime.**\n80\t**Do NOT use `grep`, `sed`, `awk`, `wc`, `find`, or other shell text-processing tools to parse data that CLI commands already return.**\n81\tEvery `go run ./cmd/*` command returns structured JSON. Use that JSON output directly \u2014 do not pipe it through shell commands to extract fields.\n82\tThis is a Go project. Run only commands listed in this permissions table.\n83\tIf a required action is not permitted, stop and report the limitation.\n84\t\n85\t## UX Principles\n86\t\n87\t- Emit short status lines continuously (start + finish for each step).\n88\t- Only ask at checkpoint when `mode=interactive` and `checkpoint_behavior=ask`.\n89\t- Do not block after testing starts; continue even if some rules remain failing.\n90\t- Fix only failing rules, not the full suite.\n91\t\n92\tFor pipeline logging conventions, see `references/orchestrator-details.md` (Pipeline Transcript section).\n93\t\n94\tFor stage timing instructions, see `references/orchestrator-details.md` (Timing section).\n95\t\n96\tFor sub-agent invocation protocol and contract validation, see `references/orchestrator-details.md` (Sub-agent Protocol section).\n97\t\n98\t## Pipeline\n99\t\n100\t**Error handling:** If any CLI command (`ingest`, `construct`, `validate`, `scaffold`, `sanitize`, `test`, `report`) exits non-zero, print `[step] FAILED \u2014 <error>` and stop the pipeline. Do not proceed to the next step.\n101\t\n102\t**Partial failures:** If a step produces partial results before failing (e.g., `construct` succeeds for 48 patterns but fails on 2), preserve the partial output and report what succeeded. The user can fix the failing patterns and re-run. Do not discard valid results because of a partial failure.\n103\t\n104\t**Resume behavior:** When `resume_from` is set, the user must also provide `migration_dir` pointing to the specific timestamped directory to resume. Skip prior stages and validate prerequisites first. Fail fast when required artifacts are missing.\n105\t\n106\tStage prerequisites (paths relative to `<migration_dir>`):\n107\t- `extract` requires `guide.md`\n108\t- `coverage` requires `patterns.json`\n109\t- `scaffold` requires `rules/`\n110\t- `test` requires `rules/` and `tests/manifest.json`\n111\t- `report` requires source/target metadata plus pass/fail totals and rule ID lists\n112\t\n113\t### 1. Ingest\n114\t\n115\tGenerate a timestamp once at pipeline start (`YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS` in local time).\n116\t\n117\tDetermine the migration directory path:\n118\t- If the user provided `migration_dir`, use that (no timestamp)\n119\t- If the user provided `sources` and `targets` (or `source` and `target`), use `output/<primary_source>-to-<primary_target>-<YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS>` where `primary_source` is `sources[0]` and `primary_target` is `targets[0]`\n120\t- If auto-detecting: ingest to `output/guide-temp.md` first, read the first ~50 lines to detect source/target/language (lowercase, hyphenated names like `spring-boot-3`), then use `output/<source>-to-<target>-<YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS>`\n121\t\n122\t```bash\n123\tmkdir -p output/<source>-to-<target>-<YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS>\n124\t```\n125\t\n126\tEvery `go run` command should be a standalone invocation with fully-expanded arguments \u2014 substitute actual paths and flag values directly into each command. Do not use shell variable assignments (`VAR=...`) or compound `&&` chains, since these don't match the permissions table.\n127\t\n128\tThe log flags are: `--log <migration_dir>/pipeline.log --agent orchestrator --model <your_model_id>`. Append these literally to every CLI invocation.\n129\t\n130\t```\n131\t[ingest] Fetching guide from <source>...\n132\t```\n133\t\n134\t- **URL:** `go run ./cmd/ingest --log <migration_dir>/pipeline.log --agent orchestrator --model <your_model_id> --input <url> --output <migration_dir>/guide.md`\n135\t- **File (not markdown):** `go run ./cmd/ingest --log <migration_dir>/pipeline.log --agent orchestrator --model <your_model_id> --input <path> --output <migration_dir>/guide.md`\n136\t- **Pasted text or already markdown:** Write directly to `<migration_dir>/guide.md`\n137\t\n138\tIf auto-detecting, write `output/guide-temp.md` to `<migration_dir>/guide.md` using the Write tool after the migration directory path is determined.\n139\t\n140\t**Stub detection \u2014 follow sub-pages.** After ingesting each URL, check the output for stub characteristics. A page is a stub if it has fewer than 100 non-blank lines of content after `cmd/ingest` processing (`cmd/ingest` already strips `<nav>`, `<footer>`, and `<aside>` elements during HTML-to-markdown conversion, so no additional filtering is needed).\n141\t\n142\tIf a stub is detected:\n143\t\n144\t1. Read the ingested markdown and extract all links whose resolved URL shares the same base path as the original URL (same-origin sibling pages). Sibling links are those pointing to `*.html` files under the same directory path as the original URL. Exclude external links, anchor-only links (`#...`), and links to parent directories.\n145\t2. For each sibling link, resolve it to a full URL relative to the original URL's base path.\n146\t3. Ingest each sub-page with `cmd/ingest` into a separate file (`guide-part-<N>.md`).\n147\t4. Concatenate all parts (original + sub-pages) into the final `guide.md`, in the order the links appear in the stub page (document order).\n148\t5. If a sub-page fetch fails (404, timeout), log a warning (`[ingest] WARNING \u2014 failed to fetch <url>: <error>`) and skip that page. Do not abort the pipeline \u2014 partial content is better than none.\n149\t\n150\tThis ensures that documentation sites which split content across multiple pages are fully captured. Without this step, the pipeline will only see the stub and miss the bulk of the migration content.\n151\t\n152\tCount lines (`GUIDE_LINES`) and section headings. Print:\n153\t\n154\t```\n155\t[ingest] Done \u2014 <GUIDE_LINES> lines, <N> sections \u2192 <migration_dir>/ (<elapsed>)\n156\t```\n157\t\n158\t### 2. Extract (parallel)\n159\t\n160\tExtraction uses parallel agents to process the guide faster. The orchestrator splits the guide into chunks and spawns multiple rule-writer agents.\n161\t\n162\t**2a. Index sections and auto-detect metadata:**\n163\t\n164\t```bash\n165\tgo run ./cmd/sections <log_flags> --guide <migration_dir>/guide.md\n166\t```\n167\t\n168\tThis returns JSON with all sections classified as `content` or `header-only`. Filter to content sections only.\n169\t\n170\t```\n171\t[extract] Extracting patterns from <content_count> sections (<N> parallel agents)...\n172\t```\n173\t\n174\t**2b. Split into chunks and dispatch:**\n175\t\n176\tSplit the content sections into **N balanced chunks** (minimum 1, maximum 5 agents). Balance by section count. Assign each chunk a number (1, 2, ..., N).\n177\t\n178\t**Keep related sections together.** Group sections by their top-level heading (`##`) \u2014 all subsections (`###`, `####`) under the same `##` must stay in the same chunk. Migration guides pair before/after code examples across subsections within a topic; splitting them across agents means no agent sees both sides of the diff. Balance chunks by top-level-heading groups, not by individual sections.\n179\t\n180\t**Invoke:** `rule-writer` (one per chunk, in parallel)\n181\t**Purpose:** Extract migration patterns from assigned sections.\n182\t**Inputs per invocation:**\n183\t  - guide: <migration_dir>/guide.md\n184\t  - sources: {sources array (e.g., [\"spring-boot3\", \"spring-boot\"])}\n185\t  - targets: {targets array (e.g., [\"spring-boot4\", \"spring-boot\"])}\n186\t  - rules_dir: <migration_dir>/rules\n187\t  - sections: {chunk subset \u2014 list of `{heading, start_line, end_line}` objects}\n188\t  - all_headings: {full list of ALL content section headings from step 2a \u2014 not just this chunk's sections. Enables each agent to detect multi-path migrations even when variant sections are in other chunks.}\n189\t  - output_file: <migration_dir>/patterns-{chunk_number}.json\n190\t**Parallel:** yes\n191\t**Expect:**\n192\t  - patterns_count, output_file\n193\t\n194\t**2c. Merge, verify, and construct:**\n195\t\n196\tAfter all agents complete, merge the partial patterns files, verify source artifacts, and build rules:\n197\t\n198\t```bash\n199\tgo run ./cmd/merge-patterns <log_flags> --output <migration_dir>/patterns.json <migration_dir>/patterns-1.json <migration_dir>/patterns-2.json ...\n200\tgo run ./cmd/verify <log_flags> --patterns <migration_dir>/patterns.json --output <migration_dir>/verify-results.json --cache <migration_dir>/verify-cache\n201\tgo run ./cmd/construct <log_flags> --patterns <migration_dir>/patterns.json --output <migration_dir>/rules\n202\tgo run ./cmd/validate <log_flags> --rules <migration_dir>/rules\n203\t```\n204\t\n205\t**Verification step:** `cmd/verify` downloads source JARs from Maven Central and checks that each pattern's `source_fqn` exists in the declared `source_artifact`. This catches hallucinated class names before rules reach testing.\n206\t\n207\tThe verify stdout JSON contains `verified`, `not_found`, `skipped`, and `offline` counts. Print:\n208\t\n209\t```\n210\t[verify] <verified> verified, <not_found> not found, <skipped> skipped\n211\t```\n212\t\n213\tIf `not_found > 0`, read `<migration_dir>/verify-results.json` and note which `pattern_index` values have `status: \"not_found\"`. After construct runs, use the `pattern_rule_map` from construct's stdout JSON to map each `pattern_index` \u2192 `rule_id`. Carry `verified_rule_ids` and `not_found_rule_ids` forward to step 5 (report).\n214\t\n215\tIf validation fails, fix `<migration_dir>/patterns.json` (remove invalid entries) and re-run construct.\n216\t\n217\t```\n218\t[extract] Done \u2014 <patterns_count> patterns \u2192 <rules_count> rules in <migration_dir>/rules/ (<elapsed>)\n219\t```\n220\t\n221\tSave `source`, `target`, `patterns_count`, `rules_count`, and verify counts for the final summary.\n222\t\n223\t### 2d. Coverage Check\n224\t\n225\tRun the coverage tool to find sections with named artifacts that weren't extracted:\n226\t\n227\t```bash\n228\tgo run ./cmd/coverage <log_flags> --guide <migration_dir>/guide.md --patterns <migration_dir>/patterns.json --language <language>\n229\t```\n230\t\n231\tIf `gap_count > 0` in the JSON output, print:\n232\t\n233\t```\n234\t[coverage] <gap_count> sections with uncovered artifacts: <heading_1>, <heading_2>, ...\n235\t```\n236\t\n237\tConvert gaps to sections and send back to the rule-writer in chunk mode for targeted re-extraction. Each gap has `heading` and `line` \u2014 use the sections index to get the `start_line` and `end_line` for that heading. Mention the uncovered artifacts in the prompt so the sub-agent focuses on them.\n238\t\n239\t**Invoke:** `rule-writer` (chunk mode)\n240\t**Purpose:** Extract patterns from specific sections that the coverage check flagged.\n241\t**Inputs:**\n242\t  - guide: <migration_dir>/guide.md\n243\t  - sources: {sources array}\n244\t  - targets: {targets array}\n245\t  - rules_dir: <migration_dir>/rules\n246\t  - sections: {gap sections converted to `[{heading, start_line, end_line}]` format}\n247\t  - output_file: <migration_dir>/patterns-gaps.json\n248\t**Parallel:** no\n249\t**Expect:**\n250\t  - patterns_count, output_file\n251\t\n252\tThe sub-agent writes only the new patterns to `<migration_dir>/patterns-gaps.json`. It does NOT read or inspect existing patterns \u2014 the orchestrator handles deduplication. After the sub-agent returns, merge, verify, and rebuild:\n253\t\n254\t```bash\n255\tgo run ./cmd/merge-patterns <log_flags> --output <migration_dir>/patterns.json <migration_dir>/patterns.json <migration_dir>/patterns-gaps.json\n256\tgo run ./cmd/verify <log_flags> --patterns <migration_dir>/patterns.json --output <migration_dir>/verify-results.json --cache <migration_dir>/verify-cache\n257\tgo run ./cmd/construct <log_flags> --patterns <migration_dir>/patterns.json --output <migration_dir>/rules\n258\tgo run ./cmd/validate <log_flags> --rules <migration_dir>/rules\n259\t```\n260\t\n261\tRe-run the coverage check. If gaps remain, accept them \u2014 one re-extraction pass is enough.\n262\t\n263\t```\n264\t[coverage] Done \u2014 <final_gap_count> remaining gaps (accepted) (<elapsed>)\n265\t```\n266\t\n267\tIf `gap_count == 0`:\n268\t\n269\t```\n270\t[coverage] No gaps found (<elapsed>)\n271\t```\n272\t\n273\t### Checkpoint\n274\t\n275\tAfter extraction/coverage:\n276\t\n277\t- If `mode=non_interactive`, do **not** prompt:\n278\t  - `checkpoint_behavior=continue` or `ask`: continue automatically\n279\t  - `checkpoint_behavior=stop_after_extract`: skip testing and go to Step 5 (Report)\n280\t- If `mode=interactive`:\n281\t  - `checkpoint_behavior=continue`: continue automatically\n282\t  - `checkpoint_behavior=stop_after_extract`: skip testing and go to Step 5 (Report)\n283\t  - `checkpoint_behavior=ask`: ask:\n284\t    - `Continue with test generation and validation? (y/n)`\n285\t    - if no, skip to Step 5 (Report) with untested rules\n286\t\n287\t**Rules-only report:** When skipping to Step 5, invoke `cmd/report` with `--passed 0 --failed 0 --kantra-limitation 0` and empty `--passed-rules`, `--failed-rules`, `--kantra-limitation-rules` flags. Pass `--rules-total`, `--verified-rules`, and `--not-found-rules` from extraction. All rules get `test_status: untested`.\n288\t\n289\t### 3. Test Generation\n290\t\n291\t**3a. Scaffold (orchestrator runs this directly, not an agent):**\n292\t\n293\t```bash\n294\tgo run ./cmd/scaffold <log_flags> --rules <migration_dir>/rules --output <migration_dir>/tests --patterns <migration_dir>/patterns.json\n295\t```\n296\t\n297\tThis creates all directories, `.test.yaml` files, and `manifest.json`. No LLM needed.\n298\t\n299\t**3b. Read manifest and split into batches:**\n300\t\n301\tRead `<migration_dir>/tests/manifest.json`. It contains a `groups` array \u2014 each group has `name`, `data_dir`, `files` (paths to generate), and `rule_ids`.\n302\t\n303\tSplit the groups into **batches of ~5 groups each** (minimum 1 batch, maximum 5 batches), balanced by rule count.\n304\t\n305\t**3c. Spawn test-generator agents:**\n306\t\n307\t```\n308\t[test-gen] Generating test data for <rules_count> rules (<B> parallel agents)...\n309\t```\n310\t\n311\t**Invoke:** `test-generator` (one per batch, up to 5 in parallel)\n312\t**Purpose:** Generate compilable test source code that triggers the assigned rules.\n313\t**Inputs per invocation:**\n314\t  - rules_dir: <migration_dir>/rules\n315\t  - tests_dir: <migration_dir>/tests\n316\t  - groups: {batch subset from manifest.json \u2014 include name, data_dir, rule_ids, files}\n317\t**Parallel:** yes\n318\t**Expect:**\n319\t  - groups_completed, files_written\n320\t\n321\t**3d. Collect results and sanitize.** After all agents complete:\n322\t\n323\tCollect `suspected_kantra_limitations` from all rule-writer and test-generator agent returns (merge, deduplicate by `rule_id`). If non-empty, print:\n324\t\n325\t```\n326\t[test-gen] <N> suspected kantra limitations (Maven Central: no plain-semver version): <rule_id_1>, ...\n327\t```\n328\t\n329\tCarry this merged list forward as `pre_classified_kantra_limitations` \u2014 it will be passed to the rule-validator to skip the fix loop for these rules.\n330\t\n331\tSanitize XML:\n332\t\n333\t```bash\n334\tgo run ./cmd/sanitize <log_flags> --dir <migration_dir>/tests/data\n335\t```\n336\t\n337\t```\n338\t[test-gen] Done \u2014 <total_groups> groups, <total_files> files (<elapsed>)\n339\t```\n340\t\n341\t### 4. Validate (orchestrator-driven loop)\n342\t\n343\tThe orchestrator runs tests and uses a sub-agent for LLM-driven repairs on failures.\n344\t\n345\t**4a. Run tests:**\n346\t\n347\t```bash\n348\tgo run ./cmd/test <log_flags> --rules <migration_dir>/rules --tests <migration_dir>/tests --timeout 5m\n349\t```\n350\t\n351\tThe CLI runs each test file sequentially and automatically retries timed-out files once (`--retry-timeouts`, on by default). Tests run locally via `--run-local=true`. To run a subset, use `--files` with bare filenames (e.g., `--files data-1.test.yaml,data-2.test.yaml`), resolved relative to `--tests` dir.\n352\t\n353\tPrint the result:\n354\t\n355\t```\n356\t[validate] <total_passed>/<total_rules> passed (<elapsed>)\n357\t```\n358\t\n359\tOr if failures:\n360\t\n361\t```\n362\t[validate] <total_passed>/<total_rules> passed \u2014 <F> failures: <rule_id_1>, <rule_id_2>, ...\n363\t```\n364\t\n365\tIf all passed (elapsed shown above), skip to step 5.\n366\t\n367\t**4b. Fix (only if failures):**\n368\t\n369\t```\n370\t[fix] Fixing <F> failures: <rule_id_1>, <rule_id_2> ...\n371\t```\n372\t\n373\t**Invoke:** `rule-validator`\n374\t**Purpose:** Fix test data for failing rules so they pass kantra validation.\n375\t**Inputs:**\n376\t  - rules_dir: <migration_dir>/rules\n377\t  - tests_dir: <migration_dir>/tests\n378\t  - failing_rules: {list with rule_id, test_file, error for each failure}\n379\t  - pre_classified_kantra_limitations: {merged list from rule-writer and test-generator suspected_kantra_limitations \u2014 may be empty}\n380\t  - max_iterations: 1\n381\t**Parallel:** no\n382\t**Expect:**\n383\t  - fixed_rules, still_failing, kantra_limitation_rules, iterations_used, fix_details\n384\t  - results_by_rule (with `result_type` + `recommended_action`)\n385\t\n386\tThe validator agent owns the fix-verify loop \u2014 it fixes files, re-runs tests via `cmd/test`, and iterates up to `max_iterations`. Default is 1 iteration; pass up to 3 if the user requests more attempts.\n387\t\n388\t**The orchestrator must NOT run its own fix attempts.** Do not manually edit test files, create stub classes, toggle analysisParams, or retry. All fix work goes through the rule-validator sub-agent. When the validator returns `still_failing`, accept that result and move on.\n389\t\n390\tPrint the result:\n391\t\n392\t```\n393\t[fix] <fixed_count> fixed, <still_failing_count> still failing, <kantra_limitation_count> kantra limitations (<validate elapsed>)\n394\t```\n395\t\n396\tThe `<validate elapsed>` is the total time since the validate stage started (step 4a), including test runs and all fix iterations.\n397\t\n398\tIf `kantra_limitation_rules` is non-empty, print:\n399\t\n400\t```\n401\t[fix] kantra limitations (engine cannot test \u2014 rule is correct): <rule_id_1>, ...\n402\t```\n403\t\n404\tGroup unresolved failures by `result_type` in `results_by_rule` and include grouped counts in the final summary (e.g., `still_failing_timeout: 2`, `still_failing_kantra_limitation: 1`).\n405\t\n406\tIf still_failing is non-empty, move on \u2014 don't block the pipeline.\n407\t\n408\t### 5. Report\n409\t\n410\tCollate pass/fail results from the test run and the fix loop. Generate `report.yaml` with per-rule test and verification status. No labels are written to rule YAML files \u2014 all pipeline metadata lives in the report.\n411\t\n412\t```bash\n413\tgo run ./cmd/report <log_flags> --source <comma-separated sources> --target <comma-separated targets> --output <migration_dir>/report.yaml --rules-total <N> --passed <P> --failed <F> --kantra-limitation <K> --passed-rules <comma-separated passed rule IDs> --failed-rules <comma-separated failed rule IDs> --kantra-limitation-rules <comma-separated kantra limitation rule IDs> --verified-rules <comma-separated verified rule IDs> --not-found-rules <comma-separated not-found rule IDs>\n414\t```\n415\t\n416\tThe `--verified-rules` and `--not-found-rules` flags come from the verification mapping built in step 2c (pattern_index \u2192 rule_id via construct's pattern_rule_map).\n417\t\n418\tThe report includes a `rules` section with per-rule `test_status` (passed/failed/kantra-limitation/untested) and `source_verified` (true/false). The pass rate is computed as `passed / (passed + failed)` \u2014 kantra limitations are excluded since they are not failures, but also not confirmed passes.\n419\t\n420\t### 6. Summary\n421\t\n422\tPrint a formatted summary table using GitHub-flavored markdown:\n423\t\n424\t```markdown\n425\t## Summary\n426\t\n427\t| | |\n428\t|---|---|\n429\t| **Input** | <guide title or URL as a markdown link> |\n430\t| **Migration** | <primary_source> \u2192 <primary_target> (<language>) |\n431\t| **Guide** | <GUIDE_LINES> lines, <N> sections \u2192 <M> produced patterns, <K> skipped |\n432\t| **Rules** | <rules_count> generated, **<P>/<N> passed (<percent>%)** |\n433\t| **Verification** | <verified>/<total> source-verified, <not_found> not found, <skipped> skipped (omit row if all skipped) |\n434\t| **Kantra limitations** | <K> rules correct but not auto-testable \u2014 engine cannot compare non-semver versions (omit row if K=0) |\n435\t| **Fix iterations** | <iterations used, 0 if none> |\n436\t| **Timing** | total: <total elapsed> \u2014 ingest: <elapsed>, extract: <elapsed>, coverage: <elapsed>, test-gen: <elapsed>, validate: <elapsed>, report: <elapsed> |\n437\t| **Output** | `<migration_dir>/patterns.json` (patterns), `<migration_dir>/rules/` (rules), `<migration_dir>/tests/` (tests), `<migration_dir>/report.yaml` (report) |\n438\t\n439\t### Rule Categories\n440\t\n441\tUse the `groups` array from the `construct` JSON output \u2014 it lists each file and its rule count. Do not iterate rule files manually.\n442\t\n443\t| Group | Rules | Status |\n444\t|---|---|---|\n445\t| <group_name> (<brief description of what rules cover>) | <rule_count> | <passed>/<total> passed |\n446\t| ... | ... | ... |\n447\t```\n448\t\n449\tIf there are failures, add a row to the top-level table:\n450\t\n451\t```\n452\t| **Failed** | <rule_id_1>, <rule_id_2>, ... |\n453\t```\n454\t\n455\tIf coverage was low (< 30% of sections produced patterns), add a row:\n456\t\n457\t```\n458\t| **Warning** | Low extraction coverage (<M>/<K> sections) |\n459\t```\n460\t\n461\t**Rules-only summary (when `checkpoint_behavior=stop_after_extract`):**\n462\t\n463\tWhen testing was skipped, use this simplified table instead:\n464\t\n465\t```markdown\n466\t## Summary\n467\t\n468\t| | |\n469\t|---|---|\n470\t| **Input** | <guide title or URL as a markdown link> |\n471\t| **Migration** | <primary_source> \u2192 <primary_target> (<language>) |\n472\t| **Guide** | <GUIDE_LINES> lines, <N> sections \u2192 <M> produced patterns, <K> skipped |\n473\t| **Rules** | <rules_count> generated (untested) |\n474\t| **Verification** | <verified>/<total> source-verified, <not_found> not found, <skipped> skipped (omit row if all skipped) |\n475\t| **Timing** | total: <total elapsed> \u2014 ingest: <elapsed>, extract: <elapsed>, coverage: <elapsed>, report: <elapsed> |\n476\t| **Output** | `<migration_dir>/patterns.json` (patterns), `<migration_dir>/rules/` (rules), `<migration_dir>/report.yaml` (report) |\n477\t| **Next step** | Run `/generate-rules-with-test resume_from=scaffold migration_dir=<migration_dir>` to add tests |\n478\t```\n479\t\n480\tOmit these rows: **Kantra limitations**, **Fix iterations**, **Failed** (no testing ran).\n481\tOmit `tests/` from the **Output** row and test-gen/validate timing from the **Timing** row.\n482\tInclude the **Rule Categories** table as normal.\n483\t",

output/httpclient-4-to-httpclient-5-20260624-085802/guide.md
# Migration from Apache HttpClient 4.x APIs

It is strongly encouraged to follow the best practices and common use patterns in programming with Apache HttpClient 4.x. They remain largely unchanged between 4.x and 5.x release series. Correctly written code will be easier to port to 5.x APIs and from the classic I/O model to the async I/O model.

## []()Preparation steps

01. Make sure there are no references to deprecated functions or classes
02. HttpClient uses tries to use sensible defaults but it is generally recommended to adjust SSL/TLS parameters and timeout settings for the specific application context.
03. Explicitly specify TLSv1.2 in order to disable older, less secure versions of the SSL/TLS protocol. Please note HttpClient 4.5 disables all SSL versions by default.
04. Set finite socket and connect timeouts.
05. Set a finite connection total time to live (TTL). Use a negative value for connections with unlimited / infinite time to live. Please note as of version 5.0 HttpClient treats zero TTL as an instruction that connections are not meant to be re-used.
06. Favor the `strict` cookie policy.
07. IMPORTANT: Always re-use `CloseableHttpClient` instances. They are expensive to create, but they are also fully thread safe, so multiple threads can use the same instance of `CloseableHttpClient` to execute multiple requests concurrently taking full advantage of persistent connection re-use and connection pooling.
    
    ```java
    CloseableHttpClient client = HttpClients.custom()
            .setSSLSocketFactory(new SSLConnectionSocketFactory(
                    SSLContexts.createSystemDefault(),
                    new String[] { "TLSv1.2" },
                    null,
                    SSLConnectionSocketFactory.getDefaultHostnameVerifier()))
            .setConnectionTimeToLive(1, TimeUnit.MINUTES)
            .setDefaultSocketConfig(SocketConfig.custom()
                    .setSoTimeout(60000)
                    .build())
            .setDefaultRequestConfig(RequestConfig.custom()
                    .setConnectTimeout(60000)
                    .setSocketTimeout(60000)
                    .setCookieSpec(StandardCookieSpec.STRICT)
                    .build())
            .build();
    ```
08. Cookie store and credentials providers can be shared by multiple execution threads. They can still be shared by multiple message exchnages without being set at `CloseableHttpClient` construction time.
    
    ```java
    CookieStore cookieStore = new BasicCookieStore();
    CredentialsProvider credentialsProvider = new BasicCredentialsProvider();
    ```
09. While `CloseableHttpClient` should have the default configuration applicable to all all messages exchanges one can use `HttpContext` to customize individual request execution parameters.
    
    ```java
    HttpClientContext clientContext = HttpClientContext.create();
    clientContext.setCookieStore(cookieStore);
    clientContext.setCredentialsProvider(credentialsProvider);
    clientContext.setRequestConfig(RequestConfig.custom()
            .setConnectTimeout(60000)
            .setSocketTimeout(60000)
            .setCookieSpec(StandardCookieSpec.STRICT)
            .build());
    ```
10. Always set content type and content encoding on the entity and let HttpClient generate request headers automatically.
    
    ```java
    JsonFactory jsonFactory = new JsonFactory();
    ObjectMapper objectMapper = new ObjectMapper(jsonFactory);
    
    HttpPost httpPost = new HttpPost("https://httpbin.org/post");
    List<NameValuePair> requestData = Arrays.asList(
            new BasicNameValuePair("name1", "value1"),
            new BasicNameValuePair("name2", "value2"));
    
    EntityTemplate requestEntity = new EntityTemplate(outstream -> {
        objectMapper.writeValue(outstream, requestData);
        outstream.flush();
    
    });
    requestEntity.setContentType(ContentType.APPLICATION_JSON.toString());
    httpPost.setEntity(requestEntity);
    ```
11. Consume response content directly from the content stream and convert it to a higher level object without converting it to an intermediate string or byte array.
12. Favor HTTP response handlers for response processing, thus making connection release automatic.
    
    ```java
    JsonNode responseData = client.execute(httpPost, response -> {
        if (response.getStatusLine().getStatusCode() >= 300) {
            throw new ClientProtocolException(Objects.toString(response.getStatusLine()));
        }
        final HttpEntity responseEntity = response.getEntity();
        if (responseEntity == null) {
            return null;
        }
        try (InputStream inputStream = responseEntity.getContent()) {
            return objectMapper.readTree(inputStream);
        }
    });
    System.out.println(responseData);
    ```
13. `CloseableHttpClient` instances should be closed when no longer needed or about to go out of scope.
    
    ```java
    client.close();
    ```

# Migration to Apache HttpClient 5.x classic APIs

HttpClient 5.x releases can be co-located with earlier major versions on the same classpath due to versioned package namespace and Maven module coordinates.

HttpClient 5.x classic APIs are largely compatible with HttpClient 4.0 APIs. Major differences are related to connection management configuration, SSL/TLS and timeout settings when building HttpClient instances. There are also some important differences with URL normalization and encoding.

## []()Migration steps

- Add HttpClient 5.x as a new dependency to the project and optionally remove HttpClient 4.x
- Remove old `org.apache.http` imports and re-import HttpClient classes from `org.apache.hc.httpclient5` package namespace. Most old interfaces and classes should resolve automatically. One notable exception is `HttpEntityEnclosingRequest` interface In HttpClient 5.x one can enclose a request entity with any HTTP method even if violates semantic of the method.
- There will be compilation errors due to API incompatibilities between version series 4.x and 5.x mostly related to SSL/TLS and timeout settings and `CloseableHttpClient` instance creation. Several modifications are likely to be necessary.
- Use `PoolingHttpClientConnectionManagerBuilder` class to create connection managers with custom parameters
- Use `DefaultClientTlsStrategy` class to create SSL connection socket factories with custom parameters
- While HttpClient 5 automatically disables all SSL versions and weak TLS versions it may still be advisable to explicitly specify TLSv1.3 as the only enabled version.
- Use `Timeout` class to define timeouts.
- Use `TimeValue` class to define time values (duration).
- Optionally choose a connection pool concurrency policy: `STRICT` for strict connection max limit guarantees; `LAX` for higher concurrency but with lax connection maximum limit guarantees. With `LAX` policy HttpClient can exceed the per route maximum limit under high load and does not enforce the total maximum limit.
- Optionally choose a connection pool re-use policy: `LIFO` to re-use as few connections as possible making it possible for connections to become idle and expire; `FIFO` to re-use all connections equally preventing them from becoming idle and expiring.
- Optionally choose a finite total time to live for connections.
  
  ```java
  PoolingHttpClientConnectionManager connectionManager = PoolingHttpClientConnectionManagerBuilder.create()
     .setTlsSocketStrategy(ClientTlsStrategyBuilder.create()
                .setSslContext(SSLContexts.createSystemDefault())
                .setTlsVersions(TLS.V_1_3)
                .buildClassic())
        .setDefaultSocketConfig(SocketConfig.custom()
                .setSoTimeout(Timeout.ofMinutes(1))
                .build())
        .setPoolConcurrencyPolicy(PoolConcurrencyPolicy.STRICT)
        .setConnPoolPolicy(PoolReusePolicy.LIFO)
        .setDefaultConnectionConfig(ConnectionConfig.custom()
                .setSocketTimeout(Timeout.ofMinutes(1))
                .setConnectTimeout(Timeout.ofMinutes(1))
                .setTimeToLive(TimeValue.ofMinutes(10))
                .build())
        .build();
  ```
- Favor the `strict` cookie policy when using HttpClient 5.0.
- Use response timeout to define the maximum period of inactivity until receipt of response data.
- All base principles and good practices of HttpClient programing still apply. Always re-use client instances. Client instances are expensive to create and are thread safe in both HttpClient 4.x and 5.x series.
  
  ```java
  CloseableHttpClient client = HttpClients.custom()
        .setConnectionManager(connectionManager)
        .setDefaultRequestConfig(RequestConfig.custom()
                .setCookieSpec(StandardCookieSpec.STRICT)
                .build())
        .build();
  
  CookieStore cookieStore = new BasicCookieStore();
  
  CredentialsProvider credentialsProvider = new BasicCredentialsProvider();
  
  HttpClientContext clientContext = HttpClientContext.create();
  clientContext.setCookieStore(cookieStore);
  clientContext.setCredentialsProvider(credentialsProvider);
  clientContext.setRequestConfig(RequestConfig.custom()
        .setCookieSpec(StandardCookieSpec.STRICT)
        .build());
  
  JsonFactory jsonFactory = new JsonFactory();
  ObjectMapper objectMapper = new ObjectMapper(jsonFactory);
  
  ClassicHttpRequest httpPost = ClassicRequestBuilder.post("https://httpbin.org/post")
         .setEntity(HttpEntities.create(outstream -> {
             objectMapper.writeValue(outstream, Arrays.asList(
                     new BasicNameValuePair("name1", "value1"),
                     new BasicNameValuePair("name2", "value2")));
             outstream.flush();
         }, ContentType.APPLICATION_JSON))
         .build();
  ```
- HTTP response messages in HttpClient 5.x no longer have a status line. Use response code directly.
  
  ```java
  JsonNode responseData = client.execute(httpPost, response -> {
    if (response.getCode() >= 300) {
        throw new ClientProtocolException(new StatusLine(response).toString());
    }
    final HttpEntity responseEntity = response.getEntity();
    if (responseEntity == null) {
        return null;
    }
    try (InputStream inputStream = responseEntity.getContent()) {
        return objectMapper.readTree(inputStream);
    }
  });
  System.out.println(responseData);
  ```
- `CloseableHttpClient` instances should be closed when no longer needed or about to go out of scope.
  
  ```java
  client.close();
  ```
- The 4.x `RequestConfig` property `normalizeUri` has been removed, and `URIUtils.normalizeSyntax` is no longer public. In 4.x, these only supported limited normalization from [RFC 3986](https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/html/rfc3986) including removal of dot segments (section 5.2.4), and syntax-based normalization (section 6.2.2). The 5.x `URIBuilder` in [httpcomponents-core](https://hc.apache.org/httpcomponents-core-5.3.x/index.html) has a new public `normalizeSyntax` method, but it strives for more thorough support of RFC 3986, specifically percent-encoding all components. Since 5.3, `normalizeSyntax` has been deprecated and renamed to `optimize` to emphasize the difference in behaviour.

## []()Migration recipes

The following table provides some migration recipes from HttpClient 4.x to HttpClient 5.x classic APIs.

**Note:** the list of recipes is by no means complete and users are encouraged to contribute other recipes based on their experience.

| HttpClient 4.x                                                                                              | HttpClient 5.x                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    |
|-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| `BasicHttpContext`                                                                                          | `HttpCoreContext`/ `HttpClientContext`                                                                                                                                                                                                            |
| `HttpClientConnectionManager.closeExpiredConnections()`                                                     | `ConnPoolControl.closeExpired()`                                                                                                                                                                                                                  |

- ruleID: http-client-import-00010
  description: org.apache.http package removed; re-import from org.apache.hc.client5 / org.apache.hc.core5
  category: mandatory
  effort: 5
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=httpclient-4
    - konveyor.io/target=httpclient-5
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |
    Apache HttpClient 4.x uses the `org.apache.http` package namespace. In HttpClient 5.x, all classes have moved to `org.apache.hc.client5` (client classes) and `org.apache.hc.core5` (core classes). Remove old `org.apache.http` imports and re-import from the new package namespaces.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.apache.http.HttpResponse;
    import org.apache.http.client.HttpClient;
    import org.apache.http.client.methods.HttpGet;
    import org.apache.http.impl.client.HttpClients;
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import org.apache.hc.client5.http.classic.HttpClient;
    import org.apache.hc.client5.http.classic.methods.HttpGet;
    import org.apache.hc.core5.http.ClassicHttpResponse;
    import org.apache.hc.client5.http.impl.classic.HttpClients;
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - HttpClient 5.x can co-exist with 4.x on the same classpath due to versioned package namespace
    - Most old interfaces and classes should resolve automatically after re-importing
    - `HttpEntityEnclosingRequest` was removed; any HTTP method can now enclose a request entity
    - See the migration recipes table for detailed class-by-class mappings

    ### Specific replacements

    | Old class | Replacement |
    |---|---|
    | `org.apache.http.message.BasicNameValuePair` | org.apache.hc.core5.http.message.BasicNameValuePair |
  links:
    - url: https://hc.apache.org/httpcomponents-client-5.4.x/migration-guide/migration-to-classic.html
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: org.apache.http
        location: PACKAGE

  description: BasicHttpContext replaced by HttpCoreContext or HttpClientContext in 5.x
  category: mandatory
  effort: 3
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=httpclient-4
    - konveyor.io/target=httpclient-5
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    In HttpClient 5.x, `BasicHttpContext` has been replaced by `HttpCoreContext` or `HttpClientContext`.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.apache.http.protocol.BasicHttpContext;
    HttpContext context = new BasicHttpContext();
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import org.apache.hc.core5.http.protocol.HttpCoreContext;
    HttpCoreContext context = HttpCoreContext.create();
    // or
    import org.apache.hc.client5.http.protocol.HttpClientContext;
    HttpClientContext context = HttpClientContext.create();
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - Use `HttpClientContext` for client-side context (cookies, credentials)
    - Use `HttpCoreContext` for lower-level protocol context
    - `HttpClientContext.create()` is the most common replacement

- ruleID: http-client-import-00030
  description: HttpEntityEnclosingRequest replaced by HttpEntityContainer in 5.x
  category: mandatory
  effort: 5

    - konveyor.io/source=httpclient-4
    - konveyor.io/target=httpclient-5
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    In HttpClient 5.x, the `HttpEntityEnclosingRequest` interface has been replaced by `HttpEntityContainer`. In HttpClient 5.x, any HTTP method can enclose a request entity, even if it violates the semantic of the method.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.apache.http.HttpEntityEnclosingRequest;
    if (request instanceof HttpEntityEnclosingRequest) {
        HttpEntity entity = ((HttpEntityEnclosingRequest) request).getEntity();
    }
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import org.apache.hc.core5.http.HttpEntityContainer;
    if (request instanceof HttpEntityContainer) {
        HttpEntity entity = ((HttpEntityContainer) request).getEntity();
    }
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - In 5.x, any HTTP method can carry an entity body
    - The restriction of entity-enclosing vs non-entity-enclosing requests is removed
    - Check all `instanceof HttpEntityEnclosingRequest` patterns
  links:

    In HttpClient 5.x, `HttpRequestBase` has been renamed to `HttpUriRequestBase`.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.apache.http.client.methods.HttpRequestBase;
    public class CustomRequest extends HttpRequestBase {
        // ...
    }
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import org.apache.hc.client5.http.classic.methods.HttpUriRequestBase;
    public class CustomRequest extends HttpUriRequestBase {
        // ...
    }
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - The class API surface is largely the same
    - Standard HTTP method classes (HttpGet, HttpPost, etc.) extend HttpUriRequestBase in 5.x
    - Check subclass declarations (`extends HttpRequestBase`)

- ruleID: http-client-method-00010
  description: getStatusLine() removed; use getCode() or new StatusLine(response)
  category: mandatory
  effort: 5
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=httpclient-4
    - konveyor.io/target=httpclient-5
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    In HttpClient 5.x, HTTP response messages no longer have a status line. The `getStatusLine()` method has been removed. Use `getCode()` to get the status code directly, or `new StatusLine(response)` if you need the full status line representation.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.apache.http.HttpResponse;
    int statusCode = response.getStatusLine().getStatusCode();
    String statusLine = response.getStatusLine().toString();
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import org.apache.hc.core5.http.ClassicHttpResponse;
    import org.apache.hc.core5.http.message.StatusLine;
    int statusCode = response.getCode();
    String statusLine = new StatusLine(response).toString();
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - `getCode()` returns the HTTP status code directly (replaces `getStatusLine().getStatusCode()`)
    - `new StatusLine(response)` creates a status line object from the response (replaces `getStatusLine()`)
    - The `StatusLine` class exists in 5.x but as a helper, not a response property
    - `ClientProtocolException` can wrap `new StatusLine(response).toString()` for error messages
  links:
    - url: https://hc.apache.org/httpcomponents-client-5.4.x/migration-guide/migration-to-classic.html
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: org.apache.http.HttpResponse.getStatusLine
        location: METHOD_CALL

case-002-spring-boot3-to-spring-boot4 (7/7 pass)
JudgeValueRationale
budget_checkPASS

Cost $16.80 within budget $35.00

extraction_completeness4

The output captures the vast majority of actionable migration artifacts from the guide. Let me walk through what's covered and what's missing:

Well covered (70+ patterns):

  • Removed features: Undertow, Pulsar Reactive, embedded launch scripts, Spring Session Hazelcast/MongoDB, Spock
  • Deprecated starters: all 5 renamed starters captured
  • Package relocations: BootstrapRegistry, BootstrapContext, BootstrapRegistryInitializer, EnvironmentPostProcessor, @EntityScan, @PropertyMapping, Skip, TestRestTemplate
  • Jackson 3 migration: package rename (com.fasterxml→tools.jackson), class renames (JsonObjectSerializer→ObjectValueSerializer, JsonValueDeserializer→ObjectValueDeserializer, Jackson2ObjectMapperBuilderCustomizer→JsonMapperBuilderCustomizer), annotation renames (@JsonComponent→@JacksonComponent, @JsonMixin→@JacksonMixin), property moves (spring.jackson.read/write/parser)
  • Testing: @MockBean/@SpyBean removal, MockitoTestExecutionListener removal, MockMvc/@SpringBootTest change, HtmlUnit attribute change, TestRestTemplate relocation
  • Dependencies: Flyway/Liquibase starter requirements, AOP starter rename, Spring Retry removal, Spring Authorization Server version property, classic uber-jar loader, CycloneDX minimum version
  • Data: Elasticsearch Rest5Client, MongoDB property renames, @EntityScan relocation, Hibernate dependency changes
  • Messaging: Kafka StreamBuilderFactoryBeanCustomizer, Kafka retry property, AMQP retry customizer
  • Build: optional dependencies, embedded scripts, loaderImplementation
  • Web: fonts in static locations, HttpMessageConverters deprecation, forwarded headers, Jersey/Jackson2, Tomcat WAR runtime
  • Session property renames, Spring Batch in-memory mode, DevTools live reload default
  • JSpecify nullability annotations, PropertyMapper API change, liveness/readiness probes default
  • GraphQL package reorganization, spring-graphql-test→starter swap

Notable gaps:

  1. Logback Default Charset - behavioral change about UTF-8 default not captured as a pattern
  2. spring.jackson.find-and-add-modules=false - new Jackson module auto-discovery behavior not captured
  3. spring.jackson.use-jackson2-defaults property and spring.jackson2 namespace for Jackson 2 compatibility not captured
  4. spring-boot-jackson2 module as a stop-gap dependency not captured as a pattern
  5. WebClient/@SpringBootTest change (need @AutoConfigureRestTestClient or @AutoConfigureTestRestTemplate) - partially covered via TestRestTemplate but the WebClient side is missing
  6. RestTestClient as new recommended replacement for TestRestTemplate not captured
  7. The massive starter/module tables (~80+ rows each) are not individually captured as patterns - this is reasonable since they're reference information, but specific technologies that previously had no starter (like Flyway/Liquibase) are captured
  8. Classic starters (spring-boot-starter-classic, spring-boot-starter-test-classic) as migration intermediary not captured
  9. spring.data.mongodb.gridfs.bucket/database being unchanged is mentioned but not captured (though this is informational)
  10. spring.data.mongodb.representation.big-decimal property not explicitly captured (UUID representation is)

The coverage is strong across all major sections. The gaps are mostly around informational/behavioral changes and a few specific properties. The 3 verification failures (JsonValueDeserializer, StreamBuilderFactoryBeanCustomizer, Skip enum) suggest minor FQN accuracy issues but the patterns themselves are present. Test failures are all due to JAVA_HOME not being set, not pattern issues.

patterns_qualityPASS

73 patterns extracted with all required fields

report_existsPASS

report.yaml valid: 73 rules, 0% pass rate

rule_correctness4

Rules are overwhelmingly correct with accurate source-side when conditions, detailed before/after code examples, specific migration guide URLs, and reasonable category/effort values. Two rules (jackson-import-00030 for JsonValueDeserializer and kafka-import-00010 for StreamBuilderFactoryBeanCustomizer) failed source verification, suggesting potential class name inaccuracies — though these could be version-specific naming issues rather than hallucinations. Test failures are all environmental (JAVA_HOME not set), not rule defects. Messages are thorough with migration steps, additional context, and links. The 0% test pass rate is entirely an infrastructure issue, not a quality issue.

output/spring-boot3-to-spring-boot4-20260624-085756/rules/actuator.yaml
- ruleID: actuator-annotation-00010
  description: org.springframework.lang.Nullable no longer supported for actuator parameters; use org.jspecify.annotations.Nullable
  category: mandatory
  effort: 1
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot3
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot4
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    In Spring Boot 4, actuator endpoint parameters can no longer use `org.springframework.lang.Nullable` to declare that a parameter is optional. You should migrate to `org.jspecify.annotations.Nullable`.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.springframework.lang.Nullable;

    @Endpoint(id = "custom")
    public class CustomEndpoint {
        @ReadOperation
        public String read(@Nullable String param) {
            return param != null ? param : "default";
        }
    }
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import org.jspecify.annotations.Nullable;

    @Endpoint(id = "custom")
    public class CustomEndpoint {
        @ReadOperation
        public String read(@Nullable String param) {
            return param != null ? param : "default";
        }
    }
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - Only the import changes; usage syntax remains the same
    - This specifically affects actuator endpoint parameters; other uses of `@Nullable` may also need migration as part of the broader JSpecify adoption
    - Add the `org.jspecify:jspecify` dependency if not already present
    - See the [migration guide](https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#removed-support-for-javaxannotationsnonnull-and-orgspringframeworklangnullable)
  links:
    - url: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#removed-support-for-javaxannotationsnonnull-and-orgspringframeworklangnullable
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: org.springframework.lang.Nullable
        location: ANNOTATION

  category: potential
  effort: 1

    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    In Spring Boot 4, the liveness and readiness probes are enabled by default. The health endpoint now exposes the `liveness` and `readiness` groups by default.

    ### Migration Steps
    - If you do not need the liveness and readiness probes, disable them by setting `management.endpoint.health.probes.enabled=false` in your configuration
    - If you already had probes enabled explicitly, you can remove the explicit configuration as it is now the default
    - Review your health endpoint security configuration, as the probes are now publicly accessible by default
    - See the [migration guide](https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#liveness-and-readiness-probes)
  links:

      title: Migration Documentation

output/spring-boot3-to-spring-boot4-20260624-085756/rules/amqp.yaml
- ruleID: amqp-import-00010
  description: RabbitRetryTemplateCustomizer replaced by dedicated retry settings customizers
  category: mandatory
  effort: 5
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot3
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot4
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    Spring AMQP has moved its retry capabilities from Spring Retry to Spring Framework's core retry support. The `RabbitRetryTemplateCustomizer` has been replaced by two dedicated customizers: `RabbitTemplateRetrySettingsCustomizer` and `RabbitListenerRetrySettingsCustomizer`.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.springframework.boot.autoconfigure.amqp.RabbitRetryTemplateCustomizer;

    @Bean
    public RabbitRetryTemplateCustomizer retryCustomizer() {
        return (target, retryTemplate) -> {
            // customize retry template
        };
    }
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import org.springframework.boot.autoconfigure.amqp.RabbitTemplateRetrySettingsCustomizer;
    import org.springframework.boot.autoconfigure.amqp.RabbitListenerRetrySettingsCustomizer;

    @Bean
    public RabbitTemplateRetrySettingsCustomizer templateRetryCustomizer() {
        return retrySettings -> {
            // customize template retry settings
        };
    }

    @Bean
    public RabbitListenerRetrySettingsCustomizer listenerRetryCustomizer() {
        return retrySettings -> {
            // customize listener retry settings
        };
    }
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - If you were using `RabbitRetryTemplateCustomizer` to customize retry settings according to a target, you need to migrate to the appropriate dedicated customizer
    - Use `RabbitTemplateRetrySettingsCustomizer` for RabbitTemplate retry settings
    - Use `RabbitListenerRetrySettingsCustomizer` for message listener retry settings
    - Spring AMQP retry is now based on Spring Framework's core retry support instead of Spring Retry
    - See the [Spring Boot 4.0 Migration Guide](https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#spring-amqp-retry-features) for details
  links:
    - url: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#spring-amqp-retry-features
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: org.springframework.boot.autoconfigure.amqp.RabbitRetryTemplateCustomizer
        location: IMPORT

output/spring-boot3-to-spring-boot4-20260624-085756/rules/batch.yaml
- ruleID: batch-dependency-00010
  description: Spring Batch now operates in-memory by default; database metadata requires spring-boot-starter-batch-jdbc
  category: mandatory
  effort: 5
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot3
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot4
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: "Spring Batch can now operate without a database (in-memory mode), and the regular `spring-boot-starter-batch` uses this simplified mode by default. On upgrade, Spring Batch will no longer store metadata in your existing database.\n\n### Migration Steps\n1. **Option A - Use in-memory mode:** If you don't need persistent job metadata, simplify your configuration and use the new in-memory mode. No changes needed to your starter dependency.\n2. **Option B - Restore database mode:** If you need Spring Batch to continue storing metadata in a database, change your dependency from `spring-boot-starter-batch` to `spring-boot-starter-batch-jdbc`:\n   ```xml\n   <!-- Before -->\n   <dependency>\n       <groupId>org.springframework.boot</groupId>\n       <artifactId>spring-boot-starter-batch</artifactId>\n   </dependency>\n   \n   <!-- After (for database metadata) -->\n   <dependency>\n       <groupId>org.springframework.boot</groupId>\n       <artifactId>spring-boot-starter-batch-jdbc</artifactId>\n   </dependency>\n   ```\n\n### Additional Info\n- This is a **breaking change** for applications that rely on persistent job metadata in a database\n- The in-memory mode is suitable for simple batch jobs that don't require restart/recovery capabilities\n- If you have existing job metadata in your database, switching to in-memory mode means that metadata will no longer be updated\n- Review your batch job requirements carefully before choosing the migration path\n- See the [Spring Boot 4.0 Migration Guide](https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#spring-batch) for details"
  links:
    - url: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#spring-batch
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.dependency:
        name: org.springframework.boot.spring-boot-starter-batch
        upperbound: 4.0.0

output/spring-boot3-to-spring-boot4-20260624-085756/rules/build.yaml
- ruleID: build-xml-00010
  description: Embedded executable uber jar launch scripts removed in Spring Boot 4
  category: mandatory
  effort: 3
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot3
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot4
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    Support for embedded launch scripts used to create "fully executable" jar files has been removed from Spring Boot 4. The feature was specific to Unix-like operating systems and had limitations.

    ### Migration Steps
    1. Remove `<executable>true</executable>` from your Maven Spring Boot plugin configuration.
    2. For Gradle, remove `launchScript()` or `launchScript { ... }` from your `bootJar` task configuration.
    3. Run your application using `java -jar` instead of executing the jar directly.
    4. If you need similar functionality, consider using [Gradle's application plugin](https://docs.gradle.org/current/userguide/application_plugin.html).

    ### Additional Info
    - You can still create uber jars with Spring Boot's build plugins.
    - The change aligns with [recommendations for efficient deployments](https://docs.spring.io/spring-boot/4.0-SNAPSHOT/reference/packaging/efficient.html).
    - See the [migration guide](https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#embedded-executable-uber-jar-launch-scripts).
  links:
    - url: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#embedded-executable-uber-jar-launch-scripts
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    builtin.xml:
        xpath: //*[local-name()='executable' and text()='true']
        namespaces:
            m: http://maven.apache.org/POM/4.0.0
        filepaths:
            - pom.xml

  message: |-
    Support for embedded launch scripts used to create "fully executable" jar files has been removed from Spring Boot 4.

    ### Migration Steps
    1. Remove `launchScript()` or `launchScript { ... }` from your `bootJar` task in your Gradle build file.
    2. Run your application using `java -jar` instead of executing the jar directly.
    3. If you need similar functionality, consider using [Gradle's application plugin](https://docs.gradle.org/current/userguide/application_plugin.html).

    ### Additional Info
    - You can still create uber jars with Spring Boot's build plugins.
    - See the [migration guide](https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#embedded-executable-uber-jar-launch-scripts).
