- ruleID: build-xml-00020
  description: Optional dependencies no longer included in uber jars; add includeOptional config if needed
  category: potential
  effort: 3
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot3
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot4
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    Optional dependencies are no longer included in uber jars by default in Spring Boot 4.0. If your application relies on optional dependencies being available at runtime, you need to update your Spring Boot Maven plugin configuration.

    ### Migration Steps
    1. Review your `pom.xml` for any `<optional>true</optional>` dependencies
    2. If those optional dependencies are needed at runtime in the uber jar, add `<includeOptional>true</includeOptional>` to the spring-boot-maven-plugin configuration
    3. If optional dependencies are only needed at compile time, no action is needed

    ### Additional Info
    - This change affects the Spring Boot Maven plugin's repackaging behavior
    - Optional dependencies marked with `<optional>true</optional>` were previously included in uber jars
    - Use `<includeOptional>true</includeOptional>` in the plugin configuration to restore the old behavior
  links:
    - url: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#optional-dependencies-in-maven
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    builtin.xml:
        xpath: //*[local-name()='optional' and text()='true']
        namespaces:
            m: http://maven.apache.org/POM/4.0.0
        filepaths:
            - pom.xml
- ruleID: build-xml-00030
  description: Classic uber-jar loader removed; remove loaderImplementation configuration
  category: mandatory
  effort: 1

    ```xml
        <artifactId>spring-boot-maven-plugin</artifactId>
    </plugin>
    ```

    - Spring Boot 4.0 only supports the default loader implementation
    - Remove the `<loaderImplementation>` element entirely from your Maven configuration

  category: mandatory
  effort: 7

  message: |-
    Spring Boot 4.0 requires Java 17+, Jakarta EE 11 (Servlet 6.1), and Spring Framework 7.x. Before upgrading, ensure you are on the latest Spring Boot 3.5.x version and have reviewed all deprecated API calls.

    ### Migration Steps
    1. Upgrade to the latest Spring Boot 3.5.x version first.
    2. Review and fix all deprecated API usage -- these APIs are removed in 4.0.
    3. Verify your Java version is 17 or later.
    4. If using Kotlin, ensure v2.2 or later.
    5. If using GraalVM native-image, ensure v25 or later.
    6. Update Spring Framework to 7.x.
    7. Upgrade to Spring Boot 4.0.

    ### Additional Info
    - Spring Boot 4 is based on Jakarta EE 11 and requires Servlet 6.1 baseline.
    - Review dependency management changes between [3.5.x](https://docs.spring.io/spring-boot/3.5/appendix/dependency-versions/coordinates.html) and [4.0.x](https://docs.spring.io/spring-boot/4.0-SNAPSHOT/appendix/dependency-versions/coordinates.html).
    - Identify compatible versions of unmanaged dependencies (e.g., Spring Cloud) before upgrading.
    - See the [full migration guide](https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide).
  links:

      title: Migration Documentation

- ruleID: core-import-00010
  description: org.springframework.lang nullable annotations deprecated; migrate to JSpecify annotations
  category: optional
  effort: 5
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot3
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot4
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    Spring Boot 4.0 adds JSpecify nullability annotations. The Spring Framework null-safety annotations from the `org.springframework.lang` package (such as `@Nullable`, `@NonNull`) should be migrated to JSpecify equivalents.

    If you are using a null checker in your build or using Kotlin, this could lead to compilation failures because of now nullable or non-nullable types.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.springframework.lang.Nullable;
    import org.springframework.lang.NonNull;

    public class MyService {
        public String process(@Nullable String input) { ... }
    }
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import org.jspecify.annotations.Nullable;
    import org.jspecify.annotations.NonNull;

    public class MyService {
        public String process(@Nullable String input) { ... }
    }
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - Review the Spring Framework migration guide for null-safety annotations: https://docs.spring.io/spring-framework/reference/core/null-safety.html#null-safety-migrating
    - Kotlin users may see compilation failures due to stricter nullability enforcement
    - The JSpecify annotations provide standardized null-safety across Java libraries
    - Both `@Nullable` and `@NonNull` annotations need to be migrated
  links:
    - url: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#jspecify-nullability-annotations
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: org.springframework.lang
        location: PACKAGE

- ruleID: data-import-00010
  description: RestClientBuilderCustomizer replaced by Rest5ClientBuilderCustomizer for Elasticsearch
  category: mandatory
  effort: 5
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot3
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot4
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    In Spring Boot 4, the auto-configuration for the deprecated low-level Elasticsearch `RestClient` has been replaced with auto-configuration for the new `Rest5Client`. If you were using Spring Boot's `RestClientBuilderCustomizer` to customize the client, you must now use `Rest5ClientBuilderCustomizer` instead.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.springframework.boot.autoconfigure.elasticsearch.RestClientBuilderCustomizer;

    @Bean
    public RestClientBuilderCustomizer myCustomizer() {
        return builder -> builder.setMaxRetryTimeoutMillis(60000);
    }
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import org.springframework.boot.autoconfigure.elasticsearch.Rest5ClientBuilderCustomizer;

    @Bean
    public Rest5ClientBuilderCustomizer myCustomizer() {
        return builder -> builder.setMaxRetryTimeoutMillis(60000);
    }
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - The Elasticsearch client code has been consolidated in the `co.elastic.clients:elasticsearch-java` module
    - Built-in sniffer support is now part of the consolidated module
    - Support for `ElasticsearchClient` and Spring Data Elasticsearch's `ReactiveElasticsearchClient` remains, updated to use the new low-level client
    - See the [migration guide](https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#elasticsearch-client)
  links:
    - url: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#elasticsearch-client
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: org.springframework.boot.autoconfigure.elasticsearch.RestClientBuilderCustomizer
        location: IMPORT

    ```xml
        <groupId>co.elastic.clients</groupId>

    </dependency>
    ```

    In Spring Boot 4, a new `spring-boot-persistence` module has been created. Users of `@EntityScan` should adapt their imports to use the new package.

    ### Before
    ```java

    @EntityScan("com.example.entities")

    }
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import org.springframework.boot.persistence.autoconfigure.EntityScan;

    @EntityScan("com.example.entities")
    @SpringBootApplication
    public class MyApplication {
    }
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - Only the import changes; the annotation usage and behavior remain the same
    - The `spring-boot-persistence` module is a new module housing general persistence-related code
    - See the [migration guide](https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#persistence-modules)

      - `spring.data.mongodb.replica-set-name` → `spring.mongodb.replica-set-name`

  description: Flyway now requires spring-boot-starter-flyway instead of a direct dependency in Spring Boot 4

  message: |-
    In Spring Boot 4's modular design, Flyway auto-configuration is now in a dedicated module. If you previously only had the `org.flywaydb:flyway-core` dependency, you now need the Spring Boot starter.

    ### Before
    ```xml
    <dependency>
        <groupId>org.flywaydb</groupId>
        <artifactId>flyway-core</artifactId>
    </dependency>
    ```

    ### After
    ```xml
    <dependency>
        <groupId>org.springframework.boot</groupId>
        <artifactId>spring-boot-starter-flyway</artifactId>
    </dependency>
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - The starter pulls in `flyway-core` transitively, so you can remove the direct dependency.
    - Test infrastructure is available via `spring-boot-starter-flyway-test`.
    - This change is part of Spring Boot 4's modularization effort.
    - See the [migration guide](https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#main-code).

    - url: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#main-code
      title: Migration Documentation

        name: org.flywaydb.flyway-core
        lowerbound: 0.0.0

- ruleID: dependencies-dependency-00010
  description: spring-boot-starter-aop renamed to spring-boot-starter-aspectj
  category: mandatory
  effort: 3
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot3
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot4
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    The `spring-boot-starter-aop` has been renamed to `spring-boot-starter-aspectj` in Spring Boot 4.0 to clarify its scope.

    Before replacing, review whether you actually need AspectJ support:
    - Check if your application uses AspectJ annotations from the `org.aspectj.lang.annotation` package
    - Search for usage of `org.aspectj.lang.annotation.Aspect` on the classpath

    ### Before
    ```xml
    <dependency>
        <groupId>org.springframework.boot</groupId>
        <artifactId>spring-boot-starter-aop</artifactId>
    </dependency>
    ```

    ### After
    ```xml
    <dependency>
        <groupId>org.springframework.boot</groupId>
        <artifactId>spring-boot-starter-aspectj</artifactId>
    </dependency>
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - Review if you actually need AspectJ before using the replacement
    - Libraries on the classpath may use `@Aspect` (e.g., Micrometer's `@Timed` or `@Counted`)
    - If you don't use AspectJ, you may not need this starter at all
  links:
    - url: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#aop-starter-pom
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.dependency:
        name: org.springframework.boot.spring-boot-starter-aop
        lowerbound: 0.0.0
- ruleID: dependencies-dependency-00020
  description: Dependency management for Spring Retry removed; explicit version required
  category: mandatory
  effort: 3
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot3
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot4
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    Dependency management for Spring Retry has been removed from Spring Boot 4.0. The Spring portfolio is moving from Spring Retry to new core retry features in Spring Framework 7.0.

    If your application still relies on Spring Retry, you must now specify an explicit version.

    ### Before
    ```xml
    <dependency>
        <groupId>org.springframework.retry</groupId>
        <artifactId>spring-retry</artifactId>
        <!-- version managed by Spring Boot -->
    </dependency>
    ```

    ### After
    ```xml
    <dependency>
        <groupId>org.springframework.retry</groupId>
        <artifactId>spring-retry</artifactId>
        <version>2.0.11</version>
    </dependency>
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - Consider migrating to Spring Framework 7.0's built-in retry features: https://docs.spring.io/spring-framework/docs/7.0.x-SNAPSHOT/javadoc-api/org/springframework/core/retry/package-summary.html
    - Without an explicit version, the dependency will fail to resolve
    - The Spring portfolio is moving away from Spring Retry long-term
  links:
    - url: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#dependency-management-for-spring-retry
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.dependency:
        name: org.springframework.retry.spring-retry
        lowerbound: 0.0.0
- ruleID: dependencies-import-00010
  description: GraphQL auto-configuration classes moved from autoconfigure.graphql to boot.graphql module
  category: mandatory
  effort: 3
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot3
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot4
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    In Spring Boot 4, the module structure was reorganized. GraphQL support is now in the dedicated `spring-boot-graphql` module with root package `org.springframework.boot.graphql`. Classes previously under `org.springframework.boot.autoconfigure.graphql` have moved to `org.springframework.boot.graphql`.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.springframework.boot.autoconfigure.graphql.GraphQlAutoConfiguration;
    import org.springframework.boot.autoconfigure.graphql.GraphQlSourceBuilderCustomizer;
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import org.springframework.boot.graphql.GraphQlAutoConfiguration;
    import org.springframework.boot.graphql.GraphQlSourceBuilderCustomizer;
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - All Spring Boot modules follow the naming convention `spring-boot-<technology>` with root package `org.springframework.boot.<technology>`
    - The starter POM is `spring-boot-starter-graphql`
    - Update all imports from `org.springframework.boot.autoconfigure.graphql` to `org.springframework.boot.graphql`
    - See the [migration guide](https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#main-code)
  links:
    - url: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#main-code
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: org.springframework.boot.autoconfigure.graphql*
        location: PACKAGE

- ruleID: devtools-dependency-00010
  description: DevTools Live Reload is now disabled by default in Spring Boot 4
  category: potential
  effort: 1
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot3
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot4
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    DevTools Live Reload support is now disabled by default in Spring Boot 4.0. If your development workflow relies on live reload, you need to explicitly enable it.

    ### Migration Steps
    1. Add `spring.devtools.livereload.enabled=true` to your `application.properties` or `application.yml` to re-enable live reload
    2. If you were not using live reload, no action is needed

    ### Additional Info
    - This is a behavioral default change — live reload was previously enabled by default
    - The property `spring.devtools.livereload.enabled` must be set to `true` to restore the previous behavior
    - Consider whether live reload is necessary for your development workflow before re-enabling
  links:
    - url: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#devtools-live-reload-support
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.dependency:
        name: org.springframework.boot.spring-boot-devtools
        upperbound: 4.0.0

behavior\n56\t\n57\t## Permissions\n58\t\n59\t| Operation | Pattern | Purpose |\n60\t|-----------|---------|---------|\n61\t| shell | `mkdir -p output` | Create output directory |\n62\t| shell | `go run ./cmd/ingest *` | Fetch migration guide as markdown |\n63\t| shell | `go run ./cmd/sections *` | Index guide sections with classification |\n64\t| shell | `go run ./cmd/merge-patterns *` | Merge |\n67\t| shell | `go run ./cmd/construct *` | Build rule YAML from patterns.json |\n68\t| shell | `go run ./cmd/validate *` | Validate rule YAML structure |\n69\t| shell | `go run ./cmd/scaffold *` | Create test directories and manifests |\n70\t| shell | `go run ./cmd/sanitize *` | Fix XML comments in test data |\n71\t| shell | `go run ./cmd/test *` | Run kantra tests |\n72\t| shell | `go run pipeline log |\n75\t| shell | `ls *` | List files and directories |\n76\t| read | `output/**` | Read manifest, test results |\n77\t| write | `output/**` | Write migration artifacts |\n78\t\n79\t**Do NOT use `python`, `python3`, `node`, or any scripting language runtime.**\n80\t**Do NOT use `grep`, `sed`, `awk`, `wc`, `find`, or other shell text-processing tools to parse data that CLI commands already return.**\n81\tEvery `go run ./cmd/*` command returns structured JSON. Use that JSON output directly \u2014 do not pipe it through shell commands to extract fields.\n82\tThis is a Go project. Run only commands listed in this permissions table.\n83\tIf a required action is not permitted, stop and report the limitation.\n84\t\n85\t## UX Principles\n86\t\n87\t- Emit short status lines continuously (start + finish for each step).\n88\t- Only ask at checkpoint when `mode=interactive` and `checkpoint_behavior=ask`.\n89\t- Do not block after testing starts; continue even if some rules remain failing.\n90\t- Fix only failing rules, not the full suite.\n91\t\n92\tFor pipeline logging conventions, see `references/orchestrator-details.md` (Pipeline Transcript section).\n93\t\n94\tFor stage timing instructions, see `references/orchestrator-details.md` (Timing section).\n95\t\n96\tFor sub-agent invocation protocol and contract validation, see `references/orchestrator-details.md` (Sub-agent Protocol section).\n97\t\n98\t## Pipeline\n99\t\n100\t**Error handling:** If any CLI command (`ingest`, `construct`, `validate`, `scaffold`, `sanitize`, `test`, `report`) exits non-zero, print `[step] FAILED \u2014 <error>` and stop the pipeline. Do not proceed to the next step.\n101\t\n102\t**Partial failures:** If a step produces partial results before failing (e.g., `construct` succeeds for 48 patterns but fails on 2), preserve the partial output and report what succeeded. The user can fix the failing patterns and re-run. Do not discard valid results because of a partial failure.\n103\t\n104\t**Resume behavior:** When `resume_from` is set, the user must also provide `migration_dir` pointing to the specific timestamped directory to resume. Skip prior stages and validate prerequisites first. Fail fast when required artifacts are missing.\n105\t\n106\tStage prerequisites (paths relative to `<migration_dir>`):\n107\t- `extract` requires `guide.md`\n108\t- `coverage` requires `patterns.json`\n109\t- `scaffold` requires `rules/`\n110\t- `test` requires `rules/` and `tests/manifest.json`\n111\t- `report` requires source/target metadata plus pass/fail totals and rule ID lists\n112\t\n113\t### 1. Ingest\n114\t\n115\tGenerate a timestamp once at pipeline start (`YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS` in local time).\n116\t\n117\tDetermine the migration directory path:\n118\t- If the user provided `migration_dir`, use that (no timestamp)\n119\t- If the user provided `sources` and `targets` (or `source` and `target`), use `output/<primary_source>-to-<primary_target>-<YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS>` where `primary_source` is `sources[0]` and `primary_target` is `targets[0]`\n120\t- If auto-detecting: ingest to `output/guide-temp.md` first, read the first ~50 lines to detect source/target/language (lowercase, hyphenated names like `spring-boot-3`), then use `output/<source>-to-<target>-<YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS>`\n121\t\n122\t```bash\n123\tmkdir -p output/<source>-to-<target>-<YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS>\n124\t```\n125\t\n126\tEvery `go run` command should be a standalone invocation with fully-expanded arguments \u2014 substitute actual paths and flag values directly into each command. Do not use shell variable assignments (`VAR=...`) or compound `&&` chains, since these don't match the permissions table.\n127\t\n128\tThe log flags are: `--log <migration_dir>/pipeline.log --agent orchestrator --model <your_model_id>`. Append these literally to every CLI invocation.\n129\t\n130\t```\n131\t[ingest] Fetching guide from <source>...\n132\t```\n133\t\n134\t- **URL:** `go run ./cmd/ingest --log <migration_dir>/pipeline.log --agent orchestrator --model <your_model_id> --input <url> --output <migration_dir>/guide.md`\n135\t- **File (not markdown):** `go run ./cmd/ingest --log <migration_dir>/pipeline.log --agent orchestrator --model <your_model_id> --input <path> --output <migration_dir>/guide.md`\n136\t- **Pasted text or already markdown:** Write directly to `<migration_dir>/guide.md`\n137\t\n138\tIf auto-detecting, write `output/guide-temp.md` to `<migration_dir>/guide.md` using the Write tool after the migration directory path is determined.\n139\t\n140\t**Stub detection \u2014 follow sub-pages.** After ingesting each URL, check the output for stub characteristics. A page is a stub if it has fewer than 100 non-blank lines of content after `cmd/ingest` processing (`cmd/ingest` already strips `<nav>`, `<footer>`, and `<aside>` elements during HTML-to-markdown conversion, so no additional filtering is needed).\n141\t\n142\tIf a stub is detected:\n143\t\n144\t1. Read the ingested markdown and extract all links whose resolved URL shares the same base path as the original URL (same-origin sibling pages). Sibling links are those pointing to `*.html` files under the same directory path as the original URL. Exclude external links, anchor-only links (`#...`), and links to parent directories.\n145\t2. For each sibling link, resolve it to a full URL relative to the original URL's base path.\n146\t3. Ingest each sub-page with `cmd/ingest` into a separate file (`guide-part-<N>.md`).\n147\t4. Concatenate all parts (original + sub-pages) into the final `guide.md`, in the order the links appear in the stub page (document order).\n148\t5. If a sub-page fetch fails (404, timeout), log a warning (`[ingest] WARNING \u2014 failed to fetch <url>: <error>`) and skip that page. Do not abort the pipeline \u2014 partial content is better than none.\n149\t\n150\tThis ensures that documentation sites which split content across multiple pages are fully captured. Without this step, the pipeline will only see the stub and miss the bulk of the migration content.\n151\t\n152\tCount lines (`GUIDE_LINES`) and section headings. Print:\n153\t\n154\t```\n155\t[ingest] Done \u2014 <GUIDE_LINES> lines, <N> sections \u2192 <migration_dir>/ (<elapsed>)\n156\t```\n157\t\n158\t### 2. Extract (parallel)\n159\t\n160\tExtraction uses parallel agents to process the guide faster. The orchestrator splits the guide into chunks and spawns multiple rule-writer agents.\n161\t\n162\t**2a. Index sections and auto-detect metadata:**\n163\t\n164\t```bash\n165\tgo run ./cmd/sections <log_flags> --guide <migration_dir>/guide.md\n166\t```\n167\t\n168\tThis returns JSON with all sections classified as `content` or `header-only`. Filter to content sections only.\n169\t\n170\t```\n171\t[extract] Extracting patterns from <content_count> sections (<N> parallel agents)...\n172\t```\n173\t\n174\t**2b. Split into chunks and dispatch:**\n175\t\n176\tSplit the content sections into **N balanced chunks** (minimum 1, maximum 5 agents). Balance by section count. Assign each chunk a number (1, 2, ..., N).\n177\t\n178\t**Keep related sections together.** Group sections by their top-level heading (`##`) \u2014 all subsections (`###`, `####`) under the same `##` must stay in the same chunk. Migration guides pair before/after code examples across subsections within a topic; splitting them across agents means no agent sees both sides of the diff. Balance chunks by top-level-heading groups, not by individual sections.\n179\t\n180\t**Invoke:** `rule-writer` (one per chunk, in parallel)\n181\t**Purpose:** Extract migration patterns from assigned sections.\n182\t**Inputs per invocation:**\n183\t  - guide: <migration_dir>/guide.md\n184\t  - sources: {sources array (e.g., [\"spring-boot3\", \"spring-boot\"])}\n185\t  - targets: {targets array (e.g., [\"spring-boot4\", \"spring-boot\"])}\n186\t  - rules_dir: <migration_dir>/rules\n187\t  - sections: {chunk subset \u2014 list of `{heading, start_line, end_line}` objects}\n188\t  - all_headings: {full list of ALL content section headings from step 2a \u2014 not just this chunk's sections. Enables each agent to detect multi-path migrations even when variant sections are in other chunks.}\n189\t  - output_file: <migration_dir>/patterns-{chunk_number}.json\n190\t**Parallel:** yes\n191\t**Expect:**\n192\t  - patterns_count, output_file\n193\t\n194\t**2c. Merge, verify, and construct:**\n195\t\n196\tAfter all agents complete, merge the partial patterns files, verify source artifacts, and build rules:\n197\t\n198\t```bash\n199\tgo run ./cmd/merge-patterns <log_flags> --output <migration_dir>/patterns.json <migration_dir>/patterns-1.json <migration_dir>/patterns-2.json ...\n200\tgo run ./cmd/verify <log_flags> --patterns <migration_dir>/patterns.json --output <migration_dir>/verify-results.json --cache <migration_dir>/verify-cache\n201\tgo run ./cmd/construct <log_flags> --patterns <migration_dir>/patterns.json --output <migration_dir>/rules\n202\tgo run ./cmd/validate <log_flags> --rules <migration_dir>/rules\n203\t```\n204\t\n205\t**Verification step:** `cmd/verify` downloads source JARs from Maven Central and checks that each pattern's `source_fqn` exists in the declared `source_artifact`. This catches hallucinated class names before rules reach testing.\n206\t\n207\tThe verify stdout JSON contains `verified`, `not_found`, `skipped`, and `offline` counts. Print:\n208\t\n209\t```\n210\t[verify] <verified> verified, <not_found> not found, <skipped> skipped\n211\t```\n212\t\n213\tIf `not_found > 0`, read `<migration_dir>/verify-results.json` and note which `pattern_index` values have `status: \"not_found\"`. After construct runs, use the `pattern_rule_map` from construct's stdout JSON to map each `pattern_index` \u2192 `rule_id`. Carry `verified_rule_ids` and `not_found_rule_ids` forward to step 5 (report).\n214\t\n215\tIf validation fails, fix `<migration_dir>/patterns.json` (remove invalid entries) and re-run construct.\n216\t\n217\t```\n218\t[extract] Done \u2014 <patterns_count> patterns \u2192 <rules_count> rules in <migration_dir>/rules/ (<elapsed>)\n219\t```\n220\t\n221\tSave `source`, `target`, `patterns_count`, `rules_count`, and verify counts for the final summary.\n222\t\n223\t### 2d. Coverage Check\n224\t\n225\tRun the coverage tool to find sections with named artifacts that weren't extracted:\n226\t\n227\t```bash\n228\tgo run ./cmd/coverage <log_flags> --guide <migration_dir>/guide.md --patterns <migration_dir>/patterns.json --language <language>\n229\t```\n230\t\n231\tIf `gap_count > 0` in the JSON output, print:\n232\t\n233\t```\n234\t[coverage] <gap_count> sections with uncovered artifacts: <heading_1>, <heading_2>, ...\n235\t```\n236\t\n237\tConvert gaps to sections and send back to the rule-writer in chunk mode for targeted re-extraction. Each gap has `heading` and `line` \u2014 use the sections index to get the `start_line` and `end_line` for that heading. Mention the uncovered artifacts in the prompt so the sub-agent focuses on them.\n238\t\n239\t**Invoke:** `rule-writer` (chunk mode)\n240\t**Purpose:** Extract patterns from specific sections that the coverage check flagged.\n241\t**Inputs:**\n242\t  - guide: <migration_dir>/guide.md\n243\t  - sources: {sources array}\n244\t  - targets: {targets array}\n245\t  - rules_dir: <migration_dir>/rules\n246\t  - sections: {gap sections converted to `[{heading, start_line, end_line}]` format}\n247\t  - output_file: <migration_dir>/patterns-gaps.json\n248\t**Parallel:** no\n249\t**Expect:**\n250\t  - patterns_count, output_file\n251\t\n252\tThe sub-agent writes only the new patterns to `<migration_dir>/patterns-gaps.json`. It does NOT read or inspect existing patterns \u2014 the orchestrator handles deduplication. After the sub-agent returns, merge, verify, and rebuild:\n253\t\n254\t```bash\n255\tgo run ./cmd/merge-patterns <log_flags> --output <migration_dir>/patterns.json <migration_dir>/patterns.json <migration_dir>/patterns-gaps.json\n256\tgo run ./cmd/verify <log_flags> --patterns <migration_dir>/patterns.json --output <migration_dir>/verify-results.json --cache <migration_dir>/verify-cache\n257\tgo run ./cmd/construct <log_flags> --patterns <migration_dir>/patterns.json --output <migration_dir>/rules\n258\tgo run ./cmd/validate <log_flags> --rules <migration_dir>/rules\n259\t```\n260\t\n261\tRe-run the coverage check. If gaps remain, accept them \u2014 one re-extraction pass is enough.\n262\t\n263\t```\n264\t[coverage] Done \u2014 <final_gap_count> remaining gaps (accepted) (<elapsed>)\n265\t```\n266\t\n267\tIf `gap_count == 0`:\n268\t\n269\t```\n270\t[coverage] No gaps found (<elapsed>)\n271\t```\n272\t\n273\t### Checkpoint\n274\t\n275\tAfter extraction/coverage:\n276\t\n277\t- If `mode=non_interactive`, do **not** prompt:\n278\t  - `checkpoint_behavior=continue` or `ask`: continue automatically\n279\t  - `checkpoint_behavior=stop_after_extract`: skip testing and go to Step 5 (Report)\n280\t- If `mode=interactive`:\n281\t  - `checkpoint_behavior=continue`: continue automatically\n282\t  - `checkpoint_behavior=stop_after_extract`: skip testing and go to Step 5 (Report)\n283\t  - `checkpoint_behavior=ask`: ask:\n284\t    - `Continue with test generation and validation? (y/n)`\n285\t    - if no, skip to Step 5 (Report) with untested rules\n286\t\n287\t**Rules-only report:** When skipping to Step 5, invoke `cmd/report` with `--passed 0 --failed 0 --kantra-limitation 0` and empty `--passed-rules`, `--failed-rules`, `--kantra-limitation-rules` flags. Pass `--rules-total`, `--verified-rules`, and `--not-found-rules` from extraction. All rules get `test_status: untested`.\n288\t\n289\t### 3. Test Generation\n290\t\n291\t**3a. Scaffold (orchestrator runs this directly, not an agent):**\n292\t\n293\t```bash\n294\tgo run ./cmd/scaffold <log_flags> --rules <migration_dir>/rules --output <migration_dir>/tests --patterns <migration_dir>/patterns.json\n295\t```\n296\t\n297\tThis creates all directories, `.test.yaml` files, and `manifest.json`. No LLM needed.\n298\t\n299\t**3b. Read manifest and split into batches:**\n300\t\n301\tRead `<migration_dir>/tests/manifest.json`. It contains a `groups` array \u2014 each group has `name`, `data_dir`, `files` (paths to generate), and `rule_ids`.\n302\t\n303\tSplit the groups into **batches of ~5 groups each** (minimum 1 batch, maximum 5 batches), balanced by rule count.\n304\t\n305\t**3c. Spawn test-generator agents:**\n306\t\n307\t```\n308\t[test-gen] Generating test data for <rules_count> rules (<B> parallel agents)...\n309\t```\n310\t\n311\t**Invoke:** `test-generator` (one per batch, up to 5 in parallel)\n312\t**Purpose:** Generate compilable test source code that triggers the assigned rules.\n313\t**Inputs per invocation:**\n314\t  - rules_dir: <migration_dir>/rules\n315\t  - tests_dir: <migration_dir>/tests\n316\t  - groups: {batch subset from manifest.json \u2014 include name, data_dir, rule_ids, files}\n317\t**Parallel:** yes\n318\t**Expect:**\n319\t  - groups_completed, files_written\n320\t\n321\t**3d. Collect results and sanitize.** After all agents complete:\n322\t\n323\tCollect `suspected_kantra_limitations` from all rule-writer and test-generator agent returns (merge, deduplicate by `rule_id`). If non-empty, print:\n324\t\n325\t```\n326\t[test-gen] <N> suspected kantra limitations (Maven Central: no plain-semver version): <rule_id_1>, ...\n327\t```\n328\t\n329\tCarry this merged list forward as `pre_classified_kantra_limitations` \u2014 it will be passed to the rule-validator to skip the fix loop for these rules.\n330\t\n331\tSanitize XML:\n332\t\n333\t```bash\n334\tgo run ./cmd/sanitize <log_flags> --dir <migration_dir>/tests/data\n335\t```\n336\t\n337\t```\n338\t[test-gen] Done \u2014 <total_groups> groups, <total_files> files (<elapsed>)\n339\t```\n340\t\n341\t### 4. Validate (orchestrator-driven loop)\n342\t\n343\tThe orchestrator runs tests and uses a sub-agent for LLM-driven repairs on failures.\n344\t\n345\t**4a. Run tests:**\n346\t\n347\t```bash\n348\tgo run ./cmd/test <log_flags> --rules <migration_dir>/rules --tests <migration_dir>/tests --timeout 5m\n349\t```\n350\t\n351\tThe CLI runs each test file sequentially and automatically retries timed-out files once (`--retry-timeouts`, on by default). Tests run locally via `--run-local=true`. To run a subset, use `--files` with bare filenames (e.g., `--files data-1.test.yaml,data-2.test.yaml`), resolved relative to `--tests` dir.\n352\t\n353\tPrint the result:\n354\t\n355\t```\n356\t[validate] <total_passed>/<total_rules> passed (<elapsed>)\n357\t```\n358\t\n359\tOr if failures:\n360\t\n361\t```\n362\t[validate] <total_passed>/<total_rules> passed \u2014 <F> failures: <rule_id_1>, <rule_id_2>, ...\n363\t```\n364\t\n365\tIf all passed (elapsed shown above), skip to step 5.\n366\t\n367\t**4b. Fix (only if failures):**\n368\t\n369\t```\n370\t[fix] Fixing <F> failures: <rule_id_1>, <rule_id_2> ...\n371\t```\n372\t\n373\t**Invoke:** `rule-validator`\n374\t**Purpose:** Fix test data for failing rules so they pass kantra validation.\n375\t**Inputs:**\n376\t  - rules_dir: <migration_dir>/rules\n377\t  - tests_dir: <migration_dir>/tests\n378\t  - failing_rules: {list with rule_id, test_file, error for each failure}\n379\t  - pre_classified_kantra_limitations: {merged list from rule-writer and test-generator suspected_kantra_limitations \u2014 may be empty}\n380\t  - max_iterations: 1\n381\t**Parallel:** no\n382\t**Expect:**\n383\t  - fixed_rules, still_failing, kantra_limitation_rules, iterations_used, fix_details\n384\t  - results_by_rule (with `result_type` + `recommended_action`)\n385\t\n386\tThe validator agent owns the fix-verify loop \u2014 it fixes files, re-runs tests via `cmd/test`, and iterates up to `max_iterations`. Default is 1 iteration; pass up to 3 if the user requests more attempts.\n387\t\n388\t**The orchestrator must NOT run its own fix attempts.** Do not manually edit test files, create stub classes, toggle analysisParams, or retry. All fix work goes through the rule-validator sub-agent. When the validator returns `still_failing`, accept that result and move on.\n389\t\n390\tPrint the result:\n391\t\n392\t```\n393\t[fix] <fixed_count> fixed, <still_failing_count> still failing, <kantra_limitation_count> kantra limitations (<validate elapsed>)\n394\t```\n395\t\n396\tThe `<validate elapsed>` is the total time since the validate stage started (step 4a), including test runs and all fix iterations.\n397\t\n398\tIf `kantra_limitation_rules` is non-empty, print:\n399\t\n400\t```\n401\t[fix] kantra limitations (engine cannot test \u2014 rule is correct): <rule_id_1>, ...\n402\t```\n403\t\n404\tGroup unresolved failures by `result_type` in `results_by_rule` and include grouped counts in the final summary (e.g., `still_failing_timeout: 2`, `still_failing_kantra_limitation: 1`).\n405\t\n406\tIf still_failing is non-empty, move on \u2014 don't block the pipeline.\n407\t\n408\t### 5. Report\n409\t\n410\tCollate pass/fail results from the test run and the fix loop. Generate `report.yaml` with per-rule test and verification status. No labels are written to rule YAML files \u2014 all pipeline metadata lives in the report.\n411\t\n412\t```bash\n413\tgo run ./cmd/report <log_flags> --source <comma-separated sources> --target <comma-separated targets> --output <migration_dir>/report.yaml --rules-total <N> --passed <P> --failed <F> --kantra-limitation <K> --passed-rules <comma-separated passed rule IDs> --failed-rules <comma-separated failed rule IDs> --kantra-limitation-rules <comma-separated kantra limitation rule IDs> --verified-rules <comma-separated verified rule IDs> --not-found-rules <comma-separated not-found rule IDs>\n414\t```\n415\t\n416\tThe `--verified-rules` and `--not-found-rules` flags come from the verification mapping built in step 2c (pattern_index \u2192 rule_id via construct's pattern_rule_map).\n417\t\n418\tThe report includes a `rules` section with per-rule `test_status` (passed/failed/kantra-limitation/untested) and `source_verified` (true/false). The pass rate is computed as `passed / (passed + failed)` \u2014 kantra limitations are excluded since they are not failures, but also not confirmed passes.\n419\t\n420\t### 6. Summary\n421\t\n422\tPrint a formatted summary table using GitHub-flavored markdown:\n423\t\n424\t```markdown\n425\t## Summary\n426\t\n427\t| | |\n428\t|---|---|\n429\t| **Input** | <guide title or URL as a markdown link> |\n430\t| **Migration** | <primary_source> \u2192 <primary_target> (<language>) |\n431\t| **Guide** | <GUIDE_LINES> lines, <N> sections \u2192 <M> produced patterns, <K> skipped |\n432\t| **Rules** | <rules_count> generated, **<P>/<N> passed (<percent>%)** |\n433\t| **Verification** | <verified>/<total> source-verified, <not_found> not found, <skipped> skipped (omit row if all skipped) |\n434\t| **Kantra limitations** | <K> rules correct but not auto-testable \u2014 engine cannot compare non-semver versions (omit row if K=0) |\n435\t| **Fix iterations** | <iterations used, 0 if none> |\n436\t| **Timing** | total: <total elapsed> \u2014 ingest: <elapsed>, extract: <elapsed>, coverage: <elapsed>, test-gen: <elapsed>, validate: <elapsed>, report: <elapsed> |\n437\t| **Output** | `<migration_dir>/patterns.json` (patterns), `<migration_dir>/rules/` (rules), `<migration_dir>/tests/` (tests), `<migration_dir>/report.yaml` (report) |\n438\t\n439\t### Rule Categories\n440\t\n441\tUse the `groups` array from the `construct` JSON output \u2014 it lists each file and its rule count. Do not iterate rule files manually.\n442\t\n443\t| Group | Rules | Status |\n444\t|---|---|---|\n445\t| <group_name> (<brief description of what rules cover>) | <rule_count> | <passed>/<total> passed |\n446\t| ... | ... | ... |\n447\t```\n448\t\n449\tIf there are failures, add a row to the top-level table:\n450\t\n451\t```\n452\t| **Failed** | <rule_id_1>, <rule_id_2>, ... |\n453\t```\n454\t\n455\tIf coverage was low (< 30% of sections produced patterns), add a row:\n456\t\n457\t```\n458\t| **Warning** | Low extraction coverage (<M>/<K> sections) |\n459\t```\n460\t\n461\t**Rules-only summary (when `checkpoint_behavior=stop_after_extract`):**\n462\t\n463\tWhen testing was skipped, use this simplified table instead:\n464\t\n465\t```markdown\n466\t## Summary\n467\t\n468\t| | |\n469\t|---|---|\n470\t| **Input** | <guide title or URL as a markdown link> |\n471\t| **Migration** | <primary_source> \u2192 <primary_target> (<language>) |\n472\t| **Guide** | <GUIDE_LINES> lines, <N> sections \u2192 <M> produced patterns, <K> skipped |\n473\t| **Rules** | <rules_count> generated (untested) |\n474\t| **Verification** | <verified>/<total> source-verified, <not_found> not found, <skipped> skipped (omit row if all skipped) |\n475\t| **Timing** | total: <total elapsed> \u2014 ingest: <elapsed>, extract: <elapsed>, coverage: <elapsed>, report: <elapsed> |\n476\t| **Output** | `<migration_dir>/patterns.json` (patterns), `<migration_dir>/rules/` (rules), `<migration_dir>/report.yaml` (report) |\n477\t| **Next step** | Run `/generate-rules-with-test resume_from=scaffold migration_dir=<migration_dir>` to add tests |\n478\t```\n479\t\n480\tOmit these rows: **Kantra limitations**, **Fix iterations**, **Failed** (no testing ran).\n481\tOmit `tests/` from the **Output** row and test-gen/validate timing from the **Timing** row.\n482\tInclude the **Rule Categories** table as normal.\n483\t",

# Spring Boot 4.0 Migration Guide

[Jump to bottom](#wiki-pages-box)

Andy Wilkinson edited this page Apr 30, 2026 · [67 revisions](/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide/_history)

This document is meant to help you migrate your application to Spring Boot 4.0.

## Before You Start

[](#before-you-start)

### Upgrade to the Latest `3.5.x` Version

[](#upgrade-to-the-latest-35x-version)

Before you start the upgrade, make sure to upgrade to the latest available `3.5.x` version. This will make sure that you are building against the most recent dependencies of that line.

Please take time to review any calls you might be making to deprecated methods as these will be removed in Spring Boot 4.0.

### Review Dependencies

[](#review-dependencies)

The move to Spring Boot 4 will upgrade a number of dependencies and might require work on your end. You can review [dependency management for `3.5.x`](https://docs.spring.io/spring-boot/3.5/appendix/dependency-versions/coordinates.html) with [dependency management for `4.0.x`](https://docs.spring.io/spring-boot/4.0-SNAPSHOT/appendix/dependency-versions/coordinates.html) to asses how your project is affected.

You may also use dependencies that are not managed by Spring Boot (e.g. [Spring Cloud](https://github.com/spring-cloud/spring-cloud-release/wiki/Supported-Versions#supported-releases)). As your project defines an explicit version for those, identify the compatible version before upgrading.

### Review System Requirements

[](#review-system-requirements)

Spring Boot 4.0 requires Java 17 or later. Using the latest LTS release of Java is encouraged.

Spring Boot applications can also be developed using Kotlin where v2.2 or later must be used.

If you’re using GraalVM’s native-image, v25 or later must be used.

Spring Boot 4 is based on Jakarta EE 11 and requires a Servlet 6.1 baseline.

If you manage dependencies directly, make sure you update them accordingly. In particular, you must use Spring Framework 7.x.

### Review Deprecations from Spring Boot 3.x

[](#review-deprecations-from-spring-boot-3x)

Classes, methods and properties that were deprecated in Spring Boot 3.x have been removed in this release. Please ensure that you aren’t calling deprecated methods before upgrading.

## Upgrade to Spring Boot 4

[](#upgrade-to-spring-boot-4)

Once you have reviewed the state of your project and its dependencies, upgrade to the latest maintenance release of Spring Boot 4.0.

### Configuration Properties Migration

[](#configuration-properties-migration)

Configuration properties were renamed/removed and developers need to update their `application.properties`/`application.yml` accordingly. To help you with that, Spring Boot provides a `spring-boot-properties-migrator` module. Once added as a dependency to your project, this will not only analyze your application’s environment and print diagnostics at startup, but also temporarily migrate properties at runtime for you.

You can add the migrator by adding the following to your Maven `pom.xml`:

```
<dependency>
	<groupId>org.springframework.boot</groupId>
	<artifactId>spring-boot-properties-migrator</artifactId>
	<scope>runtime</scope>
</dependency>
```

Or if you use Gradle:

```
runtimeOnly("org.springframework.boot:spring-boot-properties-migrator")
```

| Note | Once you’re done with the migration, please make sure to remove this module from your project’s dependencies. |
|------|---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|

### Features Removed From This Release

[](#features-removed-from-this-release)

The features have been removed from this release and are no longer available

#### Undertow

[](#undertow)

Spring Boot 4 requires a Servlet 6.1 baseline, with which Undertow is not yet compatible. As a result, Undertow support is dropped, including the Undertow starter and the ability to use Undertow as an embedded server.

We do not recommend deploying Spring Boot 4.0 applications to a non-Servlet 6.1 compliant container.

#### Pulsar Reactive

[](#pulsar-reactive)

Following the decision of removing reactor support in Spring Pulsar, Spring Boot no longer manages the reactive Pulsar client. Auto-configuration for Spring Pulsar Reactive has been removed as well.

#### Embedded Executable Uber Jar Launch Scripts

[](#embedded-executable-uber-jar-launch-scripts)

Support for embedded launch scripts, used to create "fully executable" jar files, has been removed. The support was specific to Unix-like operating systems and had a number of limitations, most notably conflicting with the [recommendations for efficient deployments](https://docs.spring.io/spring-boot/4.0-SNAPSHOT/reference/packaging/efficient.html). If you still require similar functionality, we recommend looking at alternatives such as [Gradle’s application plugin](https://docs.gradle.org/current/userguide/application_plugin.html).

You can still create uber jars with Spring Boot’s build plugins and run them using `java -jar`.

#### Spring Session Hazelcast

[](#spring-session-hazelcast)

Spring Session Hazelcast is now under the [leadership of the Hazelcast team](https://spring.io/blog/2025/10/14/spring-session-hazelcast-new-leadership). As such, direct support for Spring Session Hazelcast has been removed from Spring Boot itself.

#### Spring Session MongoDB

[](#spring-session-mongodb)

Spring Session MongoDB is now under the [leadership of the MongoDB team](https://spring.io/blog/2025/10/14/spring-session-mongodb-new-leadership). As such, direct support for Spring Session MongoDB has been removed from Spring Boot itself.

#### Spock Integration

[](#spock-integration)

Spring Boot’s Spock integration has been removed as Spock does not yet support Groovy 5.

### Module Dependencies

[](#module-dependencies)

Spring Boot 4.0 has [a new modular design](https://spring.io/blog/2025/10/28/modularizing-spring-boot/) and now ships smaller focused modules rather than several large jars. As a result, this release has a more consistent set of “starter” POMs, and features that only relied on a third-party dependency to work can require an additional starter.

You will need to make dependency modifications if your current application doesn’t use Spring Boot “starter” POMs.

#### Main Code

[](#main-code)

The new modules and “starter” POMs follow a convention that lets you identify where the support for a given technology comes from:

- All Spring Boot modules are named `spring-boot-<technology>`.
- The root package of each module is `org.springframework.boot.<technology>`.
- All “starter” POMs are named `spring-boot-starter-<technology>`.

To illustrate the above, support for GraphQL is in `spring-boot-graphql` with a root package of `org.springframework.boot.graphql`. The “starter” POM is `spring-boot-starter-graphql`.

| Note | Review the list of “starter” POMs below based on the technologies that you are using and review your dependencies. You may face issue if you use a technology that previously had no “starter” POM.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />For instance, if you are using Flyway or Liquibase you used to only have the relevant third-party dependency. You now need to replace that with `spring-boot-starter-flyway` or `spring-boot-starter-liquibase`, respectively. |
|------|-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|

#### Test Code

[](#test-code)

The modularity also applies to the test infrastructure. A similar convention is applied:

- All Spring Boot test modules are named `spring-boot-<technology>-test`.
- The root package of each such module is `org.springframework.boot.<technology>.test`.
- All test “starter” POMs are named `spring-boot-starter-<technology>-test`.

To illustrate the above, test infrastructure for GraphQL is in `spring-boot-graphql-test` with a root package of `org.springframework.boot.graphql.test`. The “starter” POM is `spring-boot-starter-graphql-test`.

| Note | If you are using a technology that defines its own test infrastructure, you should swap it to the `spring-boot-starter-<technology>-test` equivalent. In the example above, `spring-boot-graphql-starter-test` has a dependency on `org.springframework.graphql:spring-graphql-test`.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />Not doing so could lead to issues that are hard to track. For example, `@WithMockUser` and `@WithUserDetails` from `spring-security-test` now requires `spring-boot-starter-security-test` to operate properly. |
|------|------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|

| Tip | Given that all test “starter” POMs bring `spring-boot-starter-test` transitively, you don’t need to define this starter anymore. Rather, you should list the starters of the technologies that are under test for the module. |
|-----|-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|

#### Starters

[](#starters)

This release harmonizes the use of starters in two ways:

- Most technologies covered by Spring Boot have a dedicated starter.
- Each starter has a test starter companion.

- ruleID: jackson-import-00010
  description: Jackson 3 uses tools.jackson package namespace; com.fasterxml.jackson is replaced
  category: mandatory
  effort: 5
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot3
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot4
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    Spring Boot 4.0 uses Jackson 3 as its preferred JSON library. Jackson 3 uses new group IDs and package names with `com.fasterxml.jackson` becoming `tools.jackson`.

    An exception is `jackson-annotations` which continues to use the `com.fasterxml.jackson.core` group ID and `com.fasterxml.jackson.annotation` package.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import com.fasterxml.jackson.databind.ObjectMapper;
    import com.fasterxml.jackson.core.JsonProcessingException;
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import tools.jackson.databind.ObjectMapper;
    import tools.jackson.core.JsonProcessingException;
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - The `jackson-annotations` module continues to use `com.fasterxml.jackson.annotation` package
    - For libraries that require Jackson 2, dependency management for Jackson 2 remains
    - A Jackson 2 ObjectMapper can be used alongside Boot's auto-configuration for Jackson 3
    - Refer to the Jackson 3 wiki for details: https://github.com/FasterXML/jackson/wiki/Jackson-Release-3.0
  links:
    - url: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#upgrading-jackson
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: com.fasterxml.jackson*
        location: PACKAGE

    The `Jackson2ObjectMapperBuilderCustomizer` interface has been renamed to `JsonMapperBuilderCustomizer` in Spring Boot 4.0 for consistency with Jackson 3.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.springframework.boot.autoconfigure.jackson.Jackson2ObjectMapperBuilderCustomizer;

    @Bean
    public Jackson2ObjectMapperBuilderCustomizer customizer() {
        return builder -> builder.featuresToEnable(SerializationFeature.INDENT_OUTPUT);
    }
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import org.springframework.boot.autoconfigure.jackson.JsonMapperBuilderCustomizer;

    @Bean
    public JsonMapperBuilderCustomizer customizer() {
        return builder -> builder.featuresToEnable(SerializationFeature.INDENT_OUTPUT);
    }
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - This is a class rename — update the type reference and import statement
    - Some `JsonParser.Feature` properties have also been renamed (see `spring.jackson.json.read`)
    - Part of the broader Jackson 3 migration in Spring Boot 4.0

    - Supporting classes have also been renamed replacing `Json` with `Jackson`

- ruleID: kafka-import-00010
  description: StreamBuilderFactoryBeanCustomizer removed; use Spring Kafka's StreamsBuilderFactoryBeanConfigurer
  category: mandatory
  effort: 5
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot3
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot4
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    Spring Boot's `StreamBuilderFactoryBeanCustomizer` has been removed in favor of Spring Kafka's `StreamsBuilderFactoryBeanConfigurer`. When migrating to the new configurer, be aware that it implements `Ordered` with a default value of `0`.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.springframework.boot.autoconfigure.kafka.StreamBuilderFactoryBeanCustomizer;

    @Bean
    public StreamBuilderFactoryBeanCustomizer customizer() {
        return fb -> fb.setAutoStartup(false);
    }
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import org.springframework.kafka.config.StreamsBuilderFactoryBeanConfigurer;

    @Bean
    public StreamsBuilderFactoryBeanConfigurer configurer() {
        return fb -> fb.setAutoStartup(false);
    }
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - `StreamsBuilderFactoryBeanConfigurer` implements `Ordered` with a default value of `0`, which may affect ordering if you have multiple configurers
    - The new configurer is provided by Spring Kafka directly, not Spring Boot autoconfigure
    - Ensure your Spring Kafka dependency is up to date to have `StreamsBuilderFactoryBeanConfigurer` available
    - See the [Spring Boot 4.0 Migration Guide](https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#kafka-streams-customization) for details
  links:
    - url: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#kafka-streams-customization
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: org.springframework.boot.autoconfigure.kafka.StreamBuilderFactoryBeanCustomizer
        location: IMPORT
- ruleID: kafka-pattern-00010
  description: spring.kafka.retry.topic.backoff.random removed; use spring.kafka.retry.topic.backoff.jitter
  category: mandatory
  effort: 1
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot3
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot4
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    The `spring.kafka.retry.topic.backoff.random` property has been removed in Spring Boot 4.0. Spring Kafka has moved its retry capabilities from Spring Retry to Spring Framework's core retry support.

    ### Migration Steps
    1. Replace `spring.kafka.retry.topic.backoff.random` with `spring.kafka.retry.topic.backoff.jitter` in your application configuration
    2. The `jitter` property provides more flexibility over the former `random` property
    3. Review the [Spring Boot 4.0 documentation](https://docs.spring.io/spring-boot/4.0-SNAPSHOT/appendix/application-properties/index.html#application-properties.integration.spring.kafka.retry.topic.backoff.jitter) for the new jitter configuration options

    ### Additional Info
    - Spring Kafka retry has moved from Spring Retry to Spring Framework's core retry support
    - The `jitter` property provides more control than the boolean `random` property
    - Check for any other Spring Retry-based configurations that may also need updating
    - See the [Spring Framework retry documentation](https://docs.spring.io/spring-framework/docs/7.0.x-SNAPSHOT/javadoc-api/org/springframework/core/retry/package-summary.html) for the new retry API
  links:
    - url: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#spring-kafka-retry-features
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    builtin.filecontent:
        pattern: spring\.kafka\.retry\.topic\.backoff\.random
        filePattern: application.*\.(properties|ya?ml)

output/spring-boot3-to-spring-boot4-20260624-085756/rules/messaging.yaml
- ruleID: messaging-dependency-00010
  description: Reactive Pulsar support removed in Spring Boot 4
  category: mandatory
  effort: 7
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot3
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot4
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    Following the decision to remove reactor support in Spring Pulsar, Spring Boot no longer manages the reactive Pulsar client. Auto-configuration for Spring Pulsar Reactive has been removed.

    ### Migration Steps
    1. Remove `spring-boot-starter-pulsar-reactive` from your dependencies.
    2. Replace reactive Pulsar usage with the non-reactive `spring-boot-starter-pulsar`.
    3. Refactor any reactive Pulsar client code to use the imperative Spring Pulsar API.

    ### Additional Info
    - The non-reactive `spring-boot-starter-pulsar` remains fully supported.
    - Review [Spring for Apache Pulsar 2.0](https://docs.spring.io/spring-pulsar/reference/whats-new.html) for the latest changes.
    - See the [migration guide](https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#pulsar-reactive).
  links:
    - url: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#pulsar-reactive
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.dependency:
        name: org.springframework.boot.spring-boot-starter-pulsar-reactive
        lowerbound: 0.0.0

    ### Migration Steps
    1. Review the Hazelcast team's Spring Session Hazelcast module for compatibility with Spring Boot 4.

- ruleID: testing-dependency-00010
  description: Spock integration removed in Spring Boot 4; Spock does not yet support Groovy 5
  category: mandatory
  effort: 7
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot3
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot4
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    Spring Boot's Spock integration has been removed because Spock does not yet support Groovy 5, which is required by Spring Boot 4.

    ### Migration Steps
    1. Remove `spock-spring` and related Spock dependencies from your project.
    2. Migrate your Spock tests to JUnit 5 or wait for Spock to support Groovy 5.
    3. If you must keep Spock tests, they cannot run under Spring Boot 4 until Spock adds Groovy 5 support.

    ### Additional Info
    - Spock's Groovy 5 support is tracked by the Spock team.
    - JUnit 5 provides similar features like data-driven tests via `@ParameterizedTest`.
    - See the [migration guide](https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#spock-integration).

      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.dependency:
        name: org.spockframework.spock-spring
        lowerbound: 0.0.0
- ruleID: testing-dependency-00020
  description: spring-security-test now requires spring-boot-starter-security-test for @WithMockUser and @WithUserDetails
  category: mandatory
  effort: 3
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot3
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot4
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    In Spring Boot 4, `@WithMockUser` and `@WithUserDetails` from `spring-security-test` now require `spring-boot-starter-security-test` to operate properly. Without the starter, these test annotations may not work as expected.

    ### Before
    ```xml
    <dependency>
        <groupId>org.springframework.security</groupId>
        <artifactId>spring-security-test</artifactId>
        <scope>test</scope>
    </dependency>
    ```

    ### After
    ```xml
    <dependency>
        <groupId>org.springframework.boot</groupId>
        <artifactId>spring-boot-starter-security-test</artifactId>
        <scope>test</scope>
    </dependency>
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - The `spring-boot-starter-security-test` pulls in `spring-security-test` transitively.
    - All test starter POMs bring `spring-boot-starter-test` transitively, so you may remove that explicit dependency.
    - This is part of Spring Boot 4's modularization of test infrastructure.
    - See the [migration guide](https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#test-code).
  links:
    - url: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#test-code
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.dependency:
        name: org.springframework.security.spring-security-test
        lowerbound: 0.0.0
- ruleID: testing-import-00010
  description: MockitoTestExecutionListener removed; use MockitoExtension from Mockito
  category: mandatory
  effort: 3
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot3
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot4
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    The `MockitoTestExecutionListener` deprecated in Spring Boot 3.4 has been removed. This listener was often indirectly used, so deprecation warnings were easy to miss. If your `@Mock` or `@Captor` annotated fields aren't working as expected after upgrade, use `MockitoExtension` from Mockito itself.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.springframework.boot.test.mock.mockito.MockitoTestExecutionListener;
    import org.springframework.test.context.TestExecutionListeners;

    @TestExecutionListeners(MockitoTestExecutionListener.class)
    public class MyTest {
        @Mock
        private MyService myService;
    }
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import org.junit.jupiter.api.extension.ExtendWith;
    import org.mockito.junit.jupiter.MockitoExtension;

    @ExtendWith(MockitoExtension.class)
    public class MyTest {
        @Mock
        private MyService myService;
    }
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - The `MockitoTestExecutionListener` was deprecated in Spring Boot 3.4 and removed in 4.0
    - Since the listener was typically used indirectly (auto-discovered via `spring.factories`), you may not have explicit references to it
    - `@Mock` and `@Captor` annotations from Mockito still work, but now require explicit `@ExtendWith(MockitoExtension.class)` on the test class
    - If you don't have explicit references to `MockitoTestExecutionListener`, check your test base classes for `@TestExecutionListeners` annotations
    - See the [Spring Boot 4.0 Migration Guide](https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#mockito-captor-and-mock-annotations) for details
  links:
    - url: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#mockito-captor-and-mock-annotations
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: org.springframework.boot.test.mock.mockito.MockitoTestExecutionListener
        location: IMPORT
- ruleID: testing-import-00020
  description: '@SpringBootTest no longer auto-configures MockMvc; add @AutoConfigureMockMvc'
  category: potential
  effort: 3
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot3
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot4
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    Using the `@SpringBootTest` annotation will no longer provide any MockMVC support in Spring Boot 4.0. If you use MockMVC in tests annotated with `@SpringBootTest`, you must now explicitly add an `@AutoConfigureMockMvc` annotation to the test class.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.springframework.boot.test.context.SpringBootTest;
    import org.springframework.test.web.servlet.MockMvc;
    import org.springframework.beans.factory.annotation.Autowired;

    @SpringBootTest
    public class MyControllerTest {
        @Autowired
        private MockMvc mockMvc;
    }
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import org.springframework.boot.test.context.SpringBootTest;
    import org.springframework.boot.test.autoconfigure.web.servlet.AutoConfigureMockMvc;
    import org.springframework.test.web.servlet.MockMvc;
    import org.springframework.beans.factory.annotation.Autowired;

    @SpringBootTest
    @AutoConfigureMockMvc
    public class MyControllerTest {
        @Autowired
        private MockMvc mockMvc;
    }
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - Tests using `@WebMvcTest` are not affected by this change, as MockMvc is still auto-configured there
    - This only affects tests that use `@SpringBootTest` in combination with MockMvc
    - Simply adding `@AutoConfigureMockMvc` to the test class restores the previous behavior
    - See the [Spring Boot 4.0 Migration Guide](https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#using-mockmvc-and-springboottest) for details
  links:
    - url: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#using-mockmvc-and-springboottest
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: org.springframework.test.web.servlet.MockMvc
        location: IMPORT

  category: mandatory
  effort: 3
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot3

- ruleID: web-server-dependency-00010
  description: Undertow support removed in Spring Boot 4; not compatible with Servlet 6.1
  category: mandatory
  effort: 7
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot3
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot4
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    Undertow support has been removed from Spring Boot 4 because Undertow is not yet compatible with the Servlet 6.1 baseline required by Spring Boot 4.

    ### Migration Steps
    1. Remove `spring-boot-starter-undertow` from your dependencies.
    2. Add `spring-boot-starter-tomcat` or `spring-boot-starter-jetty` as your embedded server.
    3. Review any Undertow-specific configuration properties and migrate them to the equivalent Tomcat/Jetty properties.
    4. Do not deploy Spring Boot 4.0 applications to a non-Servlet 6.1 compliant container.

    ### Additional Info
    - Tomcat is the default embedded server and requires no explicit starter dependency if using `spring-boot-starter-webmvc`.
    - Jetty is an alternative if you prefer it over Tomcat.
    - Any Undertow-specific tuning (worker threads, buffer sizes, etc.) needs to be translated to Tomcat/Jetty equivalents.
    - See the [migration guide](https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#undertow).
  links:
    - url: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#undertow
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.dependency:
        name: org.springframework.boot.spring-boot-starter-undertow
        lowerbound: 0.0.0

    ```xml
    </dependency>
    ```

    ```xml
    </dependency>
    ```

    - The test companion is `spring-boot-starter-webmvc-test`.
    - `spring-boot-starter-webmvc` is functionally equivalent to the old `spring-boot-starter-web`.

- ruleID: web-import-00010
  description: PathRequest.toStaticResources() now includes /fonts/** location by default
  category: potential
  effort: 1
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot3
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot4
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    In Spring Boot 4, a new `/fonts/**` location has been added to the common static resource locations returned by `PathRequest.toStaticResources()`. If you use `PathRequest.toStaticResources().atCommonLocations()`, the `/fonts/**` path will have the same security settings as your other static resource locations.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.springframework.boot.autoconfigure.security.servlet.PathRequest;

    // /fonts/** was not included in static resource locations
    http.authorizeHttpRequests(auth -> auth
        .requestMatchers(PathRequest.toStaticResources().atCommonLocations()).permitAll()
    );
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import org.springframework.boot.autoconfigure.security.servlet.PathRequest;
    import org.springframework.boot.autoconfigure.web.servlet.StaticResourceLocation;

    // If you don't want /fonts/** included, exclude it:
    http.authorizeHttpRequests(auth -> auth
        .requestMatchers(PathRequest.toStaticResources().atCommonLocations()
            .excluding(StaticResourceLocation.FONTS)).permitAll()
    );
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - If you are comfortable with `/fonts/**` having the same security settings as other static resources, no action is needed
    - Only affects applications using `PathRequest.toStaticResources().atCommonLocations()` for security configuration
    - See the [migration guide](https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#fonts-added-to-common-static-locations)
  links:
    - url: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#fonts-added-to-common-static-locations
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: org.springframework.boot.autoconfigure.security.servlet.PathRequest
        location: IMPORT
- ruleID: web-import-00020
  description: HttpMessageConverters deprecated; use ClientHttpMessageConvertersCustomizer or ServerHttpMessageConvertersCustomizer
  category: optional
  effort: 5
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot3
    - konveyor.io/source=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot4
    - konveyor.io/target=spring-boot
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    Spring Boot's `HttpMessageConverters` has been deprecated because Spring Framework improved the converter configuration. The type conflated client and server converters. The class has moved to `org.springframework.boot.http.converter.autoconfigure.HttpMessageConverters`.

    If your application declares a custom `HttpMessageConverters` bean, the bean is still supported but the type itself is deprecated. If you are contributing `HttpMessageConverter` beans to the context (like a `JacksonJsonHttpMessageConverter`), this is no longer supported.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.springframework.boot.autoconfigure.http.HttpMessageConverters;

    @Bean
    public HttpMessageConverters customConverters() {
        return new HttpMessageConverters(new MyCustomConverter());
    }
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import org.springframework.boot.http.converter.autoconfigure.ClientHttpMessageConvertersCustomizer;
    import org.springframework.boot.http.converter.autoconfigure.ServerHttpMessageConvertersCustomizer;

    @Bean
    public ServerHttpMessageConvertersCustomizer serverConverterCustomizer() {
        return customizer -> customizer.addCustomConverter(new MyCustomConverter());
    }
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - `ClientHttpMessageConvertersCustomizer` lets you customize converters for HTTP clients (RestTemplate, WebClient)
    - `ServerHttpMessageConvertersCustomizer` lets you customize converters for the server (Spring MVC)
    - Each customizer can contribute converters as "custom" converters or replace default converters
    - Contributing `HttpMessageConverter` beans directly to the context is no longer supported
    - See the [reference documentation](https://docs.spring.io/spring-boot/4.0-SNAPSHOT/reference/web/servlet.html#web.servlet.spring-mvc.message-converters)
  links:
    - url: https://github.com/spring-projects/spring-boot/wiki/Spring-Boot-4.0-Migration-Guide#httpmessageconverters-deprecation
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: org.springframework.boot.autoconfigure.http.HttpMessageConverters
        location: IMPORT

case-003-log4j1-to-log4j2 (7/7 pass)
JudgeValueRationale
budget_checkPASS

Cost $9.84 within budget $35.00

extraction_completeness4

The extraction is very thorough, covering the vast majority of migration artifacts from the guide. All 7 type migrations from Table 2 (MDC→ThreadContext, NDC→ThreadContext, Priority→Level, Level→Level, Category→Logger, Logger→Logger, LogManager→LogManager) are captured. All 3 method migrations from Table 3 (Logger.getLogger→LogManager.getLogger, Logger.getRootLogger→LogManager.getRootLogger, Category.getEffectiveLevel→Logger.getLevel) are present. The special methods from Table 4 (Logger.getLogger with LoggerFactory, LogManager.shutdown, setLevel) are covered. All 5 dependency replacements from Table 5 are captured, plus the log4j-over-slf4j incompatibility. All 11 appender mappings from Table 6 are present. All layout conversions are covered. The filters (DenyAllFilter, LevelMatchFilter, LevelRangeFilter, StringMatchFilter) are captured. PropertyConfigurator and DOMConfigurator are included. The interpolation ${foo}→${sys:foo} change is captured. The log4j.configuration property is covered. Minor omissions: (1) The org.apache.log4j.Level→org.apache.logging.log4j.Level type mapping from Table 2 lacks its own dedicated import-level pattern (it's partially covered by the package-level rule). (2) The org.apache.log4j.LogManager→org.apache.logging.log4j.LogManager import migration doesn't have its own dedicated rule. (3) The pattern converter compatibility table (%p→%v1Level, %x→%ndc, %X→%properties) is mentioned in messages but not extracted as separate rules. (4) The rolling file specifics (fileIndex='min' for DefaultRolloverStrategy, filePattern details from Table 7) are in messages but not separate patterns. (5) The parameterized logging best practice (is*Enabled guards removal) is mentioned in a message but not a standalone rule. (6) The log4j1.compatibility configuration property isn't a standalone detection rule. These are relatively minor gaps since most are mentioned within existing rule messages.

patterns_qualityPASS

44 patterns extracted with all required fields

report_existsPASS

report.yaml valid: 44 rules, 0% pass rate

rule_correctness4

Rules are well-constructed overall with accurate source-side when conditions, real Log4j 1 classes/methods (verified against artifacts), comprehensive before/after code examples, and specific documentation URLs. Category and effort values are reasonable. Minor issues include: (1) configuration-pattern-00010/00020 use overly broad filePattern '.*' risking false positives, (2) the interpolation regex lost its negative lookahead due to Go regex limitations creating potential false positives on already-migrated syntax, and (3) minor URL inconsistencies between rules. The 0% test pass rate is entirely due to a JAVA_HOME environment issue, not rule defects. The source verification confirmed 18 of 18 Java-based patterns exist in log4j-1.2.17.jar.

output/log4j1-to-log4j2-20260624-085825/tests/data/api-1/src/main/java/com/example/Application.java
package com.example;

// Rule: api-import-00010
// (PACKAGE-level match on org.apache.log4j)
import org.apache.log4j.Logger;
import org.apache.log4j.LogManager;

// Rule: api-import-00020
import org.apache.log4j.MDC;

// Rule: api-import-00030
import org.apache.log4j.NDC;

// Rule: api-import-00040
import org.apache.log4j.Priority;

// Rule: api-import-00050
import org.apache.log4j.Category;

import org.apache.log4j.Level;

public class Application {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        // Rule: api-method-00010
        Logger logger = Logger.getLogger(Application.class);

        // Rule: api-method-00020
        Logger rootLogger = Logger.getRootLogger();

        // Rule: api-import-00020
        MDC.put("userId", "user1");

        // Rule: api-import-00030
        NDC.push("context");

        // Rule: api-import-00040
        Priority priority = Priority.WARN;

        // Rule: api-import-00050
        Category cat = Category.getInstance(Application.class);

        // Rule: api-method-00030
        Level level = cat.getEffectiveLevel();

        logger.info("Test message");
    }
}
