- ruleID: api-import-00010
  description: Log4j 1 org.apache.log4j package replaced by org.apache.logging.log4j in Log4j 2
  category: mandatory
  effort: 5
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=log4j1
    - konveyor.io/source=log4j
    - konveyor.io/target=log4j2
    - konveyor.io/target=log4j
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    Log4j 1 uses the `org.apache.log4j` package namespace, which has been completely replaced by `org.apache.logging.log4j` in Log4j 2. All imports from `org.apache.log4j` must be updated.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.apache.log4j.Logger;
    import org.apache.log4j.LogManager;
    import org.apache.log4j.Level;
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import org.apache.logging.log4j.Logger;
    import org.apache.logging.log4j.LogManager;
    import org.apache.logging.log4j.Level;
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - Log4j 2 was rewritten from scratch with a new package namespace
    - Some classes were renamed during the migration (MDC, NDC, Priority, Category) — see related rules
    - Log4j 2 features a logging API independent of its reference implementation
    - The `is*Enabled()` guards are no longer necessary with Log4j 2's parameterized logging: use `LOGGER.info("Hello {}!", username)` instead of string concatenation
    - See https://logging.apache.org/log4j/2.x/migrate-from-log4j1.html
  links:
    - url: https://logging.apache.org/log4j/2.x/migrate-from-log4j1.html#api-code-migration
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: org.apache.log4j
        location: PACKAGE
- ruleID: api-import-00020
  description: Log4j 1 MDC replaced by ThreadContext in Log4j 2
  category: mandatory
  effort: 3
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=log4j1
    - konveyor.io/source=log4j
    - konveyor.io/target=log4j2
    - konveyor.io/target=log4j
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    The `org.apache.log4j.MDC` class has been replaced by `org.apache.logging.log4j.ThreadContext` in Log4j 2. The MDC (Mapped Diagnostic Context) functionality is now provided through the ThreadContext class.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.apache.log4j.MDC;

    MDC.put("userId", userId);
    String value = (String) MDC.get("userId");
    MDC.remove("userId");
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import org.apache.logging.log4j.ThreadContext;

    ThreadContext.put("userId", userId);
    String value = ThreadContext.get("userId");
    ThreadContext.remove("userId");
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - ThreadContext combines both MDC and NDC functionality from Log4j 1
    - `ThreadContext.put()` and `ThreadContext.get()` replace `MDC.put()` and `MDC.get()`
    - ThreadContext values are strings; Log4j 1 MDC accepted Object values
    - See https://logging.apache.org/log4j/2.x/migrate-from-log4j1.html#api-code-migration
  links:
    - url: https://logging.apache.org/log4j/2.x/migrate-from-log4j1.html#api-code-migration
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: org.apache.log4j.MDC
        location: IMPORT
- ruleID: api-import-00030
  description: Log4j 1 NDC replaced by ThreadContext in Log4j 2
  category: mandatory
  effort: 3
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=log4j1
    - konveyor.io/source=log4j
    - konveyor.io/target=log4j2
    - konveyor.io/target=log4j
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    The `org.apache.log4j.NDC` class has been replaced by `org.apache.logging.log4j.ThreadContext` in Log4j 2. The NDC (Nested Diagnostic Context) functionality is now provided through ThreadContext's stack methods.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.apache.log4j.NDC;

    NDC.push("context");
    NDC.pop();
    NDC.clear();
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import org.apache.logging.log4j.ThreadContext;

    ThreadContext.push("context");
    ThreadContext.pop();
    ThreadContext.clearStack();
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - ThreadContext combines both MDC (map) and NDC (stack) functionality
    - `NDC.push()` becomes `ThreadContext.push()`, `NDC.pop()` becomes `ThreadContext.pop()`
    - `NDC.clear()` becomes `ThreadContext.clearStack()`
    - See https://logging.apache.org/log4j/2.x/migrate-from-log4j1.html#api-code-migration
  links:
    - url: https://logging.apache.org/log4j/2.x/migrate-from-log4j1.html#api-code-migration
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: org.apache.log4j.NDC
        location: IMPORT
- ruleID: api-import-00040
  description: Log4j 1 Priority class replaced by Level in Log4j 2
  category: mandatory
  effort: 1
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=log4j1
    - konveyor.io/source=log4j
    - konveyor.io/target=log4j2
    - konveyor.io/target=log4j
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    The `org.apache.log4j.Priority` class has been replaced by `org.apache.logging.log4j.Level` in Log4j 2. Priority was the parent class of Level in Log4j 1 and is no longer needed.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.apache.log4j.Priority;

    if (logger.isEnabledFor(Priority.WARN)) {
        logger.log(Priority.WARN, "Warning message");
    }
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import org.apache.logging.log4j.Level;

    if (logger.isEnabled(Level.WARN)) {
        logger.warn("Warning message");
    }
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - Priority was deprecated even in Log4j 1 in favor of Level
    - All priority constants (DEBUG, INFO, WARN, ERROR, FATAL) are available as Level constants in Log4j 2
    - See https://logging.apache.org/log4j/2.x/migrate-from-log4j1.html#api-code-migration
  links:
    - url: https://logging.apache.org/log4j/2.x/migrate-from-log4j1.html#api-code-migration
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: org.apache.log4j.Priority
        location: IMPORT
- ruleID: api-import-00050
  description: Log4j 1 Category class replaced by Logger in Log4j 2
  category: mandatory
  effort: 3
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=log4j1
    - konveyor.io/source=log4j
    - konveyor.io/target=log4j2
    - konveyor.io/target=log4j
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    The `org.apache.log4j.Category` class has been replaced by `org.apache.logging.log4j.Logger` in Log4j 2. Category was the parent class of Logger in Log4j 1 and is no longer needed as a separate class.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.apache.log4j.Category;

    Category cat = Category.getInstance(MyClass.class);
    cat.info("Information message");
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import org.apache.logging.log4j.Logger;
    import org.apache.logging.log4j.LogManager;

    Logger logger = LogManager.getLogger(MyClass.class);
    logger.info("Information message");
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - Category was the base class for Logger in Log4j 1; in Log4j 2, use Logger directly

- ruleID: configuration-pattern-00010
  description: Log4j 1 configuration file must be converted to Log4j 2 format
  category: mandatory
  effort: 7
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=log4j1
    - konveyor.io/source=log4j
    - konveyor.io/target=log4j2
    - konveyor.io/target=log4j
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    Log4j 1 uses `log4j.properties` for configuration, but Log4j 2 uses a different configuration format (`log4j2.xml`, `log4j2.yaml`, or `log4j2.json`).

    ### Migration Steps

    1. Use the `Log4j1ConfigurationConverter` utility from the `log4j-1.2-api` bridge to convert automatically:
       ```shell
       java org.apache.log4j.config.Log4j1ConfigurationConverter --in log4j.properties --out log4j2.xml
       ```
    2. Alternatively, manually rewrite the configuration in Log4j 2 XML format.
    3. If immediate conversion is not possible, use the Log4j 1 to Log4j 2 bridge with `log4j1.compatibility=true`.

    ### Additional Info

    - Download `log4j-api`, `log4j-core`, and `log4j-1.2-api` artifacts to use the converter
    - The converter handles most standard Log4j 1 configuration options
    - Log4j 2 configuration is more flexible and supports XML, YAML, JSON, and properties formats
    - See https://logging.apache.org/log4j/2.x/manual/migration.html#Log4j2ConfigurationFormat
  links:
    - url: https://logging.apache.org/log4j/2.x/manual/migration.html#Log4j2ConfigurationFormat
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    builtin.filecontent:
        pattern: log4j\.properties
        filePattern: .*

    ### Migration Steps

    1. Manually rewrite the configuration in Log4j 2 XML format (`log4j2.xml`).
    2. If immediate conversion is not possible, use the Log4j 1 to Log4j 2 bridge with `log4j1.compatibility=true` to enable runtime conversion of Log4j 1 config files.

    ### Additional Info

    - The `Log4j1ConfigurationConverter` utility supports `.properties` files; for `.xml` configs, manual conversion may be needed
    - Log4j 2 configuration supports XML, YAML, JSON, and properties formats
    - See https://logging.apache.org/log4j/2.x/manual/migration.html#Log4j2ConfigurationFormat
  links:

- ruleID: configuration-pattern-00030
  description: Log4j 1 interpolation syntax must be converted to Log4j 2 lookup syntax
  category: mandatory
  effort: 3
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=log4j1
    - konveyor.io/source=log4j
    - konveyor.io/target=log4j2
    - konveyor.io/target=log4j
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    Log4j 1 uses `${foo}` syntax for interpolation using system properties. Log4j 2 uses pluggable Lookups and requires the `sys:` prefix for system properties.

    ### Before

    ```properties
    log4j.appender.file.File=${logdir}/app.log
    ```

    ### After

    ```properties
    log4j.appender.file.File=${sys:logdir}/app.log
    ```

    ### Additional Info

    - Replace all `${foo}` with `${sys:foo}` in your Log4j configuration files
    - Log4j 2 supports other lookup prefixes: `env:` for environment variables, `jndi:` for JNDI, etc.
    - See https://logging.apache.org/log4j/2.x/manual/lookups.html
  links:
    - url: https://logging.apache.org/log4j/2.x/manual/migration.html#configuration-interpolation
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    builtin.filecontent:
        pattern: \$\{[a-zA-Z]
        filePattern: log4j.*\.(properties|xml)

- ruleID: dependencies-dependency-00010
  description: Log4j 1 log4j:log4j replaced by org.apache.logging.log4j:log4j-core
  category: mandatory
  effort: 5
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=log4j1
    - konveyor.io/source=log4j
    - konveyor.io/target=log4j2
    - konveyor.io/target=log4j
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    The `log4j:log4j` artifact (Log4j 1) has reached End of Life and must be replaced with `org.apache.logging.log4j:log4j-core` (Log4j 2). Vulnerabilities reported after August 2015 against Log4j 1 are not checked and will not be fixed.

    ### Migration Steps
    1. Remove the `log4j:log4j` dependency from your build file
    2. Add `org.apache.logging.log4j:log4j-core` as a replacement
    3. Add `org.apache.logging.log4j:log4j-api` as a compile dependency
    4. Update all code imports from `org.apache.log4j` to `org.apache.logging.log4j` (see API migration rules)
    5. Convert configuration files from Log4j 1 to Log4j 2 format

    ### Additional Info
    - Log4j 1 reached End of Life in 2015
    - If you cannot immediately migrate all code, consider using the `org.apache.logging.log4j:log4j-1.2-api` bridge as an interim solution
    - The bridge is incompatible with having `log4j:log4j` on the classpath — you must remove the old artifact first
    - See https://logging.apache.org/log4j/2.x/migrate-from-log4j1.html#backend-migration
  links:
    - url: https://logging.apache.org/log4j/2.x/migrate-from-log4j1.html#backend-migration
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.dependency:
        name: log4j.log4j
        lowerbound: 0.0.0

    - See https://logging.apache.org/log4j/2.x/migrate-from-log4j1.html#backend-migration

behavior\n56\t\n57\t## Permissions\n58\t\n59\t| Operation | Pattern | Purpose |\n60\t|-----------|---------|---------|\n61\t| shell | `mkdir -p output` | Create output directory |\n62\t| shell | `go already return.**\n81\tEvery `go run ./cmd/*` command returns structured JSON. Use that JSON output directly \u2014 do not pipe it through shell commands to extract fields.\n82\tThis is a Go project. Run only commands listed in this permissions table.\n83\tIf a required action is not permitted, stop and report the limitation.\n84\t\n85\t## UX Principles\n86\t\n87\t- Emit short status lines continuously (start + finish for each step).\n88\t- Only ask at checkpoint when `mode=interactive` and `checkpoint_behavior=ask`.\n89\t- Do not block after testing starts; continue even if some rules remain failing.\n90\t- Fix only failing rules, not the full suite.\n91\t\n92\tFor pipeline logging conventions, see `references/orchestrator-details.md` (Pipeline Transcript section).\n93\t\n94\tFor stage timing instructions, see `references/orchestrator-details.md` (Timing section).\n95\t\n96\tFor sub-agent invocation protocol and contract validation, see `references/orchestrator-details.md` (Sub-agent Protocol section).\n97\t\n98\t## Pipeline\n99\t\n100\t**Error handling:** If any CLI command (`ingest`, `construct`, `validate`, `scaffold`, `sanitize`, `test`, `report`) exits non-zero, print `[step] FAILED \u2014 <error>` and stop the pipeline. Do not proceed to the next step.\n101\t\n102\t**Partial failures:** If a step produces partial results before failing (e.g., `construct` succeeds for 48 patterns but fails on 2), preserve the partial output and report what succeeded. The user can fix the failing patterns and re-run. Do not discard valid results because of a partial failure.\n103\t\n104\t**Resume behavior:** When `resume_from` is set, the user must also provide `migration_dir` pointing to the specific timestamped directory to resume. Skip prior stages and validate prerequisites first. Fail fast when required artifacts are missing.\n105\t\n106\tStage prerequisites (paths relative to `<migration_dir>`):\n107\t- `extract` requires `guide.md`\n108\t- `coverage` requires `patterns.json`\n109\t- `scaffold` requires `rules/`\n110\t- `test` requires `rules/` and `tests/manifest.json`\n111\t- `report` requires source/target metadata plus pass/fail totals and rule ID lists\n112\t\n113\t### 1. Ingest\n114\t\n115\tGenerate a timestamp once at pipeline start (`YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS` in local time).\n116\t\n117\tDetermine the migration directory path:\n118\t- If the user provided `migration_dir`, use that (no timestamp)\n119\t- If the user provided `sources` and `targets` (or `source` and `target`), use `output/<primary_source>-to-<primary_target>-<YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS>` where `primary_source` is `sources[0]` and `primary_target` is `targets[0]`\n120\t- If auto-detecting: ingest to `output/guide-temp.md` first, read the first ~50 lines to detect source/target/language (lowercase, hyphenated names like `spring-boot-3`), then use `output/<source>-to-<target>-<YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS>`\n121\t\n122\t```bash\n123\tmkdir -p output/<source>-to-<target>-<YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS>\n124\t```\n125\t\n126\tEvery `go run` command should be a standalone invocation with fully-expanded arguments \u2014 substitute actual paths and flag values directly into each command. Do not use shell variable assignments (`VAR=...`) or compound `&&` chains, since these don't match the permissions table.\n127\t\n128\tThe log flags are: `--log <migration_dir>/pipeline.log --agent orchestrator --model <your_model_id>`. Append these literally to every CLI invocation.\n129\t\n130\t```\n131\t[ingest] Fetching guide from <source>...\n132\t```\n133\t\n134\t- **URL:** `go run ./cmd/ingest --log <migration_dir>/pipeline.log --agent orchestrator --model <your_model_id> --input <url> --output <migration_dir>/guide.md`\n135\t- **File (not markdown):** `go run ./cmd/ingest --log <migration_dir>/pipeline.log --agent orchestrator --model <your_model_id> --input <path> --output <migration_dir>/guide.md`\n136\t- **Pasted text or already markdown:** Write directly to `<migration_dir>/guide.md`\n137\t\n138\tIf auto-detecting, write `output/guide-temp.md` to `<migration_dir>/guide.md` using the Write tool after the migration directory path is determined.\n139\t\n140\t**Stub detection \u2014 follow sub-pages.** After ingesting each URL, check the output for stub characteristics. A page is a stub if it has fewer than 100 non-blank lines of content after `cmd/ingest` processing (`cmd/ingest` already strips `<nav>`, `<footer>`, and `<aside>` elements during HTML-to-markdown conversion, so no additional filtering is needed).\n141\t\n142\tIf a stub is detected:\n143\t\n144\t1. Read the ingested markdown and extract all links whose resolved URL shares the same base path as the original URL (same-origin sibling pages). Sibling links are those pointing to `*.html` files under the same directory path as the original URL. Exclude external links, anchor-only links (`#...`), and links to parent directories.\n145\t2. For each sibling link, resolve it to a full URL relative to the original URL's base path.\n146\t3. Ingest each sub-page with `cmd/ingest` into a separate file (`guide-part-<N>.md`).\n147\t4. Concatenate all parts (original + sub-pages) into the final `guide.md`, in the order the links appear in the stub page (document order).\n148\t5. If a sub-page fetch fails (404, timeout), log a warning (`[ingest] WARNING \u2014 failed to fetch <url>: <error>`) and skip that page. Do not abort the pipeline \u2014 partial content is better than none.\n149\t\n150\tThis ensures that documentation sites which split content across multiple pages are fully captured. Without this step, the pipeline will only see the stub and miss the bulk of the migration content.\n151\t\n152\tCount lines (`GUIDE_LINES`) and section headings. Print:\n153\t\n154\t```\n155\t[ingest] Done \u2014 <GUIDE_LINES> lines, <N> sections \u2192 <migration_dir>/ (<elapsed>)\n156\t```\n157\t\n158\t### 2. Extract (parallel)\n159\t\n160\tExtraction uses parallel agents to process the guide faster. The orchestrator splits the guide into chunks and spawns multiple rule-writer agents.\n161\t\n162\t**2a. Index sections and auto-detect metadata:**\n163\t\n164\t```bash\n165\tgo run ./cmd/sections <log_flags> --guide <migration_dir>/guide.md\n166\t```\n167\t\n168\tThis returns JSON with all sections classified as `content` or `header-only`. Filter to content sections only.\n169\t\n170\t```\n171\t[extract] Extracting patterns from <content_count> sections (<N> parallel agents)...\n172\t```\n173\t\n174\t**2b. Split into chunks and dispatch:**\n175\t\n176\tSplit the content sections into **N balanced chunks** (minimum 1, maximum 5 agents). Balance by section count. Assign each chunk a number (1, 2, ..., N).\n177\t\n178\t**Keep related sections together.** Group sections by their top-level heading (`##`) \u2014 all subsections (`###`, `####`) under the same `##` must stay in the same chunk. Migration guides pair before/after code examples across subsections within a topic; splitting them across agents means no agent sees both sides of the diff. Balance chunks by top-level-heading groups, not by individual sections.\n179\t\n180\t**Invoke:** `rule-writer` (one per chunk, in parallel)\n181\t**Purpose:** Extract migration patterns from assigned sections.\n182\t**Inputs per invocation:**\n183\t  - guide: <migration_dir>/guide.md\n184\t  - sources: {sources array (e.g., [\"spring-boot3\", \"spring-boot\"])}\n185\t  - targets: {targets array (e.g., [\"spring-boot4\", \"spring-boot\"])}\n186\t  - rules_dir: <migration_dir>/rules\n187\t  - sections: {chunk subset \u2014 list of `{heading, start_line, end_line}` objects}\n188\t  - all_headings: {full list of ALL content section headings from step 2a \u2014 not just this chunk's sections. Enables each agent to detect multi-path migrations even when variant sections are in other chunks.}\n189\t  - output_file: <migration_dir>/patterns-{chunk_number}.json\n190\t**Parallel:** yes\n191\t**Expect:**\n192\t  - patterns_count, output_file\n193\t\n194\t**2c. Merge, verify, and construct:**\n195\t\n196\tAfter all agents complete, merge the partial patterns files, verify source artifacts, and build rules:\n197\t\n198\t```bash\n199\tgo run ./cmd/merge-patterns <log_flags> --output <migration_dir>/patterns.json <migration_dir>/patterns-1.json <migration_dir>/patterns-2.json ...\n200\tgo run ./cmd/verify <log_flags> --patterns <migration_dir>/patterns.json --output <migration_dir>/verify-results.json --cache <migration_dir>/verify-cache\n201\tgo run ./cmd/construct <log_flags> --patterns <migration_dir>/patterns.json --output <migration_dir>/rules\n202\tgo run ./cmd/validate <log_flags> --rules <migration_dir>/rules\n203\t```\n204\t\n205\t**Verification step:** `cmd/verify` downloads source JARs from Maven Central and checks that each pattern's `source_fqn` exists in the declared `source_artifact`. This catches hallucinated class names before rules reach testing.\n206\t\n207\tThe verify stdout JSON contains `verified`, `not_found`, `skipped`, and `offline` counts. Print:\n208\t\n209\t```\n210\t[verify] <verified> verified, <not_found> not found, <skipped> skipped\n211\t```\n212\t\n213\tIf `not_found > 0`, read `<migration_dir>/verify-results.json` and note which `pattern_index` values have `status: \"not_found\"`. After construct runs, use the `pattern_rule_map` from construct's stdout JSON to map each `pattern_index` \u2192 `rule_id`. Carry `verified_rule_ids` and `not_found_rule_ids` forward to step 5 (report).\n214\t\n215\tIf validation fails, fix `<migration_dir>/patterns.json` (remove invalid entries) and re-run construct.\n216\t\n217\t```\n218\t[extract] Done \u2014 <patterns_count> patterns \u2192 <rules_count> rules in <migration_dir>/rules/ (<elapsed>)\n219\t```\n220\t\n221\tSave `source`, `target`, `patterns_count`, `rules_count`, and verify counts for the final summary.\n222\t\n223\t### 2d. Coverage Check\n224\t\n225\tRun the coverage tool to find sections with named artifacts that weren't extracted:\n226\t\n227\t```bash\n228\tgo run ./cmd/coverage <log_flags> --guide <migration_dir>/guide.md --patterns <migration_dir>/patterns.json --language <language>\n229\t```\n230\t\n231\tIf `gap_count > 0` in the JSON output, print:\n232\t\n233\t```\n234\t[coverage] <gap_count> sections with uncovered artifacts: <heading_1>, <heading_2>, ...\n235\t```\n236\t\n237\tConvert gaps to sections and send back to the rule-writer in chunk mode for targeted re-extraction. Each gap has `heading` and `line` \u2014 use the sections index to get the `start_line` and `end_line` for that heading. Mention the uncovered artifacts in the prompt so the sub-agent focuses on them.\n238\t\n239\t**Invoke:** `rule-writer` (chunk mode)\n240\t**Purpose:** Extract patterns from specific sections that the coverage check flagged.\n241\t**Inputs:**\n242\t  - guide: <migration_dir>/guide.md\n243\t  - sources: {sources array}\n244\t  - targets: {targets array}\n245\t  - rules_dir: <migration_dir>/rules\n246\t  - sections: {gap sections converted to `[{heading, start_line, end_line}]` format}\n247\t  - output_file: <migration_dir>/patterns-gaps.json\n248\t**Parallel:** no\n249\t**Expect:**\n250\t  - patterns_count, output_file\n251\t\n252\tThe sub-agent writes only the new patterns to `<migration_dir>/patterns-gaps.json`. It does NOT read or inspect existing patterns \u2014 the orchestrator handles deduplication. After the sub-agent returns, merge, verify, and rebuild:\n253\t\n254\t```bash\n255\tgo run ./cmd/merge-patterns <log_flags> --output <migration_dir>/patterns.json <migration_dir>/patterns.json <migration_dir>/patterns-gaps.json\n256\tgo run ./cmd/verify <log_flags> --patterns <migration_dir>/patterns.json --output <migration_dir>/verify-results.json --cache <migration_dir>/verify-cache\n257\tgo run ./cmd/construct <log_flags> --patterns <migration_dir>/patterns.json --output <migration_dir>/rules\n258\tgo run ./cmd/validate <log_flags> --rules <migration_dir>/rules\n259\t```\n260\t\n261\tRe-run the coverage check. If gaps remain, accept them \u2014 one re-extraction pass is enough.\n262\t\n263\t```\n264\t[coverage] Done \u2014 <final_gap_count> remaining gaps (accepted) (<elapsed>)\n265\t```\n266\t\n267\tIf `gap_count == 0`:\n268\t\n269\t```\n270\t[coverage] No gaps found (<elapsed>)\n271\t```\n272\t\n273\t### Checkpoint\n274\t\n275\tAfter extraction/coverage:\n276\t\n277\t- If `mode=non_interactive`, do **not** prompt:\n278\t  - `checkpoint_behavior=continue` or `ask`: continue automatically\n279\t  - `checkpoint_behavior=stop_after_extract`: skip testing and go to Step 5 (Report)\n280\t- If `mode=interactive`:\n281\t  - `checkpoint_behavior=continue`: continue automatically\n282\t  - `checkpoint_behavior=stop_after_extract`: skip testing and go to Step 5 (Report)\n283\t  - `checkpoint_behavior=ask`: ask:\n284\t    - `Continue with test generation and validation? (y/n)`\n285\t    - if no, skip to Step 5 (Report) with untested rules\n286\t\n287\t**Rules-only report:** When skipping to Step 5, invoke `cmd/report` with `--passed 0 --failed 0 --kantra-limitation 0` and empty `--passed-rules`, `--failed-rules`, `--kantra-limitation-rules` flags. Pass `--rules-total`, `--verified-rules`, and `--not-found-rules` from extraction. All rules get `test_status: untested`.\n288\t\n289\t### 3. Test Generation\n290\t\n291\t**3a. Scaffold (orchestrator runs this directly, not an agent):**\n292\t\n293\t```bash\n294\tgo run ./cmd/scaffold <log_flags> --rules <migration_dir>/rules --output <migration_dir>/tests --patterns <migration_dir>/patterns.json\n295\t```\n296\t\n297\tThis creates all directories, `.test.yaml` files, and `manifest.json`. No LLM needed.\n298\t\n299\t**3b. Read manifest and split into batches:**\n300\t\n301\tRead `<migration_dir>/tests/manifest.json`. It contains a `groups` array \u2014 each group has `name`, `data_dir`, `files` (paths to generate), and `rule_ids`.\n302\t\n303\tSplit the groups into **batches of ~5 groups each** (minimum 1 batch, maximum 5 batches), balanced by rule count.\n304\t\n305\t**3c. Spawn test-generator agents:**\n306\t\n307\t```\n308\t[test-gen] Generating test data for <rules_count> rules (<B> parallel agents)...\n309\t```\n310\t\n311\t**Invoke:** `test-generator` (one per batch, up to 5 in parallel)\n312\t**Purpose:** Generate compilable test source code that triggers the assigned rules.\n313\t**Inputs per invocation:**\n314\t  - rules_dir: <migration_dir>/rules\n315\t  - tests_dir: <migration_dir>/tests\n316\t  - groups: {batch subset from manifest.json \u2014 include name, data_dir, rule_ids, files}\n317\t**Parallel:** yes\n318\t**Expect:**\n319\t  - groups_completed, files_written\n320\t\n321\t**3d. Collect results and sanitize.** After all agents complete:\n322\t\n323\tCollect `suspected_kantra_limitations` from all rule-writer and test-generator agent returns (merge, deduplicate by `rule_id`). If non-empty, print:\n324\t\n325\t```\n326\t[test-gen] <N> suspected kantra limitations (Maven Central: no plain-semver version): <rule_id_1>, ...\n327\t```\n328\t\n329\tCarry this merged list forward as `pre_classified_kantra_limitations` \u2014 it will be passed to the rule-validator to skip the fix loop for these rules.\n330\t\n331\tSanitize XML:\n332\t\n333\t```bash\n334\tgo run ./cmd/sanitize <log_flags> --dir <migration_dir>/tests/data\n335\t```\n336\t\n337\t```\n338\t[test-gen] Done \u2014 <total_groups> groups, <total_files> files (<elapsed>)\n339\t```\n340\t\n341\t### 4. Validate (orchestrator-driven loop)\n342\t\n343\tThe orchestrator runs tests and uses a sub-agent for LLM-driven repairs on failures.\n344\t\n345\t**4a. Run tests:**\n346\t\n347\t```bash\n348\tgo run ./cmd/test <log_flags> --rules <migration_dir>/rules --tests <migration_dir>/tests --timeout 5m\n349\t```\n350\t\n351\tThe CLI runs each test file sequentially and automatically retries timed-out files once (`--retry-timeouts`, on by default). Tests run locally via `--run-local=true`. To run a subset, use `--files` with bare filenames (e.g., `--files data-1.test.yaml,data-2.test.yaml`), resolved relative to `--tests` dir.\n352\t\n353\tPrint the result:\n354\t\n355\t```\n356\t[validate] <total_passed>/<total_rules> passed (<elapsed>)\n357\t```\n358\t\n359\tOr if failures:\n360\t\n361\t```\n362\t[validate] <total_passed>/<total_rules> passed \u2014 <F> failures: <rule_id_1>, <rule_id_2>, ...\n363\t```\n364\t\n365\tIf all passed (elapsed shown above), skip to step 5.\n366\t\n367\t**4b. Fix (only if failures):**\n368\t\n369\t```\n370\t[fix] Fixing <F> failures: <rule_id_1>, <rule_id_2> ...\n371\t```\n372\t\n373\t**Invoke:** `rule-validator`\n374\t**Purpose:** Fix test data for failing rules so they pass kantra validation.\n375\t**Inputs:**\n376\t  - rules_dir: <migration_dir>/rules\n377\t  - tests_dir: <migration_dir>/tests\n378\t  - failing_rules: {list with rule_id, test_file, error for each failure}\n379\t  - pre_classified_kantra_limitations: {merged list from rule-writer and test-generator suspected_kantra_limitations \u2014 may be empty}\n380\t  - max_iterations: 1\n381\t**Parallel:** no\n382\t**Expect:**\n383\t  - fixed_rules, still_failing, kantra_limitation_rules, iterations_used, fix_details\n384\t  - results_by_rule (with `result_type` + `recommended_action`)\n385\t\n386\tThe validator agent owns the fix-verify loop \u2014 it fixes files, re-runs tests via `cmd/test`, and iterates up to `max_iterations`. Default is 1 iteration; pass up to 3 if the user requests more attempts.\n387\t\n388\t**The orchestrator must NOT run its own fix attempts.** Do not manually edit test files, create stub classes, toggle analysisParams, or retry. All fix work goes through the rule-validator sub-agent. When the validator returns `still_failing`, accept that result and move on.\n389\t\n390\tPrint the result:\n391\t\n392\t```\n393\t[fix] <fixed_count> fixed, <still_failing_count> still failing, <kantra_limitation_count> kantra limitations (<validate elapsed>)\n394\t```\n395\t\n396\tThe `<validate elapsed>` is the total time since the validate stage started (step 4a), including test runs and all fix iterations.\n397\t\n398\tIf `kantra_limitation_rules` is non-empty, print:\n399\t\n400\t```\n401\t[fix] kantra limitations (engine cannot test \u2014 rule is correct): <rule_id_1>, ...\n402\t```\n403\t\n404\tGroup unresolved failures by `result_type` in `results_by_rule` and include grouped counts in the final summary (e.g., `still_failing_timeout: 2`, `still_failing_kantra_limitation: 1`).\n405\t\n406\tIf still_failing is non-empty, move on \u2014 don't block the pipeline.\n407\t\n408\t### 5. Report\n409\t\n410\tCollate pass/fail results from the test run and the fix loop. Generate `report.yaml` with per-rule test and verification status. No labels are written to rule YAML files \u2014 all pipeline metadata lives in the report.\n411\t\n412\t```bash\n413\tgo run ./cmd/report <log_flags> --source <comma-separated sources> --target <comma-separated targets> --output <migration_dir>/report.yaml --rules-total <N> --passed <P> --failed <F> --kantra-limitation <K> --passed-rules <comma-separated passed rule IDs> --failed-rules <comma-separated failed rule IDs> --kantra-limitation-rules <comma-separated kantra limitation rule IDs> --verified-rules <comma-separated verified rule IDs> --not-found-rules <comma-separated not-found rule IDs>\n414\t```\n415\t\n416\tThe `--verified-rules` and `--not-found-rules` flags come from the verification mapping built in step 2c (pattern_index \u2192 rule_id via construct's pattern_rule_map).\n417\t\n418\tThe report includes a `rules` section with per-rule `test_status` (passed/failed/kantra-limitation/untested) and `source_verified` (true/false). The pass rate is computed as `passed / (passed + failed)` \u2014 kantra limitations are excluded since they are not failures, but also not confirmed passes.\n419\t\n420\t### 6. Summary\n421\t\n422\tPrint a formatted summary table using GitHub-flavored markdown:\n423\t\n424\t```markdown\n425\t## Summary\n426\t\n427\t| | |\n428\t|---|---|\n429\t| **Input** | <guide title or URL as a markdown link> |\n430\t| **Migration** | <primary_source> \u2192 <primary_target> (<language>) |\n431\t| **Guide** | <GUIDE_LINES> lines, <N> sections \u2192 <M> produced patterns, <K> skipped |\n432\t| **Rules** | <rules_count> generated, **<P>/<N> passed (<percent>%)** |\n433\t| **Verification** | <verified>/<total> source-verified, <not_found> not found, <skipped> skipped (omit row if all skipped) |\n434\t| **Kantra limitations** | <K> rules correct but not auto-testable \u2014 engine cannot compare non-semver versions (omit row if K=0) |\n435\t| **Fix iterations** | <iterations used, 0 if none> |\n436\t| **Timing** | total: <total elapsed> \u2014 ingest: <elapsed>, extract: <elapsed>, coverage: <elapsed>, test-gen: <elapsed>, validate: <elapsed>, report: <elapsed> |\n437\t| **Output** | `<migration_dir>/patterns.json` (patterns), `<migration_dir>/rules/` (rules), `<migration_dir>/tests/` (tests), `<migration_dir>/report.yaml` (report) |\n438\t\n439\t### Rule Categories\n440\t\n441\tUse the `groups` array from the `construct` JSON output \u2014 it lists each file and its rule count. Do not iterate rule files manually.\n442\t\n443\t| Group | Rules | Status |\n444\t|---|---|---|\n445\t| <group_name> (<brief description of what rules cover>) | <rule_count> | <passed>/<total> passed |\n446\t| ... | ... | ... |\n447\t```\n448\t\n449\tIf there are failures, add a row to the top-level table:\n450\t\n451\t```\n452\t| **Failed** | <rule_id_1>, <rule_id_2>, ... |\n453\t```\n454\t\n455\tIf coverage was low (< 30% of sections produced patterns), add a row:\n456\t\n457\t```\n458\t| **Warning** | Low extraction coverage (<M>/<K> sections) |\n459\t```\n460\t\n461\t**Rules-only summary (when `checkpoint_behavior=stop_after_extract`):**\n462\t\n463\tWhen testing was skipped, use this simplified table instead:\n464\t\n465\t```markdown\n466\t## Summary\n467\t\n468\t| | |\n469\t|---|---|\n470\t| **Input** | <guide title or URL as a markdown link> |\n471\t| **Migration** | <primary_source> \u2192 <primary_target> (<language>) |\n472\t| **Guide** | <GUIDE_LINES> lines, <N> sections \u2192 <M> produced patterns, <K> skipped |\n473\t| **Rules** | <rules_count> generated (untested) |\n474\t| **Verification** | <verified>/<total> source-verified, <not_found> not found, <skipped> skipped (omit row if all skipped) |\n475\t| **Timing** | total: <total elapsed> \u2014 ingest: <elapsed>, extract: <elapsed>, coverage: <elapsed>, report: <elapsed> |\n476\t| **Output** | `<migration_dir>/patterns.json` (patterns), `<migration_dir>/rules/` (rules), `<migration_dir>/report.yaml` (report) |\n477\t| **Next step** | Run `/generate-rules-with-test resume_from=scaffold migration_dir=<migration_dir>` to add tests |\n478\t```\n479\t\n480\tOmit these rows: **Kantra limitations**, **Fix iterations**, **Failed** (no testing ran).\n481\tOmit `tests/` from the **Output** row and test-gen/validate timing from the **Timing** row.\n482\tInclude the **Rule Categories** table as normal.\n483\t",

FORBIDDEN:\n9\t`python`, `python3`, `pip`, `pip3`, `node`, `npm`, `npx`, `ruby`, `perl`,\n10\t`bash -c`, `sh -c`, and any scripting runtime not explicitly listed.\n11\tDo not write or execute ad-hoc scripts in any language.\n12\tIf a task cannot be done with allowed tools, report the limitation.\n13\t\n14\t## Active Technologies\n15\t\n16\t- Go 1.25+ with stdlib `flag`, `gopkg.in/yaml.v3`, `github.com/JohannesKaufmann/html-to-markdown`, `golang.org/x/net`\n17\t\n18\t## Project Structure\n19\t\n20\t```text\n21\tcmd/                      # Extract API changes via japicmp or guide parsing\n37\t  feedback/               # Aggregate pipeline run trends and failure analysis\n38\t  compare/                # Compare rulesets side-by-side with optional app coverage\n39\tinternal/                 # Go library code (no LLM dependencies)\n40\tagents/                   # Agent skills (agentskills.io format)\n41\t  <skill>/SKILL.md        # Skill definition (inputs, returns, workflow)\n42\t  <skill>/contract.json   # Machine-readable input/return contract\n43\t  <skill>/references/     # Skill-specific reference docs\n44\tlanguages/<lang>/         # Per-language scaffold config (java, go, nodejs, csharp, python)\n45\t```\n46\t\n47\t## Skill Composition\n48\t\n49\t```text\n50\tgenerate-rules (orchestrator skill)\n51\t  \u251c\u2500\u2500 rule-writer        \u2014 extract patterns, produce rule YAML\n52\t  \u251c\u2500\u2500 test-generator     \u2014 generate test source code (parallel)\n53\t  \u2514\u2500\u2500 rule-validator     \u2014 fix failing tests, verify loop\n54\t```\n55\t\n56\tAll four are skills under `agents/`, each with `SKILL.md`, `contract.json`,\n57\tand `## Inputs` / `## Returns` sections defining their contract.\n58\t\n59\t## Sub-agent Dispatch\n60\t\n61\tWhen a skill says **\"Invoke: `<skill-name>`\"**, dispatch a new agent:\n62\t\n63\t1. Spawn an isolated agent using your runtime's agent dispatch tool.\n64\t2. Prompt: \"Read and follow `agents/<skill-name>/SKILL.md`.\" + the invoke inputs.\n65\t3. Wait for results.\n66\t\n67\t**The orchestrator must NOT execute the sub-skill's workflow itself.** Dispatch and wait.\n68\tThe orchestrator must NOT read files under `agents/<skill>/references/` \u2014 sub-agents\n69\tread their own references.\n70\tDo not pre-digest data or compose step-by-step instructions for the sub-agent.\n71\tIf `Parallel: yes`, dispatch concurrently when your runtime supports it.\n72\t\n73\t**Fallback:** If your runtime cannot dispatch sub-agents, read the SKILL.md and\n74\tfollow its workflow exactly as written \u2014 do not reinterpret or reimagine the steps.\n75\t\n76\t## CLI Commands\n77\t\n78\t```bash\n79\tgo run ./cmd/ingest    --input <url-or-file> --output output/<src>-to-<tgt>/guide.md\n80\tgo run ./cmd/sections  --guide agents/<skill>/contract.json --mode inputs|returns --payload-file payload.json\n85\tgo run ./cmd/scaffold  --rules output/<src>-to-<tgt>/rules/ --output output/<src>-to-<tgt>/tests/\n86\tgo run ./cmd/sanitize  --dir output/<src>-to-<tgt>/tests/data/\n87\tgo run ./cmd/test      --rules output/<src>-to-<tgt>/rules/ --tests output/<src>-to-<tgt>/tests/ [--files a.test.yaml,b.test.yaml] [--timeout 5m]\n88\tgo run ./cmd/report    --source <src> --target <tgt> --output output/<src>-to-<tgt>/report.yaml [--kantra-limitation N] [--kantra-limitation-rules id4,id5]\n89\tgo run ./cmd/coverage  --guide output/<src>-to-<tgt>/guide.md --patterns output/<src>-to-<tgt>/patterns.json [--language java]\n90\tgo run ./cmd/verify    --patterns output/<src>-to-<tgt>/patterns.json <model-id> --message \"<message>\"\n92\tgo run ./cmd/eval      --rules-dir output/<src>-to-<tgt>/rules/ [--app-dir <app>] [--ground-truth <ground_truth.yaml>] [--save] [--compare <baseline.json>]\n93\tgo run ./cmd/ground-truth --old-artifact <groupId:artifactId:version> --new-artifact <groupId:artifactId:version> [--output ground_truth.yaml]\n94\tgo run ./cmd/feedback <app>] [--out report.md]\n96\t\n97\tgo test ./internal/...   # Unit tests\n98\t```\n99\t\n100\t## Session Logging\n101\t\n102\tAll CLI commands support `--log`, `--agent`, and `--model` flags for pipeline logging with agent/model attribution. Pass `--log <path>` to append timestamped JSON output to a log file. Pass `--model <id>` when an LLM agent invokes the command (logs `[model=<id>]`). Omit `--model` only for manual human CLI usage (logs `[cli]`).\n103\t\n104\t```bash\n105\t# Orchestrator invocations (orchestrator is an LLM agent):\n106\tgo run ./cmd/ingest --log pipeline.log --agent orchestrator --model claude-opus-4-6 --input ... --output ...\n107\tgo run ./cmd/test   --log pipeline.log --agent orchestrator --model claude-opus-4-6 --rules ... --tests ...\n108\t\n109\t# Sub-agent invocations (e.g., rule-validator running tests):\n110\tgo run ./cmd/test   --log pipeline.log --agent rule-validator --model claude-sonnet-4-20250514 --rules ... --tests ...\n111\t\n112\t# Human manual invocation (no --model):\n113\tgo run ./cmd/validate --log pipeline.log --agent manual --rules ...\n114\t```\n115\t\n116\tLog format:\n117\t- Agent call: `[HH:MM:SS] [cmd-name] [agent=X] [model=Y] output: {json}`\n118\t- Manual CLI call: `[HH:MM:SS] [cmd-name] [agent=X] [cli] output: {json}`\n119\t\n120\tThe `RULE_GEN_LOG` environment variable also works as a fallback \u2014 `--log` takes precedence if both are set.\n121\t\n122\t## Key Concepts\n123\t\n124\t**patterns.json** \u2014 Intermediate JSON between agent extraction and `cmd/construct`.\n125\tContains source, target, language, and MigrationPattern objects (source_fqn,\n126\tdependency_name, provider_type, location_type, complexity, category, concern).\n127\t\n128\t**manifest.json** \u2014 Output of `cmd/scaffold`. cacheDir)`** \u2014 verify all patterns, returns `[]Result`\n149\t- **`Summarize(results)`** \u2014 aggregate results into verified/not_found/skipped/offline counts\n150\t- **`CleanCache(cacheDir)`** # Migrating from Log4j 1

|   | [Log4j 1](http://logging.apache.org/log4j/1.x) has [reached End of Life](https://news.apache.org/foundation/entry/apache_logging_services_project_announces) in 2015, and is no longer supported. Vulnerabilities reported after August 2015 against Log4j 1 are not checked and will not be fixed. Users should [upgrade to Log4j 2](#) to obtain security fixes. |
|---|--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|

Since Log4j 2 has been rewritten from scratch, it introduces many breaking changes to its predecessor. Most notably:

- It uses a new package namespace (`org.apache.logging.log4j`), whereas Log4j 1 used the `org.apache.log4j` namespace,
- It features a [logging API](manual/api.html) which is independent of its reference implementation,
- It uses a new more flexible [configuration file format](manual/configuration.html), which is **incompatible** with the format used by Log4j 1.

## [](#prepare-to-migrate)Prepare to migrate

|   | Are you a library developer?<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />If you are developing a library, which functionality is not related to logging, you only need to rewrite the library to use Log4j 2 API. Skip directly to [Log4j 1 API migration](#api-migration). |
|---|--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|

In order to migrate your application to Log4j 2 you need to assess first how your application **and** its dependencies use Log4j 1. While Log4j 1 didn’t have a formal split between a logging API and a logging backend, for the purpose of this guide, we’ll introduce the following split:

Log4j 1 API

It is the part of the Log4j 1 library that produces log events, and it is the most commonly used. The methods that are considered part of the Log4j 1 API are listed below:

| Class name                    | Methods                                                                                                                                                                                          |
|-------------------------------|--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| `org.apache.log4j.MDC`        | All methods                                                                                                                                                                                      |
| `org.apache.log4j.NDC`        | All methods                                                                                                                                                                                      |
| `org.apache.log4j.Priority`   | All methods                                                                                                                                                                                      |
| `org.apache.log4j.Level`      | All methods                                                                                                                                                                                      |
| `org.apache.log4j.Category`   | All methods, except: methods for the [AppenderAttachable](https://logging.apache.org/log4j/1.x/apidocs/org/apache/log4j/spi/AppenderAttachable.html) interface, `callsAppenders` and `setLevel`. |
| `org.apache.log4j.Logger`     | Same as `Category`                                                                                                                                                                               |
| `org.apache.log4j.LogManager` | All methods                                                                                                                                                                                      |

Table 1. Log4j 1 API methods

Log4j 1 Backend

This is the part of the logging library that consumes log events, formats them and writes to their destination. It also allows to configure Log4j 1 programmatically. It is usually **not used** in code, since the recommended way to configure Log4j 1 is through a configuration file.

While it is fairly simple to check which classes and methods in the `org.apache.log4j` package are used by your own application, the task is much more complex, when it comes to your application dependencies.

All the libraries that use **Log4j 1 API** in their code must have a compile dependency on either [log4j:log4j](https://central.sonatype.com/artifact/log4j/log4j) or its clone [ch.qos.reload4j:reload4j](https://central.sonatype.com/artifact/ch.qos.reload4j/reload4j). There are however misconfigured libraries that declare those dependencies, even if they don’t directly use Log4j 1 **at all**.

To distinguish between libraries that use Log4j 1 and those that don’t, you can look for the presence of other logging APIs. If a library **directly** depends on:

- [`commons-logging:commons-logging`](https://central.sonatype.com/artifact/commons-logging/commons-logging),
- [`org.apache.logging.log4j:log4j-api`](https://central.sonatype.com/artifact/org.apache.logging.log4j/log4j-api),
- [`org.slf4j:slf4j-api`](https://central.sonatype.com/artifact/org.slf4j/slf4j-api),
- [`jboss-logging`](https://central.sonatype.com/artifact/org.jboss.logging/jboss-logging),
- other logging APIs,

it is fair to assume that it uses those libraries **instead** of **Log4j 1 API**, even if it has a direct dependency on `log4j:log4j` or `ch.qos.reload4j:reload4j`.

The following sections explain how to migrate from Log4j 1 to Log4j 2, depending on the way Log4j 1 is used in your application:

- if your application or one of its dependencies is coded against Log4j 1 API, see [Log4j 1 API migration](#api-migration),
- if your application uses Log4j 1 only as logging backend, see [Log4j 1 Backend migration](#backend-migration).

## [](#api-migration)Log4j 1 API migration

To migrate an application that uses Log4j 1 API as logging API, the recommended approach is to modify your code. See [Migrate code from Log4j 1 API to Log4j 2 API](#api-code-migration) for details.

In the case one of your libraries uses Log4j 1 API or you can not modify your logging code at the moment, a Log4j 1 to Log4j 2 bridge is available. See [Use Log4j 1 to Log4j 2 API bridge](#api-use-bridge) for details.

### [](#api-code-migration)Migrate code from Log4j 1 API to Log4j 2 API

|   | You can migrate your code from Log4j 1 to Log4j 2 automatically, by using the [Log4j1ToLog4j2](https://docs.openrewrite.org/recipes/java/logging/log4j/log4j1tolog4j2) OpenRewrite recipe. See [OpenRewrite site](https://docs.openrewrite.org/recipes/java/logging/log4j/log4j1tolog4j2) for more details. |
|---|-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|

Except the change in the package name from `org.apache.log4j` to `org.apache.logging.log4j`, most of the class and method names in Log4j 2 API are inherited from Log4j 1 API.

In order to migrate you code, you need to:

- modify the imports and types used by your application, according to the following table:
  
  | Migrate Log4j 1 type          | to Log4j type                            |
  |-------------------------------|------------------------------------------|
  | `org.apache.log4j.MDC`        | `org.apache.logging.log4j.ThreadContext` |
  | `org.apache.log4j.NDC`        | `org.apache.logging.log4j.ThreadContext` |
  | `org.apache.log4j.Priority`   | `org.apache.logging.log4j.Level`         |
  | `org.apache.log4j.Level`      | `org.apache.logging.log4j.Level`         |
  | `org.apache.log4j.Category`   | `org.apache.logging.log4j.Logger`        |
  | `org.apache.log4j.Logger`     | `org.apache.logging.log4j.Logger`        |
  | `org.apache.log4j.LogManager` | `org.apache.logging.log4j.LogManager`    |
  
  Table 2. Migration of types from Log4j 1 to Log4j 2
- Some Log4j 1 methods were renamed or moved to a different class. Therefore, you need to replace the following methods with their Log4j 2 API equivalents:
  
  | Migrate Log4j 1 method         | to Log4j method              |
  |--------------------------------|------------------------------|
  | `Logger.getLogger()`           | `LogManager.getLogger()`     |
  | `Logger.getRootLogger()`       | `LogManager.getRootLogger()` |
  | `Category.getEffectiveLevel()` | `Logger.getLevel()`          |
  
  Table 3. Migration of methods from Log4j 1 to Log4j 2
- Finally, some methods need specific conversion rules to be applied:
  
  | Method                                                                                                                                                                                       | Description                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          |
  |----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
  | [`Logger.getLogger(String, LoggerFactory)`](https://logging.apache.org/log4j/1.x/apidocs/org/apache/log4j/Logger.html#getLogger%28java.lang.String,%20org.apache.log4j.spi.LoggerFactory%29) | Remove the `LoggerFactory` parameter and use one of Log4j 2’s other extension mechanisms.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            |
  | [`LogManager.shutdown()`](https://logging.apache.org/log4j/1.x/apidocs/org/apache/log4j/LogManager.html#shutdown%28%29)                                                                      | Since Log4j 2.6, an equivalent [`o.a.l.l.LogManager.shutdown()`](javadoc/log4j-api/org/apache/logging/log4j/LogManager.html#shutdown%28%29) method can be used.<br /><br /><br /><br />The utility of this method call depends upon the logging backend used with Log4j API.<br /><br /><br /><br />The Log4j Core backend automatically adds a JVM shutdown hook on start up to perform any cleanups, so the `LogManager.shutdown()` call can be safely removed. Starting in Log4j 2.1, you can also specify a custom [ShutdownCallbackRegistry](javadoc/log4j-core/org/apache/logging/log4j/core/util/ShutdownCallbackRegistry.html).<br /><br /><br /><br />See [log4j2.shutdownCallbackRegistry](manual/systemproperties.html#log4j2.shutdownCallbackRegistry) for more details. |
  | Non Log4j 1 API methods                                                                                                                                                                      | Methods outside of those listed in [\[log4j-1-api-methods\]](#log4j-1-api-methods), such as `Logger.setLevel()` need to be replaced with a method call specific to the logging backend used by the application.<br /><br /><br /><br />Some third-party integrators, such as Spring Boot, provide utility methods that let you abstract the logging backend, e.g. the [`LoggingSystem.setLogLevel()`](https://docs.spring.io/spring-boot/api/java/org/springframework/boot/logging/LoggingSystem.html#setLogLevel%28java.lang.String,org.springframework.boot.logging.LogLevel%29) Spring Boot method.                                                                                                                                                                               |
  
  Table 4. Special Log4j 1 method migration rules

|   | To prevent a performance penalty from string concatenation in disabled log statements, Log4j 1 required the use of `is*Enabled()` guards:<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />```java<br />if (LOGGER.isInfoEnabled()) {
    LOGGER.info("Hello " + username + "!");
}<br />```<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />Since Log4j 2 API introduces [parameterized logging](manual/api.html#best-practice-concat) these guards are no longer necessary and the same statement can be rewritten as:<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />```java<br />LOGGER.info("Hello {}!", username);<br />``` |
|---|--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|

### [](#api-use-bridge)[]()Use Log4j 1 to Log4j 2 API bridge

If you can not modify your application’s code or one of your dependencies is using [Log4j 1 API](#log4j-1-api-methods) as logging API, you can delay the migration process by [installing the Log4j 1 to Log4j 2 bridge](#log4j-1-2-api-installation).

Since forwarding Log4j 1 API calls to Log4j 2 API calls is the basic functionality of the bridge, no further configuration is required from your part.

## [](#backend-migration)Log4j 1 Backend migration

If your application uses Log4j 1 **only** as logging backend bound to another logging API, such as Apache Commons Logging (JCL) or SLF4J, you only need to:

1. Configure all logging bridges to log to Log4j 2 API instead. This can be done by replacing the following dependencies on your application’s runtime classpath:
   
   | Replace Log4j 1 dependency                                                                                 | with Log4j 2 dependency                                                                                                                                                                                    |
   |------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
   | [`log4j:log4j`](https://central.sonatype.com/artifact/log4j/log4j)                                         | [`org.apache.logging.log4j:log4j-core`](https://central.sonatype.com/artifact/org.apache.logging.log4j/log4j-core)                                                                                         |
   | [`ch.qos.reload4j:reload4j`](https://central.sonatype.com/artifact/ch.qos.reload4j/reload4j)               | [`org.apache.logging.log4j:log4j-core`](https://central.sonatype.com/artifact/org.apache.logging.log4j/log4j-core)                                                                                         |
   | [`commons-logging:commons-logging`](https://central.sonatype.com/artifact/commons-logging/commons-logging) | either upgrade to version 1.3.0 (or later)<br /><br /><br /><br />or replace with [`org.apache.logging.log4j:log4j-jcl`](https://central.sonatype.com/artifact/org.apache.logging.log4j/log4j-slf4j2-impl) |
   | [`org.slf4j:slf4j-log4j12`](https://central.sonatype.com/artifact/org.slf4j/slf4j-log4j12)                 | [`org.apache.logging.log4j:log4j-slf4j2-impl`](https://central.sonatype.com/artifact/org.apache.logging.log4j/log4j-slf4j2-impl)                                                                           |
   | [`org.slf4j:slf4j-reload4j`](https://central.sonatype.com/artifact/org.slf4j/slf4j-reload4j)               | [`org.apache.logging.log4j:log4j-slf4j2-impl`](https://central.sonatype.com/artifact/org.apache.logging.log4j/log4j-slf4j2-impl)                                                                           |
   
   Table 5. Dependency migration from Log4j 1 to Log4j 2
   
   See [Installation](manual/installation.html) for more details.
2. Convert your configuration files from the Log4j 1 to the Log4j 2 configuration format. See [Log4j 1 Configuration file migration](#configuration-file-migration) below for more details.

### [](#migrate-custom-components)Migrate Log4j 1 custom components

Since Log4j 1 offered a limited amount of appenders and layouts, over the years users implemented many **custom** components that offered additional features. If you are currently using a custom Log4j 1 component you should proceed as follows:

1. Log4j 2 provides many improvements to Log4j 1 components and many new components. Check if the feature offered by your custom component is not already available in Log4j 2. If you can not find the feature, ask on our [support channels](/support.html).
2. Since Log4j 2.17.2, the Log4j 1 to Log4j 2 bridge has a limited support for using native Log4j 1 appenders and layouts. Native Log4j 1 components can only be configured using Log4j 1 configuration files (see [Use Log4j 1 to Log4j 2 bridge](#ConfigurationCompatibility)) and require the [installation of the Log4j 1 to Log4j 2 bridge](#log4j-1-2-api-installation).
   
   |   | Mixing Log4j 1 and Log4j 2 components will most certainly reduce the performance of the logging system. |
   |---|---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
3. If your Log4j 1 native component is not supported by the Log4j 1 to Log4j 2 bridge, we suggest to rewrite it directly as Log4j 2 component. See [Extending](manual/extending.html) for more details.

## [](#configuration-file-migration)Log4j 1 Configuration file migration

### [](#Log4j2ConfigurationFormat)Convert configuration file from Log4j 1 to Log4j 2

Although the Log4j 2 configuration syntax is different from that of Log4j 1, most, if not all, of the same functionality is available.

The `log4j-1.2-api` bridge contains a small utility that converts `log4j.properties` files into `log4j2.xml` file. In order to use it you need to:

1. Download the `log4j-api`, `log4j-core` and `log4j-1.2-api` artifacts. To retrieve them all at once, see the [Download](download.html) page.
2. Set the `CLASSPATH` environment variable to contain the artifacts mentioned above.
3. Run

```shell
java org.apache.log4j.config.Log4j1ConfigurationConverter \
  --in log4j.properties --out log4j2.xml
```

#### [](#configuration-interpolation)Interpolation

Log4j 1 only supports interpolation using system properties and properties from the `log4j.properties` file using the `${foo}` syntax. Log4j 2 extended this mechanism, by introducing pluggable [Lookups](manual/lookups.html).

In order to convert a Log4j 1 configuration file that uses interpolation to a Log4j 2 configuration file, replace all occurrences of `${foo}` with `${sys:foo}`.

#### [](#configuration-appenders)Appenders

Log4j 2 contains an equivalent for most Log4j 1 appenders:

| Log4j 1 appender                            | Log4j 2 equivalent | Notes                                                   |
|---------------------------------------------|--------------------|---------------------------------------------------------|
| `org.apache.log4j.AsyncAppender`            | `Async`            |                                                         |
| `org.apache.log4j.ConsoleAppender`          | `Console`          |                                                         |
| `org.apache.log4j.DailyRollingFileAppender` | `RollingFile`      | See [additional steps below](#rolling-file-conversion). |
| `org.apache.log4j.FileAppender`             | `File`             |                                                         |
| `org.apache.log4j.RollingFileAppender`      | `RollingFile`      | See [additional steps below](#rolling-file-conversion). |
| `org.apache.log4j.jdbc.JDBCAppender`        | `JDBC`             |                                                         |
| `org.apache.log4j.net.JMSAppender`          | `JMS`              |                                                         |
| `org.apache.log4j.net.SocketAppender`       | `Socket`           |                                                         |
| `org.apache.log4j.net.SMTPAppender`         | `SMTP`             |                                                         |
| `org.apache.log4j.net.SyslogAppender`       | `Syslog`           | Does not support custom layouts.                        |
| `org.apache.log4j.rewrite.RewriteAppender`  | `Rewrite`          |                                                         |

Table 6. Log4j 2 equivalents of Log4j 1 appenders

The rolling file appender in Log4j 2 is based on the [org.apache.log4j.rolling.RollingFileAppender](/log4j/extras/apidocs/org/apache/log4j/rolling/RollingFileAppender.html) from [Apache™ Extras for Apache Log4j®](/log4j/extras/index.html) and additional care must be taken to convert the Log4j 1 rolling appenders to their Log4j 2 equivalent:

- Log4j 2 by default uses a different strategy to determine the index of the archived log files. Log4j 1 always rolls the current log file (e.g. `app.log`) to a log file with index `1` (e.g. `app.log.1`). Log4j 2 on the other hand uses the first available index (e.g. `app.log.42` if files `app.log.1` thru `app.log.41` already exist).
  
  To use the same algorithm to determine the index of the logged file in Log4j 1 and Log4j 2, you need to configure the `fileIndex` attribute of the [default rollover strategy](manual/appenders/rolling-file.html#DefaultRolloverStrategy) to `min`.
  
  ```xml
  <DefaultRolloverStrategy fileIndex="min"/>
  ```
- The two rolling file appenders available in Log4j 1, use an implicit file pattern and triggering policy for the archived log files. If the current log file is called `app.log`, you need to configure the Log4j 2 rolling file appender with the following `filePattern` and triggering policy configuration options:

| Log4j 1 appender                            | Log4j 2 `filePattern` | Log4j 2 triggering policy   |

case-004-tomcat9-to-tomcat10 (5/7 pass)
JudgeValueRationale
budget_checkPASS

Cost $7.41 within budget $35.00

extraction_completeness4

Good coverage with 11 of 13 actionable migration artifacts captured. All five javax-to-jakarta package renames, GenericPrincipal.getPassword() removal, web.xml defaults, session management, access log pattern change, and all four 10.0.x notable changes are properly extracted. Two concrete sections are missing: (1) HTTP/2 connector configuration deduplication change, and (2) logging behavioral change about log files only being created when there is content to write. The general 'System properties' section guidance about properties being replaced with component attributes is also only partially addressed (one specific property captured, but not the general pattern). These are minor but non-trivial omissions.

patterns_qualityPASS

13 patterns extracted with all required fields

report_existsFAIL

No report.yaml found in output

rule_correctness4

All sampled rules have accurate source-side when conditions, clear before/after code examples, and specific documentation URLs. Categories and effort levels are reasonable throughout. Minor issues include: (1) potential overlap between javax.servlet and javax.servlet.jsp patterns, (2) the session rule detects Manager presence rather than absence (slightly inverted logic), (3) two Tomcat internal artifact versions (9.0.0) don't exist on Maven Central (should be 9.0.1+), and (4) the %D filecontent pattern is short enough to risk false positives. These are minor and don't undermine the overall quality.

rules_generatedPASS

11 rule files, sampled 6 valid rules

test_coverageFAIL

No test data files found in tests/data/

output/tomcat9-to-tomcat10-20260624-085846/rules/deployment.yaml
- ruleID: deployment-method-00010
  description: HostConfig.check() semantics changed in Tomcat 10.0.3
  category: potential
  effort: 5
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=tomcat9
    - konveyor.io/source=tomcat
    - konveyor.io/target=tomcat10
    - konveyor.io/target=tomcat
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    The semantics of `HostConfig.check(String)` have changed in Tomcat 10.0.3 onwards.

    ### Before

    ```java
    import org.apache.catalina.startup.HostConfig;
    // Caller was responsible for marking the application as serviced
    // before calling check()
    hostConfig.check(appName);
    ```

    ### After

    ```java
    import org.apache.catalina.startup.HostConfig;
    // Method now handles serviced marking internally
    // If already marked as serviced when called, the method is a NO-OP
    hostConfig.check(appName);
    ```

    ### Additional Info

    - The method now marks the application as serviced before checking resources and un-marks it after checks complete
    - If the application is already marked as serviced when the method is called, it will be a NO-OP
    - Code that manually manages the serviced state around check() calls should be reviewed
    - This change affects custom deployment automation or lifecycle management code
    - See [Tomcat 10.0.x noteable changes](https://tomcat.apache.org/migration-10.html#Tomcat_10.0.x_noteable_changes)
  links:
    - url: https://tomcat.apache.org/migration-10.html#Tomcat_10.0.x_noteable_changes
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: org.apache.catalina.startup.HostConfig.check
        location: METHOD_CALL

output/tomcat9-to-tomcat10-20260624-085846/rules/el-api.yaml
- ruleID: el-api-import-00010
  description: javax.el package renamed to jakarta.el in Tomcat 10
  category: mandatory
  effort: 5
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=tomcat9
    - konveyor.io/source=tomcat
    - konveyor.io/target=tomcat10
    - konveyor.io/target=tomcat
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    The Java package for Expression Language has changed from `javax.el` to `jakarta.el` as part of Jakarta EE 9.

    ### Before

    ```java
    import javax.el.ELContext;
    import javax.el.ExpressionFactory;
    import javax.el.ValueExpression;
    ```

    ### After

    ```java
    import jakarta.el.ELContext;
    import jakarta.el.ExpressionFactory;
    import jakarta.el.ValueExpression;
    ```

    ### Additional Info

    - All `javax.el.*` imports must be changed to `jakarta.el.*`
    - Jakarta Expression Language 4.0 replaces EL 3.0
    - Custom EL resolvers and functions must be updated
    - See [Expression Language 4.0](https://tomcat.apache.org/migration-10.html#Expression_Language_4.0)
  links:
    - url: https://tomcat.apache.org/migration-10.html#Expression_Language_4.0
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: javax.el*
        location: PACKAGE
