The user can override `checkpoint_behavior` explicitly.\n34\t\n35\t## Returns\n36\t\n37\t- `rules_dir` \u2014 Path to generated rule YAML files\n38\t- `tests_dir` \u2014 Path to test data\n39\t- `report` \u2014 Path to report.yaml\n40\t- `summary` \u2014 Markdown summary table with:\n41\t  - rules_count, passed, failed, pass_rate\n42\t  - coverage_report (sections processed/skipped)\n43\t  - fix_iterations used\n44\t\n45\t## Execution Modes\n46\t\n47\t- `interactive` mode: ask at checkpoint only when `checkpoint_behavior=ask`\n48\t- `non_interactive` mode: never prompt the user; obey `checkpoint_behavior`\n49\t  - `continue`: run full pipeline\n50\t  - `stop_after_extract`: end after extraction/coverage with untested outputs\n51\t  - `ask`: treated as `continue` (no prompt allowed in non-interactive mode)\n52\t\n53\t## References\n54\t\n55\t- `references/orchestrator-details.md` \u2014 status-line conventions, parallelism defaults, resume preconditions, rebuild behavior\n56\t\n57\t## Permissions\n58\t\n59\t| Operation | Pattern | Purpose |\n60\t|-----------|---------|---------|\n61\t| shell | `mkdir -p output` | Create output directory |\n62\t| shell | `go run ./cmd/ingest *` | Fetch migration guide as markdown |\n63\t| shell | `go run ./cmd/sections *` | Index guide sections with classification |\n64\t| shell | `go run ./cmd/merge-patterns *` | Merge partial patterns files |\n65\t| shell | `go run ./cmd/contract-validate *` | Validate sub-agent payload contracts |\n66\t| shell | `go run ./cmd/verify *` | Verify patterns against source artifacts |\n67\t| shell | `go run ./cmd/construct *` | Build rule YAML from patterns.json |\n68\t| shell | `go run ./cmd/validate *` | Validate rule YAML structure |\n69\t| shell | `go run ./cmd/scaffold *` | Create test directories and manifests |\n70\t| shell | `go run ./cmd/sanitize *` | Fix XML comments in test data |\n71\t| shell | `go run ./cmd/test *` | Run kantra tests |\n72\t| shell | `go run ./cmd/report *` | Generate summary report with per-rule status |\n73\t| shell | `go run ./cmd/coverage *` | Check guide coverage |\n74\t| shell | `go run ./cmd/log *` | Append orchestrator events to pipeline log |\n75\t| shell | `ls *` | List files and directories |\n76\t| read | `output/**` | Read manifest, test results |\n77\t| write | `output/**` | Write migration artifacts |\n78\t\n79\t**Do NOT use `python`, `python3`, `node`, or any scripting language runtime.**\n80\t**Do NOT use `grep`, `sed`, `awk`, `wc`, `find`, or other shell text-processing tools to parse data that CLI commands already return.**\n81\tEvery `go run ./cmd/*` command returns structured JSON. Use that JSON output directly \u2014 do not pipe it through shell commands to extract fields.\n82\tThis is a Go project. Run only commands listed in this permissions table.\n83\tIf a required action is not permitted, stop and report the limitation.\n84\t\n85\t## UX Principles\n86\t\n87\t- Emit short status lines continuously (start + finish for each step).\n88\t- Only ask at checkpoint when `mode=interactive` and `checkpoint_behavior=ask`.\n89\t- Do not block after testing starts; continue even if some rules remain failing.\n90\t- Fix only failing rules, not the full suite.\n91\t\n92\tFor pipeline logging conventions, see `references/orchestrator-details.md` (Pipeline Transcript section).\n93\t\n94\tFor stage timing instructions, see `references/orchestrator-details.md` (Timing section).\n95\t\n96\tFor sub-agent invocation protocol and contract validation, see `references/orchestrator-details.md` (Sub-agent Protocol section).\n97\t\n98\t## Pipeline\n99\t\n100\t**Error handling:** If any CLI command (`ingest`, `construct`, `validate`, `scaffold`, `sanitize`, `test`, `report`) exits non-zero, print `[step] FAILED \u2014 <error>` and stop the pipeline. Do not proceed to the next step.\n101\t\n102\t**Partial failures:** If a step produces partial results before failing (e.g., `construct` succeeds for 48 patterns but fails on 2), preserve the partial output and report what succeeded. The user can fix the failing patterns and re-run. Do not discard valid results because of a partial failure.\n103\t\n104\t**Resume behavior:** When `resume_from` is set, the user must also provide `migration_dir` pointing to the specific timestamped directory to resume. Skip prior stages and validate prerequisites first. Fail fast when required artifacts are missing.\n105\t\n106\tStage prerequisites (paths relative to `<migration_dir>`):\n107\t- `extract` requires `guide.md`\n108\t- `coverage` requires `patterns.json`\n109\t- `scaffold` requires `rules/`\n110\t- `test` requires `rules/` and `tests/manifest.json`\n111\t- `report` requires source/target metadata plus pass/fail totals and rule ID lists\n112\t\n113\t### 1. Ingest\n114\t\n115\tGenerate a timestamp once at pipeline start (`YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS` in local time).\n116\t\n117\tDetermine the migration directory path:\n118\t- If the user provided `migration_dir`, use that (no timestamp)\n119\t- If the user provided `sources` and `targets` (or `source` and `target`), use `output/<primary_source>-to-<primary_target>-<YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS>` where `primary_source` is `sources[0]` and `primary_target` is `targets[0]`\n120\t- If auto-detecting: ingest to `output/guide-temp.md` first, read the first ~50 lines to detect source/target/language (lowercase, hyphenated names like `spring-boot-3`), then use `output/<source>-to-<target>-<YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS>`\n121\t\n122\t```bash\n123\tmkdir -p output/<source>-to-<target>-<YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS>\n124\t```\n125\t\n126\tEvery `go run` command should be a standalone invocation with fully-expanded arguments \u2014 substitute actual paths and flag values directly into each command. Do not use shell variable assignments (`VAR=...`) or compound `&&` chains, since these don't match the permissions table.\n127\t\n128\tThe log flags are: `--log <migration_dir>/pipeline.log --agent orchestrator --model <your_model_id>`. Append these literally to every CLI invocation.\n129\t\n130\t```\n131\t[ingest] Fetching guide from <source>...\n132\t```\n133\t\n134\t- **URL:** `go run ./cmd/ingest --log <migration_dir>/pipeline.log --agent orchestrator --model <your_model_id> --input <url> --output <migration_dir>/guide.md`\n135\t- **File (not markdown):** `go run ./cmd/ingest --log <migration_dir>/pipeline.log --agent orchestrator --model <your_model_id> --input <path> --output <migration_dir>/guide.md`\n136\t- **Pasted text or already markdown:** Write directly to `<migration_dir>/guide.md`\n137\t\n138\tIf auto-detecting, write `output/guide-temp.md` to `<migration_dir>/guide.md` using the Write tool after the migration directory path is determined.\n139\t\n140\t**Stub detection \u2014 follow sub-pages.** After ingesting each URL, check the output for stub characteristics. A page is a stub if it has fewer than 100 non-blank lines of content after `cmd/ingest` processing (`cmd/ingest` already strips `<nav>`, `<footer>`, and `<aside>` elements during HTML-to-markdown conversion, so no additional filtering is needed).\n141\t\n142\tIf a stub is detected:\n143\t\n144\t1. Read the ingested markdown and extract all links whose resolved URL shares the same base path as the original URL (same-origin sibling pages). Sibling links are those pointing to `*.html` files under the same directory path as the original URL. Exclude external links, anchor-only links (`#...`), and links to parent directories.\n145\t2. For each sibling link, resolve it to a full URL relative to the original URL's base path.\n146\t3. Ingest each sub-page with `cmd/ingest` into a separate file (`guide-part-<N>.md`).\n147\t4. Concatenate all parts (original + sub-pages) into the final `guide.md`, in the order the links appear in the stub page (document order).\n148\t5. If a sub-page fetch fails (404, timeout), log a warning (`[ingest] WARNING \u2014 failed to fetch <url>: <error>`) and skip that page. Do not abort the pipeline \u2014 partial content is better than none.\n149\t\n150\tThis ensures that documentation sites which split content across multiple pages are fully captured. Without this step, the pipeline will only see the stub and miss the bulk of the migration content.\n151\t\n152\tCount lines (`GUIDE_LINES`) and section headings. Print:\n153\t\n154\t```\n155\t[ingest] Done \u2014 <GUIDE_LINES> lines, <N> sections \u2192 <migration_dir>/ (<elapsed>)\n156\t```\n157\t\n158\t### 2. Extract (parallel)\n159\t\n160\tExtraction uses parallel agents to process the guide faster. The orchestrator splits the guide into chunks and spawns multiple rule-writer agents.\n161\t\n162\t**2a. Index sections and auto-detect metadata:**\n163\t\n164\t```bash\n165\tgo run ./cmd/sections <log_flags> --guide <migration_dir>/guide.md\n166\t```\n167\t\n168\tThis returns JSON with all sections classified as `content` or `header-only`. Filter to content sections only.\n169\t\n170\t```\n171\t[extract] Extracting patterns from <content_count> sections (<N> parallel agents)...\n172\t```\n173\t\n174\t**2b. Split into chunks and dispatch:**\n175\t\n176\tSplit the content sections into **N balanced chunks** (minimum 1, maximum 5 agents). Balance by section count. Assign each chunk a number (1, 2, ..., N).\n177\t\n178\t**Keep related sections together.** Group sections by their top-level heading (`##`) \u2014 all subsections (`###`, `####`) under the same `##` must stay in the same chunk. Migration guides pair before/after code examples across subsections within a topic; splitting them across agents means no agent sees both sides of the diff. Balance chunks by top-level-heading groups, not by individual sections.\n179\t\n180\t**Invoke:** `rule-writer` (one per chunk, in parallel)\n181\t**Purpose:** Extract migration patterns from assigned sections.\n182\t**Inputs per invocation:**\n183\t  - guide: <migration_dir>/guide.md\n184\t  - sources: {sources array (e.g., [\"spring-boot3\", \"spring-boot\"])}\n185\t  - targets: {targets array (e.g., [\"spring-boot4\", \"spring-boot\"])}\n186\t  - rules_dir: <migration_dir>/rules\n187\t  - sections: {chunk subset \u2014 list of `{heading, start_line, end_line}` objects}\n188\t  - all_headings: {full list of ALL content section headings from step 2a \u2014 not just this chunk's sections. Enables each agent to detect multi-path migrations even when variant sections are in other chunks.}\n189\t  - output_file: <migration_dir>/patterns-{chunk_number}.json\n190\t**Parallel:** yes\n191\t**Expect:**\n192\t  - patterns_count, output_file\n193\t\n194\t**2c. Merge, verify, and construct:**\n195\t\n196\tAfter all agents complete, merge the partial patterns files, verify source artifacts, and build rules:\n197\t\n198\t```bash\n199\tgo run ./cmd/merge-patterns <log_flags> --output <migration_dir>/patterns.json <migration_dir>/patterns-1.json <migration_dir>/patterns-2.json ...\n200\tgo run ./cmd/verify <log_flags> --patterns <migration_dir>/patterns.json --output <migration_dir>/verify-results.json --cache <migration_dir>/verify-cache\n201\tgo run ./cmd/construct <log_flags> --patterns <migration_dir>/patterns.json --output <migration_dir>/rules\n202\tgo run ./cmd/validate <log_flags> --rules <migration_dir>/rules\n203\t```\n204\t\n205\t**Verification step:** `cmd/verify` downloads source JARs from Maven Central and checks that each pattern's `source_fqn` exists in the declared `source_artifact`. This catches hallucinated class names before rules reach testing.\n206\t\n207\tThe verify stdout JSON contains `verified`, `not_found`, `skipped`, and `offline` counts. Print:\n208\t\n209\t```\n210\t[verify] <verified> verified, <not_found> not found, <skipped> skipped\n211\t```\n212\t\n213\tIf `not_found > 0`, read `<migration_dir>/verify-results.json` and note which `pattern_index` values have `status: \"not_found\"`. After construct runs, use the `pattern_rule_map` from construct's stdout JSON to map each `pattern_index` \u2192 `rule_id`. Carry `verified_rule_ids` and `not_found_rule_ids` forward to step 5 (report).\n214\t\n215\tIf validation fails, fix `<migration_dir>/patterns.json` (remove invalid entries) and re-run construct.\n216\t\n217\t```\n218\t[extract] Done \u2014 <patterns_count> patterns \u2192 <rules_count> rules in <migration_dir>/rules/ (<elapsed>)\n219\t```\n220\t\n221\tSave `source`, `target`, `patterns_count`, `rules_count`, and verify counts for the final summary.\n222\t\n223\t### 2d. Coverage Check\n224\t\n225\tRun the coverage tool to find sections with named artifacts that weren't extracted:\n226\t\n227\t```bash\n228\tgo run ./cmd/coverage <log_flags> --guide <migration_dir>/guide.md --patterns <migration_dir>/patterns.json --language <language>\n229\t```\n230\t\n231\tIf `gap_count > 0` in the JSON output, print:\n232\t\n233\t```\n234\t[coverage] <gap_count> sections with uncovered artifacts: <heading_1>, <heading_2>, ...\n235\t```\n236\t\n237\tConvert gaps to sections and send back to the rule-writer in chunk mode for targeted re-extraction. Each gap has `heading` and `line` \u2014 use the sections index to get the `start_line` and `end_line` for that heading. Mention the uncovered artifacts in the prompt so the sub-agent focuses on them.\n238\t\n239\t**Invoke:** `rule-writer` (chunk mode)\n240\t**Purpose:** Extract patterns from specific sections that the coverage check flagged.\n241\t**Inputs:**\n242\t  - guide: <migration_dir>/guide.md\n243\t  - sources: {sources array}\n244\t  - targets: {targets array}\n245\t  - rules_dir: <migration_dir>/rules\n246\t  - sections: {gap sections converted to `[{heading, start_line, end_line}]` format}\n247\t  - output_file: <migration_dir>/patterns-gaps.json\n248\t**Parallel:** no\n249\t**Expect:**\n250\t  - patterns_count, output_file\n251\t\n252\tThe sub-agent writes only the new patterns to `<migration_dir>/patterns-gaps.json`. It does NOT read or inspect existing patterns \u2014 the orchestrator handles deduplication. After the sub-agent returns, merge, verify, and rebuild:\n253\t\n254\t```bash\n255\tgo run ./cmd/merge-patterns <log_flags> --output <migration_dir>/patterns.json <migration_dir>/patterns.json <migration_dir>/patterns-gaps.json\n256\tgo run ./cmd/verify <log_flags> --patterns <migration_dir>/patterns.json --output <migration_dir>/verify-results.json --cache <migration_dir>/verify-cache\n257\tgo run ./cmd/construct <log_flags> --patterns <migration_dir>/patterns.json --output <migration_dir>/rules\n258\tgo run ./cmd/validate <log_flags> --rules <migration_dir>/rules\n259\t```\n260\t\n261\tRe-run the coverage check. If gaps remain, accept them \u2014 one re-extraction pass is enough.\n262\t\n263\t```\n264\t[coverage] Done \u2014 <final_gap_count> remaining gaps (accepted) (<elapsed>)\n265\t```\n266\t\n267\tIf `gap_count == 0`:\n268\t\n269\t```\n270\t[coverage] No gaps found (<elapsed>)\n271\t```\n272\t\n273\t### Checkpoint\n274\t\n275\tAfter extraction/coverage:\n276\t\n277\t- If `mode=non_interactive`, do **not** prompt:\n278\t  - `checkpoint_behavior=continue` or `ask`: continue automatically\n279\t  - `checkpoint_behavior=stop_after_extract`: skip testing and go to Step 5 (Report)\n280\t- If `mode=interactive`:\n281\t  - `checkpoint_behavior=continue`: continue automatically\n282\t  - `checkpoint_behavior=stop_after_extract`: skip testing and go to Step 5 (Report)\n283\t  - `checkpoint_behavior=ask`: ask:\n284\t    - `Continue with test generation and validation? (y/n)`\n285\t    - if no, skip to Step 5 (Report) with untested rules\n286\t\n287\t**Rules-only report:** When skipping to Step 5, invoke `cmd/report` with `--passed 0 --failed 0 --kantra-limitation 0` and empty `--passed-rules`, `--failed-rules`, `--kantra-limitation-rules` flags. Pass `--rules-total`, `--verified-rules`, and `--not-found-rules` from extraction. All rules get `test_status: untested`.\n288\t\n289\t### 3. Test Generation\n290\t\n291\t**3a. Scaffold (orchestrator runs this directly, not an agent):**\n292\t\n293\t```bash\n294\tgo run ./cmd/scaffold <log_flags> --rules <migration_dir>/rules --output <migration_dir>/tests --patterns <migration_dir>/patterns.json\n295\t```\n296\t\n297\tThis creates all directories, `.test.yaml` files, and `manifest.json`. No LLM needed.\n298\t\n299\t**3b. Read manifest and split into batches:**\n300\t\n301\tRead `<migration_dir>/tests/manifest.json`. It contains a `groups` array \u2014 each group has `name`, `data_dir`, `files` (paths to generate), and `rule_ids`.\n302\t\n303\tSplit the groups into **batches of ~5 groups each** (minimum 1 batch, maximum 5 batches), balanced by rule count.\n304\t\n305\t**3c. Spawn test-generator agents:**\n306\t\n307\t```\n308\t[test-gen] Generating test data for <rules_count> rules (<B> parallel agents)...\n309\t```\n310\t\n311\t**Invoke:** `test-generator` (one per batch, up to 5 in parallel)\n312\t**Purpose:** Generate compilable test source code that triggers the assigned rules.\n313\t**Inputs per invocation:**\n314\t  - rules_dir: <migration_dir>/rules\n315\t  - tests_dir: <migration_dir>/tests\n316\t  - groups: {batch subset from manifest.json \u2014 include name, data_dir, rule_ids, files}\n317\t**Parallel:** yes\n318\t**Expect:**\n319\t  - groups_completed, files_written\n320\t\n321\t**3d. Collect results and sanitize.** After all agents complete:\n322\t\n323\tCollect `suspected_kantra_limitations` from all rule-writer and test-generator agent returns (merge, deduplicate by `rule_id`). If non-empty, print:\n324\t\n325\t```\n326\t[test-gen] <N> suspected kantra limitations (Maven Central: no plain-semver version): <rule_id_1>, ...\n327\t```\n328\t\n329\tCarry this merged list forward as `pre_classified_kantra_limitations` \u2014 it will be passed to the rule-validator to skip the fix loop for these rules.\n330\t\n331\tSanitize XML:\n332\t\n333\t```bash\n334\tgo run ./cmd/sanitize <log_flags> --dir <migration_dir>/tests/data\n335\t```\n336\t\n337\t```\n338\t[test-gen] Done \u2014 <total_groups> groups, <total_files> files (<elapsed>)\n339\t```\n340\t\n341\t### 4. Validate (orchestrator-driven loop)\n342\t\n343\tThe orchestrator runs tests and uses a sub-agent for LLM-driven repairs on failures.\n344\t\n345\t**4a. Run tests:**\n346\t\n347\t```bash\n348\tgo run ./cmd/test <log_flags> --rules <migration_dir>/rules --tests <migration_dir>/tests --timeout 5m\n349\t```\n350\t\n351\tThe CLI runs each test file sequentially and automatically retries timed-out files once (`--retry-timeouts`, on by default). Tests run locally via `--run-local=true`. To run a subset, use `--files` with bare filenames (e.g., `--files data-1.test.yaml,data-2.test.yaml`), resolved relative to `--tests` dir.\n352\t\n353\tPrint the result:\n354\t\n355\t```\n356\t[validate] <total_passed>/<total_rules> passed (<elapsed>)\n357\t```\n358\t\n359\tOr if failures:\n360\t\n361\t```\n362\t[validate] <total_passed>/<total_rules> passed \u2014 <F> failures: <rule_id_1>, <rule_id_2>, ...\n363\t```\n364\t\n365\tIf all passed (elapsed shown above), skip to step 5.\n366\t\n367\t**4b. Fix (only if failures):**\n368\t\n369\t```\n370\t[fix] Fixing <F> failures: <rule_id_1>, <rule_id_2> ...\n371\t```\n372\t\n373\t**Invoke:** `rule-validator`\n374\t**Purpose:** Fix test data for failing rules so they pass kantra validation.\n375\t**Inputs:**\n376\t  - rules_dir: <migration_dir>/rules\n377\t  - tests_dir: <migration_dir>/tests\n378\t  - failing_rules: {list with rule_id, test_file, error for each failure}\n379\t  - pre_classified_kantra_limitations: {merged list from rule-writer and test-generator suspected_kantra_limitations \u2014 may be empty}\n380\t  - max_iterations: 1\n381\t**Parallel:** no\n382\t**Expect:**\n383\t  - fixed_rules, still_failing, kantra_limitation_rules, iterations_used, fix_details\n384\t  - results_by_rule (with `result_type` + `recommended_action`)\n385\t\n386\tThe validator agent owns the fix-verify loop \u2014 it fixes files, re-runs tests via `cmd/test`, and iterates up to `max_iterations`. Default is 1 iteration; pass up to 3 if the user requests more attempts.\n387\t\n388\t**The orchestrator must NOT run its own fix attempts.** Do not manually edit test files, create stub classes, toggle analysisParams, or retry. All fix work goes through the rule-validator sub-agent. When the validator returns `still_failing`, accept that result and move on.\n389\t\n390\tPrint the result:\n391\t\n392\t```\n393\t[fix] <fixed_count> fixed, <still_failing_count> still failing, <kantra_limitation_count> kantra limitations (<validate elapsed>)\n394\t```\n395\t\n396\tThe `<validate elapsed>` is the total time since the validate stage started (step 4a), including test runs and all fix iterations.\n397\t\n398\tIf `kantra_limitation_rules` is non-empty, print:\n399\t\n400\t```\n401\t[fix] kantra limitations (engine cannot test \u2014 rule is correct): <rule_id_1>, ...\n402\t```\n403\t\n404\tGroup unresolved failures by `result_type` in `results_by_rule` and include grouped counts in the final summary (e.g., `still_failing_timeout: 2`, `still_failing_kantra_limitation: 1`).\n405\t\n406\tIf still_failing is non-empty, move on \u2014 don't block the pipeline.\n407\t\n408\t### 5. Report\n409\t\n410\tCollate pass/fail results from the test run and the fix loop. Generate `report.yaml` with per-rule test and verification status. No labels are written to rule YAML files \u2014 all pipeline metadata lives in the report.\n411\t\n412\t```bash\n413\tgo run ./cmd/report <log_flags> --source <comma-separated sources> --target <comma-separated targets> --output <migration_dir>/report.yaml --rules-total <N> --passed <P> --failed <F> --kantra-limitation <K> --passed-rules <comma-separated passed rule IDs> --failed-rules <comma-separated failed rule IDs> --kantra-limitation-rules <comma-separated kantra limitation rule IDs> --verified-rules <comma-separated verified rule IDs> --not-found-rules <comma-separated not-found rule IDs>\n414\t```\n415\t\n416\tThe `--verified-rules` and `--not-found-rules` flags come from the verification mapping built in step 2c (pattern_index \u2192 rule_id via construct's pattern_rule_map).\n417\t\n418\tThe report includes a `rules` section with per-rule `test_status` (passed/failed/kantra-limitation/untested) and `source_verified` (true/false). The pass rate is computed as `passed / (passed + failed)` \u2014 kantra limitations are excluded since they are not failures, but also not confirmed passes.\n419\t\n420\t### 6. Summary\n421\t\n422\tPrint a formatted summary table using GitHub-flavored markdown:\n423\t\n424\t```markdown\n425\t## Summary\n426\t\n427\t| | |\n428\t|---|---|\n429\t| **Input** | <guide title or URL as a markdown link> |\n430\t| **Migration** | <primary_source> \u2192 <primary_target> (<language>) |\n431\t| **Guide** | <GUIDE_LINES> lines, <N> sections \u2192 <M> produced patterns, <K> skipped |\n432\t| **Rules** | <rules_count> generated, **<P>/<N> passed (<percent>%)** |\n433\t| **Verification** | <verified>/<total> source-verified, <not_found> not found, <skipped> skipped (omit row if all skipped) |\n434\t| **Kantra limitations** | <K> rules correct but not auto-testable \u2014 engine cannot compare non-semver versions (omit row if K=0) |\n435\t| **Fix iterations** | <iterations used, 0 if none> |\n436\t| **Timing** | total: <total elapsed> \u2014 ingest: <elapsed>, extract: <elapsed>, coverage: <elapsed>, test-gen: <elapsed>, validate: <elapsed>, report: <elapsed> |\n437\t| **Output** | `<migration_dir>/patterns.json` (patterns), `<migration_dir>/rules/` (rules), `<migration_dir>/tests/` (tests), `<migration_dir>/report.yaml` (report) |\n438\t\n439\t### Rule Categories\n440\t\n441\tUse the `groups` array from the `construct` JSON output \u2014 it lists each file and its rule count. Do not iterate rule files manually.\n442\t\n443\t| Group | Rules | Status |\n444\t|---|---|---|\n445\t| <group_name> (<brief description of what rules cover>) | <rule_count> | <passed>/<total> passed |\n446\t| ... | ... | ... |\n447\t```\n448\t\n449\tIf there are failures, add a row to the top-level table:\n450\t\n451\t```\n452\t| **Failed** | <rule_id_1>, <rule_id_2>, ... |\n453\t```\n454\t\n455\tIf coverage was low (< 30% of sections produced patterns), add a row:\n456\t\n457\t```\n458\t| **Warning** | Low extraction coverage (<M>/<K> sections) |\n459\t```\n460\t\n461\t**Rules-only summary (when `checkpoint_behavior=stop_after_extract`):**\n462\t\n463\tWhen testing was skipped, use this simplified table instead:\n464\t\n465\t```markdown\n466\t## Summary\n467\t\n468\t| | |\n469\t|---|---|\n470\t| **Input** | <guide title or URL as a markdown link> |\n471\t| **Migration** | <primary_source> \u2192 <primary_target> (<language>) |\n472\t| **Guide** | <GUIDE_LINES> lines, <N> sections \u2192 <M> produced patterns, <K> skipped |\n473\t| **Rules** | <rules_count> generated (untested) |\n474\t| **Verification** | <verified>/<total> source-verified, <not_found> not found, <skipped> skipped (omit row if all skipped) |\n475\t| **Timing** | total: <total elapsed> \u2014 ingest: <elapsed>, extract: <elapsed>, coverage: <elapsed>, report: <elapsed> |\n476\t| **Output** | `<migration_dir>/patterns.json` (patterns), `<migration_dir>/rules/` (rules), `<migration_dir>/report.yaml` (report) |\n477\t| **Next step** | Run `/generate-rules-with-test resume_from=scaffold migration_dir=<migration_dir>` to add tests |\n478\t```\n479\t\n480\tOmit these rows: **Kantra limitations**, **Fix iterations**, **Failed** (no testing ran).\n481\tOmit `tests/` from the **Output** row and test-gen/validate timing from the **Timing** row.\n482\tInclude the **Rule Categories** table as normal.\n483\t",

- [Upgrading 10.0.x](#Upgrading_10.0.x)
  
  1. [Tomcat 10.0.x noteable changes](#Tomcat_10.0.x_noteable_changes)
  2. [Tomcat 10.0.x configuration file differences](#Tomcat_10.0.x_configuration_file_differences)

### General

Please read the general [Migration Guide page](migration.html) first, for common considerations that apply to migration or upgrade between versions of Apache Tomcat®.

### Migrating from 9.0.x to 10.0.x

This section lists all the known changes between 9.0.x and 10.0.x which may cause backwards compatibility problems when upgrading.

#### Java 8 required

Apache Tomcat 10.0.x requires Java 8 or later. This is unchanged from Tomcat 9.0.x.

#### Specification APIs

Apache Tomcat 10 supports the Jakarta Servlet 5.0, Jakarta Pages 3.0, Jakarta Expression Language 4.0, JakartaWebSocket 2.0 and Jakarta Authentication 2.0 [specifications](https://cwiki.apache.org/confluence/display/TOMCAT/Specifications).

There is a significant breaking change between Tomcat 9.0.x and Tomcat 10.0.x. The Java package used by the specification APIs has changed from javax... to jakarta.... It will be necessary to recompile web applications against the new APIs.

Tomcat can convert an existing web application from Java EE 8 to Jakarta EE 9 at deployment time using the Apache Tomcat migration tool for Jakarta EE. To make use of the feature, the web application should be placed in the Host `legacyAppBase` folder (by default named `webapps-javaee`) and they will be converted to an equivalent Jakarta EE web application in the Host `appBase` folder (by default named `webapps`).

Alternately, the [Apache Tomcat migration tool for Jakarta EE](https://tomcat.apache.org/download-migration.cgi) or any similar conversion tool can be used ahead of time to benefit from faster deployment time and more precise conversion configuration options.

#### Servlet 5.0 API

The Java package has changed from javax.servlet to jakarta.servlet.

#### Pages 3.0

The Java package has changed from javax.servlet.jsp to jakarta.servlet.jsp.

#### Expression Language 4.0

The Java package has changed from javax.el to jakarta.el.

#### WebSocket 2.0

The Java package has changed from javax.websocket to jakarta.websocket.

#### Authentication 2.0

The Java package has changed from javax.security.auth.message to jakarta.security.auth.message.

#### Internal APIs

Whilst the Tomcat 10 internal API is broadly compatible with Tomcat 9 there have been many changes at the detail level and they are not binary compatible. Developers of custom components that interact with Tomcat's internals should review the JavaDoc for the relevant API.

Of particular note are:

- GenericPrincipal.getPassword() has been removed.

#### System properties

Support for many of the Tomcat specific system properties has been removed and the system property replaced with an attribute on the appropriate component such as the Connector, Context or Manager.

#### web.xml defaults

`conf/web.xml` sets the default request and response character encoding to UTF-8.

#### Session management

Session persistence on restart has been disabled by default. It may be re-enabled globally in conf/context.xml or per web application.

#### HTTP/2

The configuration settings that were duplicated between the HTTP/1.1 and HTTP/2 connectors have been removed from the HTTP/2 connector which will now inherit them from the associated HTTP/1.1 connector.

#### Logging

The logging implementation now only creates log files once there is something to write to the log files.

#### Access Log Patterns

To align with httpd, the `%D` pattern now logs request time in microseconds rather than milliseconds. To log request time in milliseconds, use `%{ms}T`.

### Upgrading 10.0.x

When upgrading instances of Apache Tomcat from one version of Tomcat 10 to another, particularly when using separate locations for $CATALINA\_HOME and $CATALINA\_BASE, it is necessary to ensure that any changes in the configuration files such as new attributes and changes to defaults are applied as part of the upgrade. To assist with the identification of these changes, the form below may be used to view the differences between the configuration files in different versions of Tomcat 10.

#### Tomcat 10.0.x noteable changes

The Tomcat developers aim for each patch release to be fully backwards compatible with the previous release. Occasionally, it is necessary to break backwards compatibility in order to fix a bug. In most cases, these changes will go unnoticed. This section lists changes that are not fully backwards compatible and might cause breakage when upgrading.

- In 10.0.3 onwards, the semantics of the `HostConfig.check(String)` method have changed. Rather than marking the application as serviced before calling the method, the method will mark the application as serviced before checking resources and then un-mark the application as being serviced after the checks are complete. If the application is marked as serviced when the method is called, the method will be a NO-OP.
- In 10.0.9 onwards, Tomcat no longer adds an "Expires" HTTP response header when adding "Cache-Control: private" due to a CONFIDENTIAL transport-guarantee. This will likely cause a change in caching behavior for applications that do not explicitly set their own headers but rely on Tomcat's previous behavior. If you wish to disable caching, you will need to configure it explicitly in your application. See [BZ 65513](https://bz.apache.org/bugzilla/show_bug.cgi?id=65513) for more information.
- In 10.0.11 onwards, as a result of the updated fork of Commons FileUpload now using `java.nio.file.Files`, applications using multi-part uploads need to ensure that the JVM is configured with sufficient direct memory to store all in progress multi-part uploads.
- In 10.0.14 onwards, the system property `org.apache.juli.AsyncLoggerPollInterval` is no longer used.

#### Tomcat 10.0.x configuration file differences

Select a configuration file, old version and new version from the boxes below and then click "View differences" to see the differences. The differences will be shown in a new tab/window.

**Note:** If there are no differences you will see an error page.

Configuration file: All configuration files catalina.policy catalina.properties context.xml logging.properties server.xml tomcat-users.xml web.xml

Old version: 10.0.0-M1 10.0.0-M3 10.0.0-M4 10.0.0-M5 10.0.0-M6 10.0.0-M7 10.0.0-M8 10.0.0-M9 10.0.0-M10 10.0.0 10.0.2 10.0.4 10.0.5 10.0.6 10.0.7 10.0.8 10.0.10 10.0.11 10.0.12 10.0.13 10.0.14 10.0.16 10.0.17 10.0.18 10.0.20 10.0.21 10.0.22 10.0.23 10.0.26 10.0.27 , new version: 10.0.0-M1 10.0.0-M3 10.0.0-M4 10.0.0-M5 10.0.0-M6 10.0.0-M7 10.0.0-M8 10.0.0-M9 10.0.0-M10 10.0.0 10.0.2 10.0.4 10.0.5 10.0.6 10.0.7 10.0.8 10.0.10 10.0.11 10.0.12 10.0.13 10.0.14 10.0.16 10.0.17 10.0.18 10.0.20 10.0.21 10.0.22 10.0.23 10.0.26 10.0.27 trunk (unreleased)

View Differences

You can also use a Git command similar to the following from within a working copy:

```
git diff 10.0.0 10.0.12 -- conf/
```

- ruleID: internal-api-method-00010
  description: GenericPrincipal.getPassword() removed in Tomcat 10
  category: mandatory
  effort: 5
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=tomcat9
    - konveyor.io/source=tomcat
    - konveyor.io/target=tomcat10
    - konveyor.io/target=tomcat
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    The method `GenericPrincipal.getPassword()` has been removed in Tomcat 10. This is part of the broader internal API changes between Tomcat 9 and 10.

    ### Before

    ```java
    import org.apache.catalina.realm.GenericPrincipal;

    GenericPrincipal principal = (GenericPrincipal) request.getUserPrincipal();
    String password = principal.getPassword();
    ```

    ### After

    ```java
    import org.apache.catalina.realm.GenericPrincipal;

    GenericPrincipal principal = (GenericPrincipal) request.getUserPrincipal();
    // getPassword() has been removed - passwords should not be
    // accessible from the Principal for security reasons.
    // Refactor code to avoid needing the password after authentication.
    ```

    ### Additional Info

    - This removal is for security hardening — passwords should not be accessible post-authentication
    - Custom Realms or authentication code that relied on this method must be refactored
    - Review the Tomcat 10 JavaDoc for alternative approaches
    - Other internal APIs may also have changed — review the JavaDoc for any custom components
    - See [Internal APIs](https://tomcat.apache.org/migration-10.html#Internal_APIs)
  links:
    - url: https://tomcat.apache.org/migration-10.html#Internal_APIs
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: org.apache.catalina.realm.GenericPrincipal.getPassword
        location: METHOD_CALL

- ruleID: logging-pattern-00010
  description: Access log %D pattern now logs microseconds instead of milliseconds
  category: potential
  effort: 1
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=tomcat9
    - konveyor.io/source=tomcat
    - konveyor.io/target=tomcat10
    - konveyor.io/target=tomcat
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    The `%D` access log pattern now logs request time in **microseconds** instead of milliseconds, to align with httpd. If you need millisecond precision, use `%{ms}T` instead.

    ### Migration Steps

    1. Check your `server.xml` for access log valve configurations using the `%D` pattern
    2. If your log analysis tools expect milliseconds, replace `%D` with `%{ms}T`
    3. If you are parsing access logs programmatically, update parsers to handle microsecond values

    ### Additional Info

    - `%D` now logs in microseconds (was milliseconds in Tomcat 9)
    - Use `%{ms}T` for millisecond precision (new replacement)
    - Log monitoring and analysis tools may need updates to handle the scale change
    - This change aligns Tomcat with Apache httpd behavior
    - See [Access Log Patterns](https://tomcat.apache.org/migration-10.html#Access_Log_Patterns)
  links:
    - url: https://tomcat.apache.org/migration-10.html#Access_Log_Patterns
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    builtin.filecontent:
        pattern: '%D'
        filePattern: .*server\.xml
- ruleID: logging-pattern-00020
  description: System property removed in Tomcat 10.0.14
  category: mandatory
  effort: 1
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=tomcat9
    - konveyor.io/source=tomcat
    - konveyor.io/target=tomcat10
    - konveyor.io/target=tomcat
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    The system property `org.apache.juli.AsyncLoggerPollInterval` has been removed in Tomcat 10.0.14 and is no longer used.

    ### Migration Steps

    1. Remove any references to `org.apache.juli.AsyncLoggerPollInterval` from startup scripts, system property configurations, Dockerfiles, or environment files.
    2. This property previously controlled the polling interval for asynchronous logging. The logging system now manages this internally.

    ### Additional Info

    - This property was removed without a direct replacement
    - Asynchronous logging continues to work but the poll interval is no longer configurable via system property
    - Check `catalina.sh`, `catalina.bat`, `setenv.sh`, `setenv.bat`, and any Docker or CI configurations
    - See [Tomcat 10.0.x noteable changes](https://tomcat.apache.org/migration-10.html#Tomcat_10.0.x_noteable_changes)
  links:
    - url: https://tomcat.apache.org/migration-10.html#Tomcat_10.0.x_noteable_changes
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    builtin.filecontent:
        pattern: org\.apache\.juli\.AsyncLoggerPollInterval
        filePattern: .*\.(sh|bat|properties|xml|ya?ml|Dockerfile|env)

output/tomcat9-to-tomcat10-20260624-085846/rules/security-api.yaml
- ruleID: security-api-import-00010
  description: javax.security.auth.message renamed to jakarta.security.auth.message in Tomcat 10
  category: mandatory
  effort: 5
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=tomcat9
    - konveyor.io/source=tomcat
    - konveyor.io/target=tomcat10
    - konveyor.io/target=tomcat
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    The Java package for Jakarta Authentication (JASPIC) has changed from `javax.security.auth.message` to `jakarta.security.auth.message` as part of Jakarta EE 9.

    ### Before

    ```java
    import javax.security.auth.message.AuthException;
    import javax.security.auth.message.AuthStatus;
    import javax.security.auth.message.module.ServerAuthModule;
    ```

    ### After

    ```java
    import jakarta.security.auth.message.AuthException;
    import jakarta.security.auth.message.AuthStatus;
    import jakarta.security.auth.message.module.ServerAuthModule;
    ```

    ### Additional Info

    - All `javax.security.auth.message.*` imports must be changed to `jakarta.security.auth.message.*`
    - Jakarta Authentication 2.0 replaces JASPIC 1.1
    - Custom authentication modules (SAMs) must be updated
    - See [Authentication 2.0](https://tomcat.apache.org/migration-10.html#Authentication_2.0)
  links:
    - url: https://tomcat.apache.org/migration-10.html#Authentication_2.0
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: javax.security.auth.message*
        location: PACKAGE

    Session persistence on restart has been disabled by default in Tomcat 10. Previously, sessions were persisted across Tomcat restarts.

    ### Migration Steps

    1. If your application requires session persistence across Tomcat restarts, re-enable it
    2. To re-enable globally, uncomment or add the Manager configuration in `conf/context.xml`
    3. To re-enable per web application, add the Manager configuration to the application's `context.xml`

    ### Additional Info

    - Sessions will no longer survive Tomcat restarts by default
    - This change improves startup time and reduces potential deserialization issues
    - Applications relying on session persistence must explicitly configure it
    - Check `conf/context.xml` and per-application context configurations
    - See [Session management](https://tomcat.apache.org/migration-10.html#Session_management)

- ruleID: web-defaults-pattern-00010
  description: Default request/response character encoding changed to UTF-8 in Tomcat 10
  category: potential
  effort: 3
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=tomcat9
    - konveyor.io/source=tomcat
    - konveyor.io/target=tomcat10
    - konveyor.io/target=tomcat
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    In Tomcat 10, `conf/web.xml` sets the default request and response character encoding to UTF-8. This may affect applications that relied on the previous default encoding.

    ### Migration Steps

    1. If your application explicitly sets character encoding in `web.xml`, no action is needed
    2. If your application relied on the previous default (typically ISO-8859-1), you may need to explicitly set the encoding
    3. Check for `<request-character-encoding>` and `<response-character-encoding>` elements in your `web.xml`

    ### Additional Info

    - The default encoding for both requests and responses is now UTF-8
    - Applications that already use UTF-8 are not affected
    - Applications handling non-UTF-8 encoded data may need explicit encoding configuration
    - This change aligns with modern web standards
    - See [web.xml defaults](https://tomcat.apache.org/migration-10.html#web.xml_defaults)
  links:
    - url: https://tomcat.apache.org/migration-10.html#web.xml_defaults
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    builtin.filecontent:
        pattern: <(request|response)-character-encoding>
        filePattern: .*web\.xml

    In Tomcat 10.0.9 onwards, Tomcat no longer adds an "Expires" HTTP response header when adding "Cache-Control: private" due to a CONFIDENTIAL transport-guarantee.

    ### Migration Steps

    1. Review your application's caching behavior if it relies on the CONFIDENTIAL transport-guarantee
    2. If you need to disable caching, configure it explicitly in your application using response headers or filters
    3. Applications that set their own cache headers explicitly are not affected

    ### Additional Info

    - This change aligns Tomcat's behavior with the HTTP specification
    - Applications relying on Tomcat's previous implicit Expires header will see changed caching behavior
    - You may need to add explicit cache-control headers via a servlet filter or in your application code
    - See [BZ 65513](https://bz.apache.org/bugzilla/show_bug.cgi?id=65513) for more information

- ruleID: web-annotation-00010
  description: Multi-part uploads now require sufficient JVM direct memory in Tomcat 10.0.11
  category: potential
  effort: 3
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=tomcat9
    - konveyor.io/source=tomcat
    - konveyor.io/target=tomcat10
    - konveyor.io/target=tomcat
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    In Tomcat 10.0.11 onwards, Commons FileUpload now uses `java.nio.file.Files`, which means applications using multi-part uploads need to ensure that the JVM is configured with sufficient direct memory (`-XX:MaxDirectMemorySize`) to store all in-progress multi-part uploads.

    ### Before

    ```java
    import javax.servlet.annotation.MultipartConfig;

    @MultipartConfig(maxFileSize = 1024 * 1024 * 10)
    public class UploadServlet extends HttpServlet {
        // ...
    }
    ```

    ### After

    ```java
    import jakarta.servlet.annotation.MultipartConfig;

    @MultipartConfig(maxFileSize = 1024 * 1024 * 10)
    public class UploadServlet extends HttpServlet {
        // Ensure JVM has sufficient direct memory:
        // -XX:MaxDirectMemorySize=256m (or appropriate size)
    }
    ```

    ### Additional Info

    - The underlying implementation changed from stream-based to NIO file-based processing
    - JVM direct memory must be sized to handle concurrent multi-part upload traffic
    - Configure `-XX:MaxDirectMemorySize` appropriately in startup scripts
    - Monitor direct memory usage under load after upgrading
    - See [Tomcat 10.0.x noteable changes](https://tomcat.apache.org/migration-10.html#Tomcat_10.0.x_noteable_changes)
  links:
    - url: https://tomcat.apache.org/migration-10.html#Tomcat_10.0.x_noteable_changes
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: javax.servlet.annotation.MultipartConfig
        location: ANNOTATION

The patterns.json comprehensively captures virtually all migration artifacts from the guide. All annotation changes are covered: @Test (org.junit.Test → org.junit.jupiter.api.Test), @Before → @BeforeEach, @After → @AfterEach, @BeforeClass → @BeforeAll, @AfterClass → @AfterAll, @Ignore → @Disabled, @Category → @Tag, @RunWith → @ExtendWith, @Rule → @ExtendWith, @ClassRule → @ExtendWith. The @Test expected/timeout parameter removal is thoroughly documented in the @Test pattern's message. Class-level changes are captured: Assert → Assertions, Assume → Assumptions. The TestRule interface migration to extension callbacks is captured. Build configuration changes (surefire <groups> → <includeTags>/<excludeTags>) have a dedicated pattern. The junit:junit dependency migration and junit-vintage-engine transitional dependency are both captured. The only remaining coverage gaps identified by the system were standard library references (Integer, Arrays) and generic POM structural elements (build, plugins) which are not migration artifacts. Every before/after code example difference in the guide has a corresponding pattern with detailed messages including equivalent before/after examples.

output/junit4-to-junit5-20260624-085834/rules/annotations.yaml
- ruleID: annotations-annotation-00010
  description: '@Test annotation moved from org.junit to org.junit.jupiter.api in JUnit 5'
  category: mandatory
  effort: 5
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=junit4
    - konveyor.io/source=junit
    - konveyor.io/target=junit5
    - konveyor.io/target=junit
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    The `@Test` annotation has been relocated from `org.junit.Test` to `org.junit.jupiter.api.Test` in JUnit 5.

    Additionally, the `expected` and `timeout` parameters of `@Test` have been removed. Use `Assertions.assertThrows()` for expected exceptions and `Assertions.assertTimeout()` for timeouts instead.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.junit.Test;

    @Test(expected = Exception.class)
    public void shouldRaiseAnException() throws Exception {
        // ...
    }

    @Test(timeout = 1)
    public void shouldFailBecauseTimeout() throws InterruptedException {
        Thread.sleep(10);
    }
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import org.junit.jupiter.api.Test;
    import org.junit.jupiter.api.Assertions;
    import java.time.Duration;

    @Test
    void shouldRaiseAnException() {
        Assertions.assertThrows(Exception.class, () -> {
            // ...
        });
    }

    @Test
    void shouldFailBecauseTimeout() {
        Assertions.assertTimeout(Duration.ofMillis(1), () -> Thread.sleep(10));
    }
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - The `expected` parameter is replaced by `Assertions.assertThrows()`
    - The `timeout` parameter is replaced by `Assertions.assertTimeout()`
    - Test methods no longer need to be `public` in JUnit 5
    - The `@Test` annotation no longer accepts any parameters
    - See: https://www.baeldung.com/junit-5-migration#1-annotations
  links:
    - url: https://www.baeldung.com/junit-5-migration#1-annotations
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: org.junit.Test
        location: ANNOTATION
- ruleID: annotations-annotation-00020
  description: '@Before annotation replaced by @BeforeEach in JUnit 5'
  category: mandatory
  effort: 1
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=junit4
    - konveyor.io/source=junit
    - konveyor.io/target=junit5
    - konveyor.io/target=junit
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    The `@Before` annotation has been replaced by `@BeforeEach` in JUnit 5.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.junit.Before;

    @Before
    public void setUp() {
        // ...
    }
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import org.junit.jupiter.api.BeforeEach;

    @BeforeEach
    void setUp() {
        // ...
    }
    ```

    ### Additional Info

output/junit4-to-junit5-20260624-085834/rules/assertions.yaml
- ruleID: assertions-import-00010
  description: Assert class moved from org.junit to org.junit.jupiter.api.Assertions in JUnit 5
  category: mandatory
  effort: 5
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=junit4
    - konveyor.io/source=junit
    - konveyor.io/target=junit5
    - konveyor.io/target=junit
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    The `org.junit.Assert` class has been replaced by `org.junit.jupiter.api.Assertions` in JUnit 5.

    In JUnit 5, assertion messages can now be provided as a lambda for lazy evaluation, and assertions can be grouped using `Assertions.assertAll()`.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.junit.Assert;

    Assert.assertEquals(expected, actual);
    Assert.assertTrue(condition);
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import org.junit.jupiter.api.Assertions;

    Assertions.assertEquals(expected, actual);
    Assertions.assertTrue(condition);
    // New: lazy message evaluation
    Assertions.assertTrue(2 == 3, () -> "Numbers are not equal!");
    // New: grouped assertions
    Assertions.assertAll("group",
        () -> Assertions.assertEquals(1, 1),
        () -> Assertions.assertEquals(2, 2));
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - Method names are the same but the class and package changed
    - JUnit 5 supports lazy message evaluation via lambda suppliers
    - `Assertions.assertAll()` allows grouping multiple assertions
    - The message parameter order may differ: JUnit 5 puts the message last
    - See: https://www.baeldung.com/junit-5-migration#2-assertions
  links:
    - url: https://www.baeldung.com/junit-5-migration#2-assertions
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: org.junit.Assert
        location: IMPORT
- ruleID: assertions-import-00020
  description: Assume class moved from org.junit to org.junit.jupiter.api.Assumptions in JUnit 5
  category: mandatory
  effort: 3
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=junit4
    - konveyor.io/source=junit
    - konveyor.io/target=junit5
    - konveyor.io/target=junit
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    The `org.junit.Assume` class has been replaced by `org.junit.jupiter.api.Assumptions` in JUnit 5.

    JUnit 5 fully supports the existing assumption methods and adds new methods like `assumingThat()` for conditional assertions.

    ### Before
    ```java
    import org.junit.Assume;

    Assume.assumeTrue(condition);
    Assume.assumeFalse(condition);
    ```

    ### After
    ```java
    import org.junit.jupiter.api.Assumptions;

    Assumptions.assumeTrue(condition);
    Assumptions.assumeFalse(condition);
    // New: conditional assertion execution
    Assumptions.assumingThat("WEB".equals(System.getenv("ENV")),
        () -> Assertions.assertTrue(condition));
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - Method names are largely the same but the class and package changed
    - JUnit 5 adds `assumingThat()` for running assertions under specific conditions
    - Located in `org.junit.jupiter.api` package
    - See: https://www.baeldung.com/junit-5-migration#3-assumptions
  links:
    - url: https://www.baeldung.com/junit-5-migration#3-assumptions
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.referenced:
        pattern: org.junit.Assume
        location: IMPORT

output/junit4-to-junit5-20260624-085834/rules/build.yaml
- ruleID: build-xml-00010
  description: Surefire <groups> config for JUnit 4 @Category replaced by <includeTags>/<excludeTags> for JUnit 5 @Tag
  category: mandatory
  effort: 5
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=junit4
    - konveyor.io/source=junit
    - konveyor.io/target=junit5
    - konveyor.io/target=junit
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    The Maven Surefire plugin `<groups>` configuration element was used in JUnit 4 to filter tests by `@Category` marker interfaces. In JUnit 5, `@Category` is replaced by `@Tag` with string labels, and the surefire configuration must use `<includeTags>` and `<excludeTags>` instead of `<groups>` and `<excludedGroups>`.

    ### Before
    ```xml
    <plugin>
        <artifactId>maven-surefire-plugin</artifactId>
        <configuration>
            <groups>com.example.SlowTests,com.example.IntegrationTests</groups>
            <excludedGroups>com.example.BrokenTests</excludedGroups>
        </configuration>
    </plugin>
    ```

    ### After
    ```xml
    <plugin>
        <artifactId>maven-surefire-plugin</artifactId>
        <configuration>
            <properties>
                <includeTags>slow,integration</includeTags>
                <excludeTags>broken</excludeTags>
            </properties>
        </configuration>
    </plugin>
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - JUnit 4 `@Category` used marker interfaces (e.g., `SlowTests.class`); JUnit 5 `@Tag` uses string labels (e.g., `"slow"`)
    - `<groups>` and `<excludedGroups>` elements should be replaced with `<includeTags>` and `<excludeTags>` inside `<properties>`
    - The category marker interfaces are no longer needed and can be removed
    - This change must be coordinated with replacing `@Category` annotations with `@Tag` annotations in test classes
    - See: https://www.baeldung.com/junit-5-migration#4-tagging-and-filtering
  links:
    - url: https://www.baeldung.com/junit-5-migration#4-tagging-and-filtering
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    builtin.xml:
        xpath: //*[local-name()='plugin'][*[local-name()='artifactId' and text()='maven-surefire-plugin']]//*[local-name()='groups']
        namespaces:
            m: http://maven.apache.org/POM/4.0.0
        filepaths:
            - pom.xml

output/junit4-to-junit5-20260624-085834/rules/dependencies.yaml
- ruleID: dependencies-dependency-00010
  description: JUnit 4 junit:junit dependency should be replaced with JUnit 5 junit-jupiter
  category: mandatory
  effort: 5
  labels:
    - konveyor.io/source=junit4
    - konveyor.io/source=junit
    - konveyor.io/target=junit5
    - konveyor.io/target=junit
    - konveyor.io/generated-by=ai-rule-gen
  message: |-
    The `junit:junit` dependency provides JUnit 4. To migrate to JUnit 5, replace it with the JUnit Jupiter dependency (`org.junit.jupiter:junit-jupiter`).

    For an incremental migration, you can temporarily add `junit-vintage-engine` alongside the JUnit 5 dependencies to run existing JUnit 4 tests within the JUnit 5 platform while you migrate tests one by one.

    ### Before
    ```xml
    <dependency>
        <groupId>junit</groupId>
        <artifactId>junit</artifactId>
        <version>4.13.2</version>
        <scope>test</scope>
    </dependency>
    ```

    ### After
    ```xml
    <!-- JUnit 5 Jupiter -->
    <dependency>
        <groupId>org.junit.jupiter</groupId>
        <artifactId>junit-jupiter</artifactId>
        <version>${junit5.version}</version>
        <scope>test</scope>
    </dependency>

    <!-- Optional: Vintage engine for running JUnit 4 tests during migration -->
    <dependency>
        <groupId>org.junit.vintage</groupId>
        <artifactId>junit-vintage-engine</artifactId>
        <version>${junit5.vintage.version}</version>
        <scope>test</scope>
    </dependency>
    ```

    ### Additional Info
    - Replace `junit:junit` with `org.junit.jupiter:junit-jupiter` for full JUnit 5 support
    - During incremental migration, add `junit-vintage-engine` to run JUnit 3/4 tests alongside JUnit 5 tests
    - Once all tests are migrated, remove both `junit:junit` and `junit-vintage-engine`
    - The JUnit 5 platform supports running tests from multiple engines simultaneously
    - See: https://www.baeldung.com/junit-5-migration#7-junit-5-vintage
  links:
    - url: https://www.baeldung.com/junit-5-migration#7-junit-5-vintage
      title: Migration Documentation
  when:
    java.dependency:
        name: junit.junit
        lowerbound: 0.0.0

already return.**\n81\tEvery `go run ./cmd/*` command returns structured JSON. Use that JSON output directly \u2014 do not pipe it through shell commands to extract fields.\n82\tThis is a Go project. Run only commands listed in this permissions table.\n83\tIf a required action is not permitted, stop and report the limitation.\n84\t\n85\t## UX Principles\n86\t\n87\t- Emit short status lines continuously (start + finish for each step).\n88\t- Only ask at checkpoint when `mode=interactive` and `checkpoint_behavior=ask`.\n89\t- Do not block after testing starts; continue even if some rules remain failing.\n90\t- Fix only failing rules, not the full suite.\n91\t\n92\tFor pipeline logging conventions, see `references/orchestrator-details.md` (Pipeline Transcript section).\n93\t\n94\tFor stage timing instructions, see `references/orchestrator-details.md` (Timing section).\n95\t\n96\tFor sub-agent invocation protocol and contract validation, see `references/orchestrator-details.md` (Sub-agent Protocol section).\n97\t\n98\t## Pipeline\n99\t\n100\t**Error handling:** If any CLI command (`ingest`, `construct`, `validate`, `scaffold`, `sanitize`, `test`, `report`) exits non-zero, print `[step] FAILED \u2014 <error>` and stop the pipeline. Do not proceed to the next step.\n101\t\n102\t**Partial failures:** If a step produces partial results before failing (e.g., `construct` succeeds for 48 patterns but fails on 2), preserve the partial output and report what succeeded. The user can fix the failing patterns and re-run. Do not discard valid results because of a partial failure.\n103\t\n104\t**Resume behavior:** When `resume_from` is set, the user must also provide `migration_dir` pointing to the specific timestamped directory to resume. Skip prior stages and validate prerequisites first. Fail fast when required artifacts are missing.\n105\t\n106\tStage prerequisites (paths relative to `<migration_dir>`):\n107\t- `extract` requires `guide.md`\n108\t- `coverage` requires `patterns.json`\n109\t- `scaffold` requires `rules/`\n110\t- `test` requires `rules/` and `tests/manifest.json`\n111\t- `report` requires source/target metadata plus pass/fail totals and rule ID lists\n112\t\n113\t### 1. Ingest\n114\t\n115\tGenerate a timestamp once at pipeline start (`YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS` in local time).\n116\t\n117\tDetermine the migration directory path:\n118\t- If the user provided `migration_dir`, use that (no timestamp)\n119\t- If the user provided `sources` and `targets` (or `source` and `target`), use `output/<primary_source>-to-<primary_target>-<YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS>` where `primary_source` is `sources[0]` and `primary_target` is `targets[0]`\n120\t- If auto-detecting: ingest to `output/guide-temp.md` first, read the first ~50 lines to detect source/target/language (lowercase, hyphenated names like `spring-boot-3`), then use `output/<source>-to-<target>-<YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS>`\n121\t\n122\t```bash\n123\tmkdir -p output/<source>-to-<target>-<YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS>\n124\t```\n125\t\n126\tEvery `go run` command should be a standalone invocation with fully-expanded arguments \u2014 substitute actual paths and flag values directly into each command. Do not use shell variable assignments (`VAR=...`) or compound `&&` chains, since these don't match the permissions table.\n127\t\n128\tThe log flags are: `--log <migration_dir>/pipeline.log --agent orchestrator --model <your_model_id>`. Append these literally to every CLI invocation.\n129\t\n130\t```\n131\t[ingest] Fetching guide from <source>...\n132\t```\n133\t\n134\t- **URL:** `go run ./cmd/ingest --log <migration_dir>/pipeline.log --agent orchestrator --model <your_model_id> --input <url> --output <migration_dir>/guide.md`\n135\t- **File (not markdown):** `go run ./cmd/ingest --log <migration_dir>/pipeline.log --agent orchestrator --model <your_model_id> --input <path> --output <migration_dir>/guide.md`\n136\t- **Pasted text or already markdown:** Write directly to `<migration_dir>/guide.md`\n137\t\n138\tIf auto-detecting, write `output/guide-temp.md` to `<migration_dir>/guide.md` using the Write tool after the migration directory path is determined.\n139\t\n140\t**Stub detection \u2014 follow sub-pages.** After ingesting each URL, check the output for stub characteristics. A page is a stub if it has fewer than 100 non-blank lines of content after `cmd/ingest` processing (`cmd/ingest` already strips `<nav>`, `<footer>`, and `<aside>` elements during HTML-to-markdown conversion, so no additional filtering is needed).\n141\t\n142\tIf a stub is detected:\n143\t\n144\t1. Read the ingested markdown and extract all links whose resolved URL shares the same base path as the original URL (same-origin sibling pages). Sibling links are those pointing to `*.html` files under the same directory path as the original URL. Exclude external links, anchor-only links (`#...`), and links to parent directories.\n145\t2. For each sibling link, resolve it to a full URL relative to the original URL's base path.\n146\t3. Ingest each sub-page with `cmd/ingest` into a separate file (`guide-part-<N>.md`).\n147\t4. Concatenate all parts (original + sub-pages) into the final `guide.md`, in the order the links appear in the stub page (document order).\n148\t5. If a sub-page fetch fails (404, timeout), log a warning (`[ingest] WARNING \u2014 failed to fetch <url>: <error>`) and skip that page. Do not abort the pipeline \u2014 partial content is better than none.\n149\t\n150\tThis ensures that documentation sites which split content across multiple pages are fully captured. Without this step, the pipeline will only see the stub and miss the bulk of the migration content.\n151\t\n152\tCount lines (`GUIDE_LINES`) and section headings. Print:\n153\t\n154\t```\n155\t[ingest] Done \u2014 <GUIDE_LINES> lines, <N> sections \u2192 <migration_dir>/ (<elapsed>)\n156\t```\n157\t\n158\t### 2. Extract (parallel)\n159\t\n160\tExtraction uses parallel agents to process the guide faster. The orchestrator splits the guide into chunks and spawns multiple rule-writer agents.\n161\t\n162\t**2a. Index sections and auto-detect metadata:**\n163\t\n164\t```bash\n165\tgo run ./cmd/sections <log_flags> --guide <migration_dir>/guide.md\n166\t```\n167\t\n168\tThis returns JSON with all sections classified as `content` or `header-only`. Filter to content sections only.\n169\t\n170\t```\n171\t[extract] Extracting patterns from <content_count> sections (<N> parallel agents)...\n172\t```\n173\t\n174\t**2b. Split into chunks and dispatch:**\n175\t\n176\tSplit the content sections into **N balanced chunks** (minimum 1, maximum 5 agents). Balance by section count. Assign each chunk a number (1, 2, ..., N).\n177\t\n178\t**Keep related sections together.** Group sections by their top-level heading (`##`) \u2014 all subsections (`###`, `####`) under the same `##` must stay in the same chunk. Migration guides pair before/after code examples across subsections within a topic; splitting them across agents means no agent sees both sides of the diff. Balance chunks by top-level-heading groups, not by individual sections.\n179\t\n180\t**Invoke:** `rule-writer` (one per chunk, in parallel)\n181\t**Purpose:** Extract migration patterns from assigned sections.\n182\t**Inputs per invocation:**\n183\t  - guide: <migration_dir>/guide.md\n184\t  - sources: {sources array (e.g., [\"spring-boot3\", \"spring-boot\"])}\n185\t  - targets: {targets array (e.g., [\"spring-boot4\", \"spring-boot\"])}\n186\t  - rules_dir: <migration_dir>/rules\n187\t  - sections: {chunk subset \u2014 list of `{heading, start_line, end_line}` objects}\n188\t  - all_headings: {full list of ALL content section headings from step 2a \u2014 not just this chunk's sections. Enables each agent to detect multi-path migrations even when variant sections are in other chunks.}\n189\t  - output_file: <migration_dir>/patterns-{chunk_number}.json\n190\t**Parallel:** yes\n191\t**Expect:**\n192\t  - patterns_count, output_file\n193\t\n194\t**2c. Merge, verify, and construct:**\n195\t\n196\tAfter all agents complete, merge the partial patterns files, verify source artifacts, and build rules:\n197\t\n198\t```bash\n199\tgo run ./cmd/merge-patterns <log_flags> --output <migration_dir>/patterns.json <migration_dir>/patterns-1.json <migration_dir>/patterns-2.json ...\n200\tgo run ./cmd/verify <log_flags> --patterns <migration_dir>/patterns.json --output <migration_dir>/verify-results.json --cache <migration_dir>/verify-cache\n201\tgo run ./cmd/construct <log_flags> --patterns <migration_dir>/patterns.json --output <migration_dir>/rules\n202\tgo run ./cmd/validate <log_flags> --rules <migration_dir>/rules\n203\t```\n204\t\n205\t**Verification step:** `cmd/verify` downloads source JARs from Maven Central and checks that each pattern's `source_fqn` exists in the declared `source_artifact`. This catches hallucinated class names before rules reach testing.\n206\t\n207\tThe verify stdout JSON contains `verified`, `not_found`, `skipped`, and `offline` counts. Print:\n208\t\n209\t```\n210\t[verify] <verified> verified, <not_found> not found, <skipped> skipped\n211\t```\n212\t\n213\tIf `not_found > 0`, read `<migration_dir>/verify-results.json` and note which `pattern_index` values have `status: \"not_found\"`. After construct runs, use the `pattern_rule_map` from construct's stdout JSON to map each `pattern_index` \u2192 `rule_id`. Carry `verified_rule_ids` and `not_found_rule_ids` forward to step 5 (report).\n214\t\n215\tIf validation fails, fix `<migration_dir>/patterns.json` (remove invalid entries) and re-run construct.\n216\t\n217\t```\n218\t[extract] Done \u2014 <patterns_count> patterns \u2192 <rules_count> rules in <migration_dir>/rules/ (<elapsed>)\n219\t```\n220\t\n221\tSave `source`, `target`, `patterns_count`, `rules_count`, and verify counts for the final summary.\n222\t\n223\t### 2d. Coverage Check\n224\t\n225\tRun the coverage tool to find sections with named artifacts that weren't extracted:\n226\t\n227\t```bash\n228\tgo run ./cmd/coverage <log_flags> --guide <migration_dir>/guide.md --patterns <migration_dir>/patterns.json --language <language>\n229\t```\n230\t\n231\tIf `gap_count > 0` in the JSON output, print:\n232\t\n233\t```\n234\t[coverage] <gap_count> sections with uncovered artifacts: <heading_1>, <heading_2>, ...\n235\t```\n236\t\n237\tConvert gaps to sections and send back to the rule-writer in chunk mode for targeted re-extraction. Each gap has `heading` and `line` \u2014 use the sections index to get the `start_line` and `end_line` for that heading. Mention the uncovered artifacts in the prompt so the sub-agent focuses on them.\n238\t\n239\t**Invoke:** `rule-writer` (chunk mode)\n240\t**Purpose:** Extract patterns from specific sections that the coverage check flagged.\n241\t**Inputs:**\n242\t  - guide: <migration_dir>/guide.md\n243\t  - sources: {sources array}\n244\t  - targets: {targets array}\n245\t  - rules_dir: <migration_dir>/rules\n246\t  - sections: {gap sections converted to `[{heading, start_line, end_line}]` format}\n247\t  - output_file: <migration_dir>/patterns-gaps.json\n248\t**Parallel:** no\n249\t**Expect:**\n250\t  - patterns_count, output_file\n251\t\n252\tThe sub-agent writes only the new patterns to `<migration_dir>/patterns-gaps.json`. It does NOT read or inspect existing patterns \u2014 the orchestrator handles deduplication. After the sub-agent returns, merge, verify, and rebuild:\n253\t\n254\t```bash\n255\tgo run ./cmd/merge-patterns <log_flags> --output <migration_dir>/patterns.json <migration_dir>/patterns.json <migration_dir>/patterns-gaps.json\n256\tgo run ./cmd/verify <log_flags> --patterns <migration_dir>/patterns.json --output <migration_dir>/verify-results.json --cache <migration_dir>/verify-cache\n257\tgo run ./cmd/construct <log_flags> --patterns <migration_dir>/patterns.json --output <migration_dir>/rules\n258\tgo run ./cmd/validate <log_flags> --rules <migration_dir>/rules\n259\t```\n260\t\n261\tRe-run the coverage check. If gaps remain, accept them \u2014 one re-extraction pass is enough.\n262\t\n263\t```\n264\t[coverage] Done \u2014 <final_gap_count> remaining gaps (accepted) (<elapsed>)\n265\t```\n266\t\n267\tIf `gap_count == 0`:\n268\t\n269\t```\n270\t[coverage] No gaps found (<elapsed>)\n271\t```\n272\t\n273\t### Checkpoint\n274\t\n275\tAfter extraction/coverage:\n276\t\n277\t- If `mode=non_interactive`, do **not** prompt:\n278\t  - `checkpoint_behavior=continue` or `ask`: continue automatically\n279\t  - `checkpoint_behavior=stop_after_extract`: skip testing and go to Step 5 (Report)\n280\t- If `mode=interactive`:\n281\t  - `checkpoint_behavior=continue`: continue automatically\n282\t  - `checkpoint_behavior=stop_after_extract`: skip testing and go to Step 5 (Report)\n283\t  - `checkpoint_behavior=ask`: ask:\n284\t    - `Continue with test generation and validation? (y/n)`\n285\t    - if no, skip to Step 5 (Report) with untested rules\n286\t\n287\t**Rules-only report:** When skipping to Step 5, invoke `cmd/report` with `--passed 0 --failed 0 --kantra-limitation 0` and empty `--passed-rules`, `--failed-rules`, `--kantra-limitation-rules` flags. Pass `--rules-total`, `--verified-rules`, and `--not-found-rules` from extraction. All rules get `test_status: untested`.\n288\t\n289\t### 3. Test Generation\n290\t\n291\t**3a. Scaffold (orchestrator runs this directly, not an agent):**\n292\t\n293\t```bash\n294\tgo run ./cmd/scaffold <log_flags> --rules <migration_dir>/rules --output <migration_dir>/tests --patterns <migration_dir>/patterns.json\n295\t```\n296\t\n297\tThis creates all directories, `.test.yaml` files, and `manifest.json`. No LLM needed.\n298\t\n299\t**3b. Read manifest and split into batches:**\n300\t\n301\tRead `<migration_dir>/tests/manifest.json`. It contains a `groups` array \u2014 each group has `name`, `data_dir`, `files` (paths to generate), and `rule_ids`.\n302\t\n303\tSplit the groups into **batches of ~5 groups each** (minimum 1 batch, maximum 5 batches), balanced by rule count.\n304\t\n305\t**3c. Spawn test-generator agents:**\n306\t\n307\t```\n308\t[test-gen] Generating test data for <rules_count> rules (<B> parallel agents)...\n309\t```\n310\t\n311\t**Invoke:** `test-generator` (one per batch, up to 5 in parallel)\n312\t**Purpose:** Generate compilable test source code that triggers the assigned rules.\n313\t**Inputs per invocation:**\n314\t  - rules_dir: <migration_dir>/rules\n315\t  - tests_dir: <migration_dir>/tests\n316\t  - groups: {batch subset from manifest.json \u2014 include name, data_dir, rule_ids, files}\n317\t**Parallel:** yes\n318\t**Expect:**\n319\t  - groups_completed, files_written\n320\t\n321\t**3d. Collect results and sanitize.** After all agents complete:\n322\t\n323\tCollect `suspected_kantra_limitations` from all rule-writer and test-generator agent returns (merge, deduplicate by `rule_id`). If non-empty, print:\n324\t\n325\t```\n326\t[test-gen] <N> suspected kantra limitations (Maven Central: no plain-semver version): <rule_id_1>, ...\n327\t```\n328\t\n329\tCarry this merged list forward as `pre_classified_kantra_limitations` \u2014 it will be passed to the rule-validator to skip the fix loop for these rules.\n330\t\n331\tSanitize XML:\n332\t\n333\t```bash\n334\tgo run ./cmd/sanitize <log_flags> --dir <migration_dir>/tests/data\n335\t```\n336\t\n337\t```\n338\t[test-gen] Done \u2014 <total_groups> groups, <total_files> files (<elapsed>)\n339\t```\n340\t\n341\t### 4. Validate (orchestrator-driven loop)\n342\t\n343\tThe orchestrator runs tests and uses a sub-agent for LLM-driven repairs on failures.\n344\t\n345\t**4a. Run tests:**\n346\t\n347\t```bash\n348\tgo run ./cmd/test <log_flags> --rules <migration_dir>/rules --tests <migration_dir>/tests --timeout 5m\n349\t```\n350\t\n351\tThe CLI runs each test file sequentially and automatically retries timed-out files once (`--retry-timeouts`, on by default). Tests run locally via `--run-local=true`. To run a subset, use `--files` with bare filenames (e.g., `--files data-1.test.yaml,data-2.test.yaml`), resolved relative to `--tests` dir.\n352\t\n353\tPrint the result:\n354\t\n355\t```\n356\t[validate] <total_passed>/<total_rules> passed (<elapsed>)\n357\t```\n358\t\n359\tOr if failures:\n360\t\n361\t```\n362\t[validate] <total_passed>/<total_rules> passed \u2014 <F> failures: <rule_id_1>, <rule_id_2>, ...\n363\t```\n364\t\n365\tIf all passed (elapsed shown above), skip to step 5.\n366\t\n367\t**4b. Fix (only if failures):**\n368\t\n369\t```\n370\t[fix] Fixing <F> failures: <rule_id_1>, <rule_id_2> ...\n371\t```\n372\t\n373\t**Invoke:** `rule-validator`\n374\t**Purpose:** Fix test data for failing rules so they pass kantra validation.\n375\t**Inputs:**\n376\t  - rules_dir: <migration_dir>/rules\n377\t  - tests_dir: <migration_dir>/tests\n378\t  - failing_rules: {list with rule_id, test_file, error for each failure}\n379\t  - pre_classified_kantra_limitations: {merged list from rule-writer and test-generator suspected_kantra_limitations \u2014 may be empty}\n380\t  - max_iterations: 1\n381\t**Parallel:** no\n382\t**Expect:**\n383\t  - fixed_rules, still_failing, kantra_limitation_rules, iterations_used, fix_details\n384\t  - results_by_rule (with `result_type` + `recommended_action`)\n385\t\n386\tThe validator agent owns the fix-verify loop \u2014 it fixes files, re-runs tests via `cmd/test`, and iterates up to `max_iterations`. Default is 1 iteration; pass up to 3 if the user requests more attempts.\n387\t\n388\t**The orchestrator must NOT run its own fix attempts.** Do not manually edit test files, create stub classes, toggle analysisParams, or retry. All fix work goes through the rule-validator sub-agent. When the validator returns `still_failing`, accept that result and move on.\n389\t\n390\tPrint the result:\n391\t\n392\t```\n393\t[fix] <fixed_count> fixed, <still_failing_count> still failing, <kantra_limitation_count> kantra limitations (<validate elapsed>)\n394\t```\n395\t\n396\tThe `<validate elapsed>` is the total time since the validate stage started (step 4a), including test runs and all fix iterations.\n397\t\n398\tIf `kantra_limitation_rules` is non-empty, print:\n399\t\n400\t```\n401\t[fix] kantra limitations (engine cannot test \u2014 rule is correct): <rule_id_1>, ...\n402\t```\n403\t\n404\tGroup unresolved failures by `result_type` in `results_by_rule` and include grouped counts in the final summary (e.g., `still_failing_timeout: 2`, `still_failing_kantra_limitation: 1`).\n405\t\n406\tIf still_failing is non-empty, move on \u2014 don't block the pipeline.\n407\t\n408\t### 5. Report\n409\t\n410\tCollate pass/fail results from the test run and the fix loop. Generate `report.yaml` with per-rule test and verification status. No labels are written to rule YAML files \u2014 all pipeline metadata lives in the report.\n411\t\n412\t```bash\n413\tgo run ./cmd/report <log_flags> --source <comma-separated sources> --target <comma-separated targets> --output <migration_dir>/report.yaml --rules-total <N> --passed <P> --failed <F> --kantra-limitation <K> --passed-rules <comma-separated passed rule IDs> --failed-rules <comma-separated failed rule IDs> --kantra-limitation-rules <comma-separated kantra limitation rule IDs> --verified-rules <comma-separated verified rule IDs> --not-found-rules <comma-separated not-found rule IDs>\n414\t```\n415\t\n416\tThe `--verified-rules` and `--not-found-rules` flags come from the verification mapping built in step 2c (pattern_index \u2192 rule_id via construct's pattern_rule_map).\n417\t\n418\tThe report includes a `rules` section with per-rule `test_status` (passed/failed/kantra-limitation/untested) and `source_verified` (true/false). The pass rate is computed as `passed / (passed + failed)` \u2014 kantra limitations are excluded since they are not failures, but also not confirmed passes.\n419\t\n420\t### 6. Summary\n421\t\n422\tPrint a formatted summary table using GitHub-flavored markdown:\n423\t\n424\t```markdown\n425\t## Summary\n426\t\n427\t| | |\n428\t|---|---|\n429\t| **Input** | <guide title or URL as a markdown link> |\n430\t| **Migration** | <primary_source> \u2192 <primary_target> (<language>) |\n431\t| **Guide** | <GUIDE_LINES> lines, <N> sections \u2192 <M> produced patterns, <K> skipped |\n432\t| **Rules** | <rules_count> generated, **<P>/<N> passed (<percent>%)** |\n433\t| **Verification** | <verified>/<total> source-verified, <not_found> not found, <skipped> skipped (omit row if all skipped) |\n434\t| **Kantra limitations** | <K> rules correct but not auto-testable \u2014 engine cannot compare non-semver versions (omit row if K=0) |\n435\t| **Fix iterations** | <iterations used, 0 if none> |\n436\t| **Timing** | total: <total elapsed> \u2014 ingest: <elapsed>, extract: <elapsed>, coverage: <elapsed>, test-gen: <elapsed>, validate: <elapsed>, report: <elapsed> |\n437\t| **Output** | `<migration_dir>/patterns.json` (patterns), `<migration_dir>/rules/` (rules), `<migration_dir>/tests/` (tests), `<migration_dir>/report.yaml` (report) |\n438\t\n439\t### Rule Categories\n440\t\n441\tUse the `groups` array from the `construct` JSON output \u2014 it lists each file and its rule count. Do not iterate rule files manually.\n442\t\n443\t| Group | Rules | Status |\n444\t|---|---|---|\n445\t| <group_name> (<brief description of what rules cover>) | <rule_count> | <passed>/<total> passed |\n446\t| ... | ... | ... |\n447\t```\n448\t\n449\tIf there are failures, add a row to the top-level table:\n450\t\n451\t```\n452\t| **Failed** | <rule_id_1>, <rule_id_2>, ... |\n453\t```\n454\t\n455\tIf coverage was low (< 30% of sections produced patterns), add a row:\n456\t\n457\t```\n458\t| **Warning** | Low extraction coverage (<M>/<K> sections) |\n459\t```\n460\t\n461\t**Rules-only summary (when `checkpoint_behavior=stop_after_extract`):**\n462\t\n463\tWhen testing was skipped, use this simplified table instead:\n464\t\n465\t```markdown\n466\t## Summary\n467\t\n468\t| | |\n469\t|---|---|\n470\t| **Input** | <guide title or URL as a markdown link> |\n471\t| **Migration** | <primary_source> \u2192 <primary_target> (<language>) |\n472\t| **Guide** | <GUIDE_LINES> lines, <N> sections \u2192 <M> produced patterns, <K> skipped |\n473\t| **Rules** | <rules_count> generated (untested) |\n474\t| **Verification** | <verified>/<total> source-verified, <not_found> not found, <skipped> skipped (omit row if all skipped) |\n475\t| **Timing** | total: <total elapsed> \u2014 ingest: <elapsed>, extract: <elapsed>, coverage: <elapsed>, report: <elapsed> |\n476\t| **Output** | `<migration_dir>/patterns.json` (patterns), `<migration_dir>/rules/` (rules), `<migration_dir>/report.yaml` (report) |\n477\t| **Next step** | Run `/generate-rules-with-test resume_from=scaffold migration_dir=<migration_dir>` to add tests |\n478\t```\n479\t\n480\tOmit these rows: **Kantra limitations**, **Fix iterations**, **Failed** (no testing ran).\n481\tOmit `tests/` from the **Output** row and test-gen/validate timing from the **Timing** row.\n482\tInclude the **Rule Categories** table as normal.\n483\t",

Course – LJU – NPI (tag = JUnit)

![announcement - icon](/wp-content/uploads/2022/04/announcement-icon.png)

Master the most popular **testing framework for Java**, through the *Learn JUnit* course:

[**&gt;&gt; LEARN JUNIT**](/Course-LJU-NPI-1-2v0k)

## 1. Overview

In this tutorial, we’ll learn how to migrate from JUnit 4 to the latest JUnit 5 release, with an overview of the differences between the two versions of the library.

For the general guidelines on using JUnit 5, see our article [here](/junit-5).

## 2. JUnit 5 Advantages

Let’s start with the previous version, JUnit 4 , which has some clear limitations:

- A single jar library contains the entire framework. We need to import the whole library, even when we only require a particular feature. **In JUnit 5, we get more granularity and can import only what’s necessary.**
- Only one test runner can execute tests at a time in JUnit 4 (e.g. *SpringJUnit4ClassRunner* or *Parameterized* ). **JUnit 5 allows multiple runners to work simultaneously.**
- JUnit 4 never advanced beyond Java 7, missing out on a lot of features from Java 8. **JUnit 5 makes good use of the Java 8 features.**

The idea behind JUnit 5 was to completely rewrite JUnit 4 in order to negate most of these drawbacks.

## 3. Differences

JUnit 4 was divided into the modules that comprise JUnit 5:

- **JUnit Platform –** this module scopes all the extension frameworks we might have an interest in: test execution, discovery, and reporting.
- **JUnit Vintage –** this module allows backward compatibility with JUnit 4 or even JUnit 3.

### 3.1. Annotations

JUnit 5 comes with important changes to its annotations. Instead of *@org.junit.Test* we now need to use *@org.junit.jupiter.api.Test*.

**The most important one is that we can no longer use the *@Test* annotation for specifying expectations.**

The *expected* parameter in JUnit 4:
